Hajj Rituals from Tarwiyah to Arafat
Describes the sequence of Hajj from Mina to Arafat with sermon rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sequence of actions on the 8th and 9th of Dhul Hijjah and explain the ruling (sunnah muakkadah) of the imam's two sermons at Arafat.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice establishes the exact sequence from Mina to Arafat, and the imam's two sermons at Arafat are a confirmed sunnah like Friday.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah details the recommended actions for the 8th and 9th of Dhul Hijjah. It covers the departure to Mina, the standing at Arafat (excluding Batn 'Uranah), and the imam's two sermons after noon. Understanding this sequence is essential for performing Hajj according to the Hanafi school, as it preserves the Prophetic model.

Guided Path
1
Identify the temporal sequence
Notice the days: Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th) and Yawm 'Arafah (9th). The Prophet left for Mina on the morning of the 8th and stayed until Fajr of the 9th, then moved to Arafat.
The term 'ghadāh' means after sunrise, not dawn.
2
Locate the boundaries of the standing place
All of Arafat is valid for wuquf except the valley of Batn 'Uranah. This exception is based on the hadith 'Avoid Batn 'Uranah'.
Batn 'Uranah is a specific valley within the plain of Arafat.
3
Note the timing and content of the sermon
After the sun passes its zenith (zawāl), the imam delivers two sermons (khutbatayn) similar to Friday sermons, teaching the Hajj rites.
The two sermons are separated by a brief sitting, like Jumu'ah.
4
Recognize the legal status
These actions are sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) based on the Prophet's fi'l (action). The Hanafi school holds that the Prophet's practice indicates istihbāb, not wujūb.
This is distinct from wajib or fard.
5
Relate the ruling to the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Jabir (Sahih Muslim) describing the Prophet's actions on Hajj. The detailed description of the sequence and the two sermons establishes the sunnah.
The dalil is ahad (single-transmitter) with zanni thubut and dalāla.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَفْصِلُ بين كل خطبتين بيوم. ثُمَّ خرجَ غداة يوم التروية، إلى مني، ومكث فيها إلى فجر يوم عرفة. ثم منها إلى عرفات، وكلها موقفٌ إلا بطنَ عُرَنة، وإذا زالَتْ الشَّمسُ منه خَطَبَ الإمامُ خُطبتين كالجمعة، وعَلَّمَ فيها المناسك.
He separates between every two sermons by a day. Then he set out in the morning of the Day of Tarwiyah to Mina, and stayed there until the dawn of the Day of Arafah. Then from there to Arafat, and all of it is a standing place except the valley of 'Uranah. And when the sun declines from its zenith, the Imam delivers two sermons like those of Friday, and teaches in them the rites.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sunnah regarding the sequence of actions on the 8th and 9th of Dhul Hijjah. The commentator explains that the first sermon is on the 7th, the second on the 9th (the Day of Arafah), and the third on the 11th, separating each by a day. The Prophet ﷺ set out on the morning of the 8th (Tarwiyah) to Mina and stayed there until Fajr of the 9th, then moved to Arafat. The entire area of Arafat is valid for standing (wuquf) except Batn 'Uranah, based on the hadith: 'Arafah is all a standing place, and avoid Batn 'Uranah.' After the sun passes its zenith, the imam gives two sermons similar to Jumu'ah, teaching the rituals of Hajj, such as standing at Arafat, Muzdalifah, stoning, sacrifice, shaving, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah. This is supported by the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as recorded in Sahih Muslim and other collections.

Key Terms
يوم التروية (Yawm al-Tarwiyah): The eighth day of Dhul Hijjah, named because people used to water their camels for the journey to Arafat.
غداة (Ghadāh): Morning, specifically after sunrise, as the Prophet ﷺ set out after Fajr.
بطن عرنة (Baṭn 'Uranah): A valley within Arafat where standing is forbidden; based on the command to 'avoid' it.
خطبتين (Khuṭbatayn): Two sermons delivered by the imam on the Day of Arafah after noon, similar to Friday sermons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On which day does the imam deliver the two sermons at Arafat?
A) The Day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah)
B) The Day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) after noon
C) The Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah)
D) The Day of 'Eid

Key Takeaway
The sequence from Tarwiyah to Arafat, the standing place, and the two sermons are all confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) based on the Prophet's practice.

All of Arafat is a Place of Standing Except Batn Uranah
Defining the valid boundaries for wuquf at Arafat and the imam's sermon procedure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the valid places for wuquf at Arafat and explain the proof from the hadith that excludes Batn Uranah.

Core Idea
All of Arafat is valid for wuquf except the valley of Uranah — established by the Prophet's command to avoid it.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya defines the precise boundaries for the rukn of wuquf at Arafat. While the entire plain is a place of standing, the Hanafi school excludes a specific valley called Batn Uranah based on a prophetic hadith. The passage also describes the imam's two sermons on this day, but the core legal ruling is the exception of Uranah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that all of Arafat is a valid place of standing (mawqif) except Batn Uranah. This is a condition for the validity of the rukn of wuquf.
Wuquf at Arafat is a rukn of Hajj; missing it invalidates the Hajj.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'All of Arafat is a place of standing, and avoid the valley of Uranah.' This is an ahad hadith, but clear in meaning.
The hadith is reported by Ibn Majah and others.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'ارتفعوا' (avoid) indicates prohibition of standing in Batn Uranah, while the statement 'كلها موقف' indicates permissibility elsewhere.
The hadith uses a general statement followed by a specific exception.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i and others consider all of Arafat including Batn Uranah as valid for wuquf, based on a different interpretation or other proofs.
The Hanafi school prioritises the explicit prohibition in the hadith.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative position) is the Hanafi view excluding Uranah, as it is based on a clear sunnah and is part of zahir al-riwayah.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الإحرام
ثم منها إلى عرفات، وكلها موقفٌ إلا بطنَ عُرَنة ، وإذا زالَتْ الشَّمسُ منه خَطَبَ الإمامُ خُطبتين كالجمعة، وعَلَّمَ فيها المناسك
قوله : وكلّها ؛ أي جميعُ وادي عرفات موقف، فيقف في أي موضع شاء، ويجتنب بطنَ عُرَنَة - بضم العين المهملة، وفتح الراء المهملة، وفتح النون - : وادٍ في عرفات ؛ لحديث: «عرفة كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن عرنة، والمزدلفة كلّها موقف، وارتفعوا عن وادي محسّ» أخرجه ابن ماجه وغيره.
قوله : خطب ... الخ ؛ قال في «اللباب» : «إذا وصل إلى عرفة مكث بها داعياً مصلياً ذاكراً ملبياً، فإذا زالت الشمس اغتسل أو توضأ والغسل أفضل، ثم سار إلى المسجد : أي مسجد نمرة بلا تأخير فإذا بلغه صعد الإمام الأعظم أو نائبه المنبر، ويجلس عليه، ويؤذن المؤذنون بين يديه. فإذا فرغ قام الإمام فخطب خطبتين، فيحمد الله ويثني عليه، ويلبي ويهلّل، ويكبر ويصلي على النبي الله ويعظ الناس، ويأمرهم وينهاهم، ويعلمهم المناسك ، كالوقوف بعرفة والمزدلفة، والجمع بهما، والذبح والحلق والطواف وسائر المناسك إلى الخطبة الثالثة، ثم يدعو الله حالة وينزل».
The Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram. Then from there to Arafat, and all of it is a place of standing except the valley of Uranah. And when the sun has passed its zenith from it, the imam delivers two sermons like Friday, and teaches in them the rites. His statement: 'and all of it' means all of the valley of Arafat is a place of standing, so one stands in any place he wishes, and avoids Batn Uranah - with damm on 'ayn, fatha on ra', and fatha on nun - a valley in Arafat; due to the hadith: 'All of Arafat is a place of standing, and avoid the valley of Uranah, and all of Muzdalifah is a place of standing, and avoid the valley of Muhassir.' Reported by Ibn Majah and others. His statement: 'he delivers a sermon' etc.; Al-Lubab said: 'When he reaches Arafat, he stays there supplicating, praying, remembering, and reciting talbiyah. When the sun passes its zenith, he performs ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is better. Then he proceeds to the mosque, i.e., the mosque of Namirah without delay. When he reaches it, the greater imam or his deputy ascends the minbar, sits on it, and the mu'adhdhins call the adhan before him. When he finishes, the imam stands and delivers two sermons, praising Allah and extolling Him, reciting talbiyah, tahleel, takbir, sending blessings on the Prophet ﷺ, admonishing the people, commanding them, forbidding them, and teaching them the rites, such as standing at Arafat, Muzdalifah, the combined prayer there, slaughtering, shaving, tawaf, and all the rites up to the third sermon. Then he supplicates to Allah while standing, and descends.'
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the boundaries of the place of standing (wuquf) at Arafat during Hajj. The matn states that all of Arafat is a valid place for wuquf except the valley known as Batn Uranah. The commentary clarifies that 'every part of the valley of Arafat is a place of standing' meaning a pilgrim may choose any spot within its boundaries, but must avoid Batn Uranah, which is a specific valley within Arafat. The proof is a hadith narrated by Ibn Majah and others: 'All of Arafat is a place of standing, and avoid the valley of Uranah; all of Muzdalifah is a place of standing, and avoid the valley of Muhassir.' This establishes the exception. The commentary then turns to the imam's two sermons on the day of Arafat. Quoting from 'Al-Lubab', it describes the sequence: after reaching Arafat, the pilgrim engages in dhikr and dua; at noon, he performs ghusl (preferred) or wudu; then proceeds to the mosque of Namirah. The imam ascends the minbar, the adhan is called, and he delivers two sermons teaching the rites. The sermons include praising Allah, talbiyah, takbir, blessing the Prophet, and instructing the people about standing at Arafat, Muzdalifah, the combined prayers, sacrifice, shaving, tawaf, and all other rites. The imam concludes with supplication. This passage defines both the location for wuquf and the ritual of the sermon.

Key Terms
موقف (mawqif): The place where standing (wuquf) is performed during Hajj at Arafat.
بطن عرنة (baṭn ʿuranah): A valley within Arafat that is excluded from the valid place of standing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which area within Arafat is NOT a valid place for wuquf?
A) The entire valley of Arafat
B) Batn Uranah
C) The mosque of Namirah
D) The desert of Arafat

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school excludes Batn Uranah from the valid mawqif based on a clear prophetic command, emphasizing the importance of precise location in Hajj rituals.

Conditions for Combining Prayers at Arafat
Stating conditions for combining at Arafat with proof from prophetic practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for combining zuhr and asr at Arafat and apply them to determine who may participate.

Core Idea
Combining prayers at Arafat is a sunnah concession restricted to those in ihram praying with an imam.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on combining the zuhr and asr prayers at Arafat on the day of Arafat. The Prophet ﷺ established this practice, and the Hanafi school specifies conditions: the prayer must be led by an imam, and all worshipers must be in the state of ihram for the Hajj. The passage expands on the base text, providing the procedure and rationale for these restrictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining zuhr and asr at Arafat using jam' al-taqdim (advancing asr to zuhr time). The ruling is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) based on the Prophet's practice.
Not fard or wajib; it is a concession for ease during the Hajj.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof comes from the Sunna of the Prophet ﷺ, transmitted via abundant narrations (e.g., Jabir's report in Sahih Muslim). The actual practice (fi'l) of the Prophet is the evidence.
The dalil is ahad but established with multiple chains.
3
Identify the conditions
The text states two conditions: the prayer must be led by an imam (congregation), and everyone must be in ihram. These conditions are necessary for the validity of the combined prayer.
Combining is an exception to the general rule (khilaf al-qiyas), so it is restricted to its specific context.
4
Understand the exceptions
Combining is not allowed for a person who prays either zuhr or asr alone (without congregation), nor for one who prayed zuhr with the imam but was not in ihram, even if he later enters ihram.
The concession is for the gathered congregation in ihram, not for individuals.
5
Note the procedure
The imam leads both prayers with one adhan (sufficient for time announcement) and two iqamas (one for each prayer). No supererogatory prayer is performed between them. If the imam is a traveller, he prays 2 rak'ahs; residents follow and complete to 4.
The adhan is common; each prayer has its own iqama.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلى بهم الظهر والعصر بأذان وإقامتين ، وشُرِطَ الإمام والإحرام فيهما ، فلا يجوز العصر للمنفرد في أحدهما، ولا لمن صلى الظهر بجماعة ثم أحرم
قوله : أي في وقت الظهر؛ هذا جمع التقديم، اتفق عليه أهل العلم لثبوته عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بالروايات المستفيضة، وكذا جمع التأخير بمزدلفة، وفي ذكر الظهر إشارة إلى أنه لا يصلي صلاة الجمعة يوم عرفة إن كان يوم الجمعة، وقد مر ذكره في موضعه.
قوله : بأذان وإقامتين ؛ هكذا نقل عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في «صحيح مسلم» وغيره، والسرّ فيه : أنّ الأذان لإعلام دخول الوقت، فيكفي الواحد، بخلاف الإقامة، فيؤذن المؤذن ويقيم، فيصلّي بهم الظهر ثم يقيم للعصر، فيصلي العصر، ولا يفصل بينهما بتطوع.
ثم إن كان الإمامُ مسافراً يُصلّي بهم ركعتين ركعتين، ويقتدي به المسافرون والمقيمون، ويتم المقيمون ركعتين ركعتين، وإن كان مقيماً يُصلّي أربعاً أربعاً، ويأتم به القوم كلهم.
قوله : وشرط ... الخ ؛ لَمَّا كان الجمعُ على غير القياس، وما هو كذلك لا يتعدى إلى ما هو غير مورده ، ومورد هذا الجمع هو كون الصلاة مع الإمام والإحرام، اشترطوا لهما ذلك.
قوله : للمنفرد في أحدهما ؛ أي الظهر والعصر، فمَن صَلَّى أحدهما منفرداً من غير جماعة لا يجمع، بل يُصلي كل منهما في وقته.
قوله : ولا لمن صلّى ... الخ ؛ أي لا يجوز الجمع من صلى الظهر مع الإمام ، وهو غير محرم، ثم أحرم بالحج في وادي عرفة.
And he leads them in zuhr and asr with one adhan and two iqamas, and the condition is the imam and ihram in them. So asr is not permissible for one who prays alone in either of them, nor for one who prayed zuhr in congregation then entered ihram.  His statement: 'i.e., in the time of zuhr' – this is combining by advance (jam' taqdim), agreed upon by the scholars due to its established transmission from the Prophet ﷺ via abundant narrations, and similarly combining by delay at Muzdalifah. Mentioning zuhr indicates that he does not pray Friday on the day of Arafat if it is Friday, and this was mentioned in its place.  His statement: 'with one adhan and two iqamas' – this is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ in Sahih Muslim and elsewhere. The wisdom is that the adhan is for announcing the entrance of the time, so one is sufficient, unlike the iqama. So the mu'adhdhin calls the adhan and iqama, then he leads them in zuhr, then he says iqama for asr, then he leads asr, and he does not separate between them with supererogatory prayer.  Then if the imam is a traveller, he leads them in two rak'ahs each, and travellers and residents follow him, and the residents complete two more rak'ahs. If he is a resident, he prays four rak'ahs each, and all the people follow him.  His statement: 'and the condition...' – since combining is contrary to analogy, and what is contrary to analogy does not extend beyond its specific context, and the context of this combining is prayer with an imam and ihram, they stipulated these conditions.  His statement: 'for one who prays alone in either of them' – i.e., zuhr and asr. Whoever prays one of them alone without a congregation does not combine, but prays each in its time.  His statement: 'nor for one who prayed...' – i.e., it is not permissible to combine for one who prayed zuhr with the imam while not in ihram, then entered ihram for Hajj in the valley of Arafat.
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the combined prayer (jam' taqdim) at Arafat on the day of Arafat. The matn states that the imam leads the congregation in zuhr and asr with one adhan and two iqamas, and it is conditional that the prayer is performed with an imam and in the state of ihram. Consequently, a person who prays zuhr or asr alone without a congregation cannot combine; he must pray each in its own time. Similarly, a person who prayed zuhr with the imam but was not in ihram, and then entered ihram, cannot combine asr with that zuhr. The commentary expands on several points: (1) The time: this combining is jam' taqdim (advancing asr to zuhr time), which is established by the Prophet's practice via numerous narrations and is agreed upon by scholars. The mention of zuhr implicitly excludes Friday prayer; if the day of Arafat is Friday, the imam does not pray Friday but zuhr. (2) The procedure: one adhan suffices for both prayers because it announces the time, but each prayer has its own iqama. No supererogatory prayer is performed between them. (3) The imam's travel status: if the imam is a traveller (musafir), he prays two rak'ahs for each prayer, and residents follow him but complete their prayers to four rak'ahs after his taslim. If the imam is a resident, he prays four rak'ahs. (4) The rationale for conditions: since combining prayers is an exception from the general rule (qiyas), it is restricted to its specific context, which is the large congregation under an imam and the state of ihram. Thus, individual prayer without imam or without ihram does not qualify for the concession of combining.

Key Terms
جمع التقديم (jam' al-taqdim): Combining two prayers by offering the second prayer (asr) in the time of the first (zuhr), done at Arafat on the day of Arafat.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, which is a condition for the validity of the combined prayer at Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any pilgrim in ihram praying alone
B) A person who missed the zuhr congregation and enters ihram later
C) The imam and the congregation, all of whom are in ihram
D) Only the imam, regardless of his ihram status

Key Takeaway
Conditions of imam and ihram restrict the sunnah of combining at Arafat to a congregational setting during Hajj.

Combining Zuhr and Asr on Arafah: Conditions and Sunnah
Explains the ruling and conditions for joining Zuhr and Asr on Arafah with one adhan and two iqamahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for combining Zuhr and 'Asr on 'Arafah and explain the evidence from the sunnah.

Core Idea
Combining prayers on 'Arafah is a sunnah conditional on imam and ihram.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on combining Zuhr and 'Asr on the day of 'Arafah. The text from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the conditions and the proof from the Prophet's practice. Understanding this exception to the general rule of praying each prayer in its time is crucial for the pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining (jam') Zuhr and 'Asr on 'Arafah by advancing 'Asr to Zuhr time. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) when conditions are met.
The text explicitly states this is jam' al-taqdim, agreed upon by scholars.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Jabir (RA) in Sahih Muslim: the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed Zuhr and 'Asr with one adhan and two iqamahs, with no supererogatory between them.
Ibn Mas'ud's hadith also confirms this practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit action of the Prophet demonstrates the permissibility and recommendation. The imperative by action indicates sunnah. The omission of nafl between them is part of the practice.
The adhan suffices for both because it announces the time; each prayer gets its own iqamah.
4
Note the conditions (shurut)
Two conditions are required: the presence of an imam (congregation) and the state of ihram for both prayers. Without both, combining is not valid.
The text says 'Shurita al-imam wa al-ihram fihima'.
5
Apply the conditions to edge cases
A person praying alone (munfarid) cannot combine, even if in ihram. A person who prayed Zuhr with the congregation but was not in ihram cannot combine, even if he later enters ihram.
The condition of ihram must be present at the time of each prayer in the jam'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلى بهم الظهر والعصر بأذان وإقامتين ، وشُرِطَ الإمام والإحرام فيهما ، فلا يجوز العصر للمنفرد في أحدهما، ولا لمن صلى الظهر بجماعة ثم أحرم وصلى بهم الظهر والعصر ) : أي في وقتِ الظُّهر، بأذان وإقامتين ، وشرط الإمام والإحرام فيهما ، فلا يجوز العصر للمنفرد في أحدهما، ولا لِمَن صلى الظهر بجماعة ثُمَّ أحرم [1]قوله : أي في وقت الظهر؛ هذا جمع التقديم، اتفق عليه أهل العلم لثبوته عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بالروايات المستفيضة) ، وكذا جمع التأخير بمزدلفة، وفي ذكر الظهر إشارة إلى أنه لا يصلي صلاة الجمعة يوم عرفة إن كان يوم الجمعة، وقد مر ذكره في موضعه. [2] قوله : بأذان وإقامتين ؛ هكذا نقل عن رسول الله ) في «صحيح مسلم» وغيره، والسرّ فيه : أنّ الأذان لإعلام دخول الوقت، فيكفي الواحد، بخلاف الإقامة، فيؤذن المؤذن ويقيم، فيصلّي بهم الظهر ثم يقيم للعصر، فيصلي العصر، ولا يفصل بينهما بتطوع.

ثم إن كان الإمامُ مسافراً يُصلّي بهم ركعتين ركعتين، ويقتدي به المسافرون والمقيمون، ويتم المقيمون ركعتين ركعتين، وإن كان مقيماً يُصلّي أربعاً أربعاً، ويأتم به القوم كلهم.

[3]قوله : وشرط ... الخ ؛ لَمَّا كان الجمعُ على غير القياس، وما هو كذلك لا يتعدى إلى ما هو غير مورده ، ومورد هذا الجمع هو كون الصلاة مع الإمام والإحرام، اشترطوا لهما ذلك.

[4]قوله ؛ للمنفرد في أحدهما ؛ أي الظهر والعصر، فمَن صَلَّى أحدهما منفرداً من غير جماعة لا يجمع، بل يُصلي كل منهما في وقته. ( 1 ) قوله : ولا لمن صلّى ... الخ ؛ أي لا يجوز الجمع من صلى الظهر مع الإمام ، وهو غير محرم، ثم أحرم بالحج في وادي عرفة.

(۱) فعن ابن مسعود ه قال : كان رسول الله الله يصلي الصلاة لوقتها إلا بجمع وعرفات» في سنن النسائي الكبرى (۲) : (٤۲۳) ، و(المجتبى (٥) : ٢٥٤) ، وإسناده صحيح كما في «إعلاء السنن» (٢ : ٨٤)، وغيره.

(۲) فعن جابر : «إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أذن ثم أقام فصلى الظهر، ثم أقام فصلى العصر ولم يصل بينهما شيئاً» في «صحيح مسلم (۲) : (۸۹۰) ، و (صحیح ابن خزيمة»(٤ : ٢٥٢)، وغيرها.

إلا في وقتِه " ) : هذا استثناء من قوله : فلا يجوز العصر، وإِنما خَصَّ العصر بهذا الحكم ؛ لأنَّ الظهر جائز لوقوعه في وقتِه ، أما العصر فلا يجوز قبل الوقت إلا بشرط الجماعة في صلاة الظهر والعصر، وكونِهِ مُحْرِماً في كلِّ واحدٍ من الصلاتين (ثم ذَهَبَ إلى الموقف بغُسل سُن"، ووقف الإمام على ناقته بقرب جبل الرحمة (١) قوله : إلا في وقته ؛ أي لا يجوز العصر لمن فاته الإحرام أو الجماعة فيهما، أو في أحدهما في وقت من الأوقات إلا في وقت العصر.

[٤] [٢] قوله : إلى الموقف ; - بكسر القاف - : أي موضع الوقوف، «فإنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعدما صلّى أتــى المـوقـف واشتغل في الذكر والدعاء مستقبل القبلة علــى ناقته إلى الغروب ، أخرجه مسلم وغيره. [٣] قوله : سُن ؛ مجهول، وهو صفة لغسل، وظاهره أنه يسن الغسل عند الرواح إلى الموقف بعد الفراغ من الصلاة ) ، وقيل : إنّه قبل ذلك، فإنَّه يُسنّ أن لا يؤخر بين الفراغ من الصلاة وبين ذهابه إلى الموقف.

[٤] قوله : جبل الرحمة ؛ هو جبل بوسط وادي عرفات، وموقف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عند الحجرات السود التي بقربها.

(۱) فعن جابر ه: «إن رسول الله أتى الموقف فجعل بطن ناقته القصواء إلى الصخرات وجعل حبل - أي طريقهم - المشاة بين يديه واستقبل القبلة) في (صحيح مسلم»(۲ : ۸۹۰). وعن عمرو بن شعيب عن أبيه عن جده الله ، قال : «خير الدعاء : دعاء يوم عرفة، وخير ما قلت أنا والنبيون من قبلي : لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له ، له الملك وله الحمد، وهو على كل شيء قدير» في سنن الترمذي (۲) : ٥٧٢ ، ورجاله ثقات عند أحمد. كما في «إعلاء السنن»(۱۰ : ۱۲۹). وعن الفضل له قال : «رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم واقفاً بعرفة ماداً يديه كالمستطعم أو كلمة نحوها» في مسند البزار (٦) : ۱۰۲ ) ، و التاريخ الكبير (۱ : ۱۲۷). وعن سليمان بن موسى ، قال : «لم يحفظ عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه رفع يديه الرفع كله إلا في ثلاثة مواطن : الاستسقاء، والاستنصار وعشيّة عرفة ، ثم كان بعد رفع دون رفع» في «مراسيل أبي داود (ص۱۵۳)، وقال شيحنا الأرنؤوط : رجاله ثقات.

(۲) روي : «إن عليا لله كان يغتسل يوم العيدين، ويوم الجمعة ، ويوم عرفة، وإذا أراد أن يحرم» في مسند الشافعي (ص٧٤)، وغيرها.
[He] prayed Zuhr and 'Asr with them with one adhan and two iqamahs, and the imam and ihram are conditions for them both, so 'Asr is not permissible for the individual in either of them, nor for the one who prayed Zuhr with congregation then entered ihram... [1] His saying: meaning in the time of Zuhr; this is jam' al-taqdim, agreed upon by the scholars due to its being established from the Prophet (ﷺ) through frequently transmitted narrations, and likewise jam' al-ta'khir at Muzdalifah, and mentioning Zuhr indicates that the Friday prayer is not prayed on the day of 'Arafah if it is Friday, and its mention has passed in its place. [2] His saying: with one adhan and two iqamahs; thus it is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) in Sahih Muslim and others, and the secret behind it is that the adhan is to notify the entry of time, so one is sufficient, unlike the iqamah, so the mu'adhdhin adhans and he (the imam) gives iqamah, then prays Zuhr with them, then gives iqamah for 'Asr, then prays 'Asr, and there is no supererogatory prayer between them. Then if the imam is a traveler, he prays two rak'ahs with them, and the travelers and residents follow him, and the residents complete two rak'ahs each. And if he is a resident, he prays four rak'ahs each, and all the people follow him. [3] His saying: and condition... etc.; since the jam' is not based on qiyas, and what is like that does not extend beyond its applied case, and the case of this jam' is that the prayer is with the imam and ihram, they stipulated both of these. [4] His saying: for the individual in either of them; i.e., Zuhr and 'Asr; whoever prays either of them individually without a congregation does not combine, but rather prays each in its time. (1) His saying: nor for the one who prayed... etc; i.e., combining is not permissible for the one who prayed Zuhr with the imam while he was not in ihram, then he entered ihram for Hajj in the valley of 'Arafah. (1) From Ibn Mas'ud (RA) that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) used to pray the prayers at their times except at Jam' (Muzdalifah) and 'Arafat. (In Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra, etc.) (2) From Jabir (RA) that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) gave adhan then iqamah and prayed Zuhr, then gave iqamah and prayed 'Asr, and he did not pray anything between them. (In Sahih Muslim, etc.) "Except in its time": This is an exception from his saying: "So 'Asr is not permissible". And he specified 'Asr with this ruling because Zuhr is permissible due to occurring in its time, but 'Asr is not permissible before its time except with the condition of congregation in Zuhr and 'Asr, and that he be in ihram in each of the two prayers. (Then he went to the standing place with a sunnah ghusl, and the imam stood on his she-camel near the Mount of Mercy.) [1] His saying: except in its time; i.e., 'Asr is not permissible for the one who missed ihram or congregation in both or in one of them in any time, except in the time of 'Asr. [2] His saying: to the standing place (al-mawqif); with kasrah on the qaf, i.e., the place of standing. Indeed, the Prophet (ﷺ) after praying came to the standing place and engaged in remembrance and supplication facing the qibla on his she-camel until sunset, reported by Muslim and others. [3] His saying: sunnah; it is passive, and it is a description of ghusl, and its apparent is that ghusl is recommended at the time of going to the standing place after finishing the prayers, and it is said that it is before that, for it is recommended not to delay between finishing the prayers and going to the standing place. [4] His saying: Mount of Mercy; it is a mountain in the middle of the valley of 'Arafat, and the standing place of the Prophet (ﷺ) is near the black rocks that are near it. (1) From Jabir (RA) that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) came to the standing place and made the belly of his she-camel al-Qaswa' toward the rocks and made the rope - meaning their path - the pedestrians in front of him and faced the qibla. (In Sahih Muslim, etc.) And from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather (RA) that he said: The best of supplication is the supplication on the day of 'Arafah, and the best that I and the prophets before me said is: There is no deity but Allah alone, no partner for Him, to Him belongs the dominion and to Him belongs praise, and He is over all things competent. (In Sunan al-Tirmidhi, etc.) And from al-Fadl (RA) that he said: I saw the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) standing at 'Arafah extending his hands like a beggar or similar phrase. (In Musnad al-Bazzar, etc.) And from Sulayman ibn Musa (RA) that he said: It is not preserved from the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) that he raised his hands in full raising except in three situations: seeking rain, seeking victory, and the evening of 'Arafah, then after that he would raise less than full raising. (In Marasil Abi Dawud, etc.) (2) It is narrated that 'Ali (RA) used to perform ghusl on the two 'Eids, on Friday, on the day of 'Arafah, and when he intended to enter ihram. (In Musnad al-Shafi'i, etc.)
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a ruling regarding the combination (jama') of Zuhr and 'Asr on the day of 'Arafah during Hajj. The author begins by stating the ruling: the imam prays both Zuhr and 'Asr with one adhan and two iqamahs, but two conditions are required: the presence of an imam and the state of ihram. If either condition is missing, the 'Asr prayer cannot be performed before its time via jama'. Specifically, a person praying alone (munfarid) is not allowed to combine; nor is a person who prayed Zuhr with the congregation but was not in ihram permitted to combine, even if he later enters ihram. The commentary clarifies that this combination is jam' al-taqdim (advancing 'Asr to Zuhr time), which is unanimously agreed upon by scholars due to authentic hadith. The reason for one adhan and two iqamahs is that the adhan is for announcing the time of the first prayer only, while each prayer requires its own iqamah. No supererogatory prayer is offered between them. The text then discusses the number of rak'ahs: if the imam is a traveler, he prays two rak'ahs for each, and the residents complete two extra rak'ahs after the imam's salaam; if the imam is a resident, all pray four. The condition of imam and ihram is necessary because jama' is an exception to the general rule of praying each prayer in its time, and exceptions are not extended beyond their specified cases. The author then explains the exception 'except in its time' for 'Asr: if the conditions of congregational prayer and ihram are not met, then 'Asr must be delayed until its own time. After the prayers, it is sunnah to perform ghusl before proceeding to the standing place (al-mawqif) at 'Arafah, and the imam should stand near Jabal al-Rahmah on his mount, facing the qibla and engaging in remembrance and supplication until sunset. The commentary includes several hadith to support these practices, including the famous hadith of Jabir describing the actions of the Prophet (ﷺ) on that day.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam'): Combining two obligatory prayers in one time, specifically here jam' al-taqdim for Zuhr and 'Asr on 'Arafah.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, which is a condition for the validity of combining prayers on 'Arafah.
المنفرد (al-munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation. Such a person is not permitted to combine Zuhr and 'Asr on 'Arafah.
الموقف (al-mawqif): The standing place at 'Arafah where pilgrims gather after the combined prayers, engaging in supplication until sunset.
الغسل (ghusl): The ritual bath recommended (sunnah) before going to the standing place on 'Arafah.
جبل الرحمة (Jabal al-Rahmah): A mountain in the middle of the valley of 'Arafat, near which the Prophet (ﷺ) stood and which is the most meritorious place for wuquf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two conditions required for the validity of combining Zuhr and 'Asr on the day of 'Arafah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Traveling and rain
B) Imam and ihram
C) Fear and illness
D) Friday and Jumu'ah

Key Takeaway
Combining Zuhr and 'Asr on 'Arafah is a sunnah that requires the presence of an imam and the state of ihram; without these, the combination is not valid.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Sunnah Acts of Standing at Arafah and Muzdalifah
Describes the Prophet's sunnah actions from Arafah to Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah actions at Arafah and Muzdalifah as described in the Hanafi school and identify which parts are sunnah versus wajib.

Core Idea
The Prophet's sunnah at Arafah and Muzdalifah includes ghusl, facing qibla, supplication, and staying until sunset; all of Muzdalifah except Wadi Muhassir is valid for standing.

The Hajj rituals include many sunnah actions that enhance the spiritual experience. This passage from the sharh details the Prophet's practice when standing at Arafah and then moving to Muzdalifah, providing a model for pilgrims to emulate. Understanding these sunnah acts helps maximize the rewards of Hajj while avoiding common pitfalls.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts at Arafah
Scan the passage for the actions mentioned: ghusl, standing near Jabal al-Rahmah facing qibla, supplicating with exertion, and teaching the rituals.
The ghusl is sunnah, not obligatory.
2
Understand the timing and movement
Note that the Prophet left Arafah after sunset. Delaying departure until sunset is sunnah; leaving earlier is makruh but does not invalidate Hajj.
The standing itself is valid regardless of departure time according to Hanafis.
3
Recognize the valid areas in Muzdalifah
All of Muzdalifah is a place for standing (mawqif) except Wadi Muhassir. Pilgrims should avoid standing in this valley.
Wadi Muhassir is between Muzdalifah and Mina.
4
Apply the sunnah to modern practice
Pilgrims today can follow these sunnah acts: perform ghusl before Arafah, stand facing qibla, make du'a, and proceed to Muzdalifah after sunset, then stand near Jabal Quzah.
These actions are recommended, not required for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ ذَهَبَ إلى الموقف بغُسلِ سُنّ، ووقف الإمام على ناقته بقرب جبل الرحمة مستقبلاً، ودَعَا بجهد، وعَلَّمَ المناسك، ووقف الناس خلفه بقربه مستقبلين سامعين مَقُولَه، وإذا غَرَبَتْ أتى مُزْدَلِفَةً وكلها موقف إلا وادي مُحَسّر ونزلَ عند جبلٍ قُزَح مستقبلاً، ودَعَا بجهد، وعلم المناسك، ووقف الناس خلفَهُ بقربه مستقبلينَ سامعينَ مَقُولَه.
Then he went to the standing place with a sunnah ghusl, and the Imam stood on his she-camel near Jabal al-Rahmah facing the qibla, and he supplicated with exertion, and taught the rituals, and the people stood behind him near him facing and listening to his words. And when the sun set, he came to Muzdalifah, all of which is a standing place except Wadi Muhassir, and he descended near Jabal Quzah facing the qibla, and supplicated with exertion, and taught the rituals, and the people stood behind him near him facing and listening to his words.
Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage describes the recommended (sunnah) actions of the Prophet during the Hajj after the combined prayer. It is an expansion on the matn, detailing the sequence: first, the pilgrim performs a ghusl (ritual bath) as a sunnah before going to Arafah for the standing. Then the imam (or the pilgrim if alone) proceeds to the standing area near Jabal al-Rahmah, facing the qibla, and engages in earnest supplication and teaching of Hajj rituals. The people stand behind him, also facing the qibla and listening. After sunset, the pilgrim moves to Muzdalifah (also called al-Mash'ar al-Haram), and all of Muzdalifah is a valid place for standing except Wadi Muhassir (a valley between Muzdalifah and Mina). Upon arrival, the pilgrim descends near Jabal Quzah, again faces the qibla, and repeats the supplication and teaching. The commentator notes that the ghusl is recommended either after the prayer or before going, with the apparent view being after prayer. This is a sunnah, and one who delays the departure from Arafah until after sunset is following the prophetic example; leaving before sunset is disapproved (makes it bad, but the standing is still valid according to the Hanafi school).

Key Terms
الموقف (al-mawqif): The place of standing at Arafah
غسل سنة (ghusl sunnah): A recommended ritual bath before going to Arafah
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Arafah and Mina where pilgrims spend the night
وادي محسر (Wadi Muhassir): A valley between Muzdalifah and Mina where standing is not valid

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on leaving Arafah before sunset according to the commentary?
A) It is permissible and recommended
B) It is impermissible and invalidates Hajj
C) It is disapproved (isaa) but the standing is still valid
D) It is obligatory to leave after sunset

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's sunnah at Arafah and Muzdalifah provides a model for pilgrims to maximize their devotion; the key practices include ghusl, facing qibla, supplication, staying until sunset, and avoiding Wadi Muhassir.

Sunnah Time for Ifadah and Valid Wuquf at Muzdalifah
Explains the sunnah time to depart Arafat and valid standing at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah time for departing Arafat and identify the valid standing area in Muzdalifah, applying the Hanafi ruling to a pilgrim's scenario.

Core Idea
Depart Arafat after sunset; all Muzdalifah is valid standing except Wadi Muhassir.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains two key sunnahs of Hajj: the time to leave Arafat and the place to stand in Muzdalifah. The Prophet ﷺ remained at Arafat until after sunset and then proceeded to Muzdalifah, where he stood at Mount Quzah and taught that all of Muzdalifah is a standing place except a specific valley. Understanding these rulings ensures the pilgrim follows the prophetic practice and avoids invalidating their wuquf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (departure from Arafat) and its hukm level (sunnah). Note the consequence of departing early (asaa – doing wrong, not haram).
Departure before sunset is a violation of the sunnah, not a sin requiring expiation.
2
Locate the dalil for the ruling
The passage quotes hadith from Jabir showing the Prophet waited until complete sunset. Identify this as the primary evidence (sunnah fi'liyyah).
Also references from Muslim, Ibn Khuzaymah, etc.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's action (waiting until after sunset) indicates the sunnah; doing otherwise opposes his practice.
The evidence is zanni al-dalala, leading to sunnah, not wujub.
4
Identify the scope of valid standing at Muzdalifah
Extract the ruling that all Muzdalifah is a valid standing area except Wadi Muhassir. Note the exclusion and its basis in hadith.
Standing in Wadi Muhassir invalidates wuquf; also Batin Urana at Arafat is excluded.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Some schools consider wuquf at Muzdalifah wajib, but Hanafis deem it sunnah. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is sunnah, as confirmed by al-Marghinani.
Practical difference: if omitted, no dam in Hanafi school (since sunnah), but others require a sacrifice.

مستقبلاً، ودعا بجهد، وعلم المناسك، ووقف الناس خلفه بقربه مستقبلين سامعين مقوله، وإذا غربت أتى مزدلفة وكلها موقف إلا وادي محسر ونزل عند جبل قزح مستقبلاً، ودعا بجهد، وعلم المناسك، ووقف الناس خلفه بقربه مستقبلين سامعين مقوله. قوله: بجهد - بفتح الجيم وبضمها - أي باجتهاد وتضرع. قوله: وإذا غربت؛ فلو أفاض قبل الغروب أساء لمخالفته للسنة، فإنه أفاض بعد الغروب، أخرجه الترمذي وغيره. قوله: وكلها؛ أي جميع المزدلفة يجوز فيه الوقوف ما سوى وادي محسر، لما مر من الحديث، وهو على وزن اسم فاعل من باب التفعيل: واد بين مزدلفة ومنى، فلو وقف به أو ببطن عرنة بعرفة لم يجز ذلك. قوله: محسر؛ هذا النزول الخاص مستحب، وأما أصل الوقوف بمزدلفة. قوله: عند جبل قزح - بضم القاف وفتح الزاي المعجمة، ثم حاء مهملة - أي مبيت؛ لأن التبييت بمزدلفة ليلة النحر سنة. ينظر: فتح باب العناية (1:656). لأنه هو الموقف، فينزل عنده، ولا ينزل على الطريق؛ كيلا يضيق على المارة، ولا ينفرد في النزول. ينظر: التبيين (2:27). فعن جابر: إن رسول الله لم يزل واقفاً حتى غربت الشمس وذهبت الصفرة قليلاً حتى غاب القرص، وأردف أسامة خلفه ودفع رسول الله في صحيح مسلم (2:890)، وصحيح ابن خزيمة (4:258)، وصحيح ابن حبان (9:257)، وغيرها. وعن المسور بن مخرمة، قال: خطبنا رسول الله بعرفات فحمد الله وأثنى عليه، ثم قال: أما بعد؛ فإن أهل الشرك والأوثان كانوا يدفعون من هذا الموضع إذا كانت الشمس على رؤوس الجبال، كأنها عمائم الرجال في وجوهها، وإنا ندفع بعد أن تغيب في المستدرك (3:601)، وقال الحاكم: هذا حديث صحيح على شرط الشيخين ولم يخرجاه. فعن ابن عباس، قال: ارفعوا عن بطن محسر في صحيح ابن خزيمة (4:254)، والمستدرك (1:633)، وصححه. وعن جابر، قال: كل المزدلفة موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن محسر في سنن ابن ماجة (2:1002)، وسنن أبي داود (2:193)، وسنن البيهقي الكبير (5:122)، وغيرها.
Facing the qibla, and he supplicated earnestly, and taught the rituals, and the people stood behind him near him, facing and listening to his words. And when the sun set, he came to Muzdalifah, and all of it is a standing place except the Valley of Muhassir, and he camped at Mount Quzah, facing the qibla, and supplicated earnestly, and taught the rituals, and the people stood behind him near him, facing and listening to his words. His statement: 'with effort' – with fatha on jim and dammah on it – meaning with striving and humility. His statement: 'when it set' – if he departed before sunset, he does wrong due to opposing the sunnah, for he (the Prophet) departed after sunset, recorded by Tirmidhi and others. His statement: 'all of it' – i.e., all of Muzdalifah, standing is permitted in it except the Valley of Muhassir, due to the hadith mentioned earlier, and it is a valley between Muzdalifah and Mina. If one stands there or in Batin Urana at Arafat, it is not valid. His statement: 'Muhassir' – this specific descent is recommended, but the original standing at Muzdalifah... His statement: 'at Mount Quzah' – with dammah on qaf and fatha on zay, then a hamza? – i.e., overnight stay, because staying overnight at Muzdalifah on the night of sacrifice is sunnah. Refer to Fath Bab al-Inayah. Because it is the standing place, so he camps near it, and does not camp on the road so as not to inconvenience passersby, and he does not isolate himself in camping. Refer to al-Tabyin. From Jabir: 'The Messenger of Allah did not stop until the sun set and the redness disappeared a little until the disk disappeared, and he proceeded...' in Sahih Muslim, etc. From al-Miswar ibn Makhramah: 'The Messenger of Allah addressed us at Arafat...' in al-Mustadrak. From Ibn Abbas: 'Leave aside the valley of Muhassir' in Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah and al-Mustadrak. From Jabir: 'All of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and leave aside the valley of Muhassir' in Sunan Ibn Majah, etc.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the sunnah regarding the departure from Arafat and the place of standing at Muzdalifah. The text states that the Prophet ﷺ stood at Arafat until after sunset and then proceeded to Muzdalifah, establishing that the sunnah is to depart after sunset, not before. The valley of Muhassir between Muzdalifah and Mina is excluded from the valid standing area; standing there invalidates the wuquf. The area of Batin Urana at Arafat also invalidates standing. The text also recommends descending at Mount Quzah in Muzdalifah for supplication and staying overnight is sunnah. Hadith proofs are provided from various sources, including Jabir, al-Miswar, and Ibn Abbas.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): The place between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims stand after sunset on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah.
وادي محسر (Wadi Muhassir): A valley between Muzdalifah and Mina; standing there is not valid.
قزح (Quzah): A mountain in Muzdalifah; standing there is recommended (sunnah).
الإفاضة (al-ifadah): The departure from Arafat to Muzdalifah after sunset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is a sin (haram).
B) It is disliked (makruh) but valid.
C) It is a violation of the sunnah (asaa).
D) It is permissible (mubah).

Key Takeaway
Departing Arafat after sunset and standing in Muzdalifah outside Wadi Muhassir are sunnah acts confirmed by the Prophet's practice; violating them is not haram but a loss of reward.

Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah: Ritual, Dispute, and Repetition
Explains combination ruling, intra-Hanafi dispute, and repetition obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling for combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, EXPLAIN the intra-Hanafi dispute on the iqamah, and APPLY the wajib repetition rule for Maghrib prayed before reaching Muzdalifah.

Core Idea
Combining at Muzdalifah is a wajib Hajj ritual, not a travel concession; one iqamah for both prayers is the relied-upon view.

The prayer at Muzdalifah is a distinctive ritual of Hajj, combining Maghrib and Isha in a single timeframe. While all schools agree on its occurrence, the Hanafi school has an internal debate on the number of iqamahs. This lesson walks through the ruling, the dispute, and the obligation to repeat Maghrib if performed on the way.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint that combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah is a wajib ritual of Hajj, not merely a travel concession. Note that it requires one adhan, and the dispute is on the iqamah.
The text states it is 'min manasik al-hajj' (from the rituals of Hajj).
2
State the intra-Hanafi dispute on the iqamah
Abu Hanifa held that the single iqamah is only for Maghrib because Isha is in its time. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held that one iqamah covers both prayers based on authentic hadiths.
The commentator says 'وهو الأرجح' (it is the more correct), favoring the Sahibayn.
3
Follow the evidence for each position
Abu Hanifa's dalil: Hadith in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah mentioning one adhan and one iqamah, plus the principle that Isha needs no announcement. Sahibayn's dalil: Hadith of Ibn Umar in Sahih Bukhari and Muslim stating 'with one iqamah' for both prayers.
The Sahih hadiths are considered more authoritative.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
The commentator gives preference to the Sahibayn because the authentic hadiths explicitly mention a single iqamah. This is the mufta bihi position.
Practical difference: if two iqamahs are given, it is still valid but contrary to sunnah.
5
Apply the repetition rule for Maghrib
The text states that if Maghrib was performed on the way to Muzdalifah, it must be repeated wajib at Muzdalifah because its valid performance is restricted to the time of Isha and the place Muzdalifah.
The hadith of Usamah supports this: 'The prayer is ahead of you.'

وصلى العشائين بأذان وإقامة وأعاد مغرباً إن أداه في الطريق. وصلى العشائين بأذان وإقامة هاهنا جمع المغرب والعشاء في وقت العشاء وأعاد مغرباً إن أداه في الطريق. وهو غير منصرف لوجود العدل التقديري فيه كعمر، وهو اسم للجبل الذي بالمزدلفة، وقد ثبت أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقف عليه، أخرجه الترمذي، والقازح في اللغة بمعنى المرتفع، وقيل: هو من القزح، بمعنى الطريق واللون. قوله: وصلى؛ ولا يشترط لهذا الجمع كونه بجماعة، نعم يشترط له الإحرام بالحج، وتقديم وقوف عرفة عليه، وهذا الجمع، وكذا الجمع بعرفة عندنا من مناسك الحج فيأتيه كل من حج، ولو لم يكن مسافراً. كذا في شرح لباب المناسك. قوله: بأذان وإقامة؛ أي واحدة، أما توحد الأذان فظاهر؛ لأنه لإعلام دخول الوقت، فيكفي الواحد، كما في الجمع بعرفة، وأما توحد الإقامة، وهي في الأولى؛ فلأن العشاء في وقته فلا يحتاج إلى الإعلام بوقته، بخلاف الصلاة الثانية في عرفة، فإنها مقدمة على وقتها، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، ويشهد له ما ورد في مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: إن النبي جمع بمزدلفة بأذان وإقامة، والذي ثبت في الصحاح الإقامة، وبه قال أبو يوسف ومحمد، وهو الأرجح. قوله: وقت العشاء؛ فلو وصل إلى المزدلفة قبل وقته لا يصلّيهما حتى يدخل وقت العشاء. قوله: وأعاد؛ أي وجوباً؛ لأن أداء المغرب في تلك الليلة مقيد بالزمان وهو وقت العشاء، والمكان وهو مزدلفة، يدل عليه قول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: الصلاة أمامك، لمن قال له في الطريق: الصلاة، وكذا لو صلى العشاء قبل الوصول بمزدلفة يعيده. عن جابر: صلى الله الفجر حين تبين له الصبح بأذان وإقامة، ثم ركب القصواء حتى أتى المشعر الحرام - أي جبل قزح -، فاستقبل القبلة فدعاه وكبره وهلله ووحده، فلم يزل واقفاً حتى أسفر جدا، فدفع قبل أن تطلع الشمس في صحيح مسلم (2:891)، وغيره. المسلك المتقسط (ص236). إذا كان الرجحان لكون الحديث في الصحيح، فها هو حديث الأذان والإقامة الواحدة في الصحيحين، فعن ابن عمر، قال: جمع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بين المغرب والعشاء بجمع: صلى المغرب ثلاثاً، والعشاء ركعتين بإقامة واحدة في صحيح مسلم (2:983)، وصحيح البخاري (2:602)، وغيرها. فعن أسامة، قال: الصلاة أمامك فركب فلما جاء المزدلفة في صحيح مسلم (2:934)، وصحيح البخاري (1:65)، وغيرهما.
And he prayed the two evening prayers (Maghrib and Isha) with one adhan and one iqamah, and he repeated Maghrib if he performed it on the way. And he prayed the two evening prayers with one adhan and one iqamah: here he combined Maghrib and Isha at the time of Isha, and he repeated Maghrib if he performed it on the way. And it is indeclinable due to the presence of estimated analogy in it like 'Umar, and it is the name of the mountain in Muzdalifah, and it is confirmed that the Messenger of Allah stood on it, recorded by Tirmidhi. Al-Qazih in language means high, and it is said it is from al-qazh, meaning road and color. His statement: 'and he prayed' – congregation is not required for this combination; rather, it requires ihram for Hajj, preceding wuquf at Arafat, and this combination. Likewise, the combination at Arafat, in our school, is from the rituals of Hajj, so every pilgrim performs it, even if not traveling. Thus in Sharh Lubab al-Manasik. His statement: 'with one adhan and iqamah' – i.e., one (of each). As for the singleness of the adhan, it is obvious because it is for announcing the entry of the time, so one adhan suffices, as in the combination at Arafat. As for the singleness of the iqamah – and it is for the first prayer – because Isha is in its time, so it does not need an announcement of its time, unlike the second prayer at Arafat, because it is advanced before its time. This is the view of Abu Hanifa, and it is supported by what is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: 'The Prophet combined at Muzdalifah with one adhan and one iqamah.' What is established in the authentic collections is the iqamah (singular), and that is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and it is the more correct (al-rajih). His statement: 'at the time of Isha' – if he reaches Muzdalifah before its time, he does not pray them until the time of Isha enters. His statement: 'and he repeated' – i.e., as an obligation; because the performance of Maghrib on that night is restricted by time (the time of Isha) and place (Muzdalifah), as indicated by the Prophet's statement to one who said 'prayer' on the road: 'The prayer is ahead of you.' Likewise, if he prayed Isha before reaching Muzdalifah, he repeats it. From Jabir: He prayed Fajr when dawn was clear with adhan and iqamah, then rode al-Qaswa until he came to al-Mash'ar al-Haram (Mount Quzah), faced the qibla, supplicated, and said Allahu Akbar, etc. in Sahih Muslim. Al-Maslik al-Mutassit (p.236). If the stronger view is that the hadith is in the authentic collections, here is the hadith of the single adhan and iqamah in the two Sahihs: from Ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah: he prayed Maghrib three rak'ahs and Isha two rak'ahs with one iqamah' in Sahih Muslim and Sahih Bukhari. From Usamah: he said 'The prayer is ahead of you' and he rode, and when he came to Muzdalifah... in Sahih Muslim and Bukhari.
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage contains rulings and an intra-Hanafi dispute about the prayer at Muzdalifah. The text begins by stating that the Prophet combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah with one adhan and one iqamah. The commentator explains that this combination is a specific ritual of Hajj, not merely a travel concession; it applies to all pilgrims, even those not considered travelers. The combination is performed at the time of Isha, so if one arrives at Muzdalifah before Isha time, he must wait. The text then addresses the issue of the adhan and iqamah. Abu Hanifa held that the single adhan is obvious, and the single iqamah is for the first prayer (Maghrib) because Isha is in its time. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held that the authentic hadiths (like that of Ibn Umar) mention only one iqamah for both prayers, and this is the more correct position (al-rajih). Finally, the text rules that if Maghrib was prayed on the way to Muzdalifah, it must be repeated at Muzdalifah because the performance of Maghrib on that night is restricted to both the time of Isha and the place Muzdalifah. The hadith of Usamah supports this, where the Prophet told him 'the prayer is ahead of you' when he asked about praying on the road.

Key Terms
جمع (jam'): Combining two prayers (Maghrib and Isha) at one time at Muzdalifah, a specific Hajj ritual.
أذان (adhan): The call to prayer; one adhan is given at Muzdalifah for the combined prayer.
إقامة (iqamah): The second call to commence prayer; the text discusses whether one iqamah is for only Maghrib or for both.
إعادة (i'adah): Repetition of Maghrib if it was performed on the way to Muzdalifah; wajib to repeat at Muzdalifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah is a wajib Hajj ritual; the single iqamah for both prayers is the relied-upon position, and Maghrib must be repeated if performed before reaching Muzdalifah.

Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah: A Hajj Ritual
Ruling and commentary on combining two prayers at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling and conditions for combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah and identify the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Combining at Muzdalifah is a Hajj ritual, not a travel concession—all pilgrims perform it.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya explains the Hanafi position on combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. It clarifies that this combination is a specific ritual of Hajj, not a general travel exemption. The commentator also discusses the name 'Qazah' and its significance and notes that congregation is not required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqama at Muzdalifah. In the Hanafi school, this is sunna mu'akkada (emphasized sunna).
The ruling derives from the Prophet's practice and the classification as a Hajj ritual.
2
List the conditions
Two conditions are required: being in ihram for Hajj and having performed wuquf at Arafah prior. Congregation is not a condition.
Travel is also not a condition; the combination is for all pilgrims.
3
Identify what is NOT a condition
Congregation and travel status are explicitly not required. The text states 'ولا يشترط لهذا الجمع كونه بجماعة' and 'ولو لم يكن مسافراً'.
This distinguishes it from general travel concessions.
4
Identify the proof
The commentator cites the hadith of the Prophet standing on Qazah mountain (reported by Tirmidhi). This establishes the location's significance; the combination itself is established by other texts (e.g., the practice of the Companions).
The proof is from Sunnah ahad, with zanni thubut and dalala.
5
Note the cross-madhhab distinction
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require travel for combining prayers. The Hanafi school treats this combination as a Hajj-specific ritual, so all pilgrims perform it regardless of travel.
The practical difference: a resident Hajji combines in Hanafi but not in other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الإحرام
وصلى العشائين بأذان وإقامة وأعاد مغرباً إن أداه في الطريق
وهو غير منصرف؛ لوجود العدل التقديري فيه كعُمَر، وهو اسم للجبل الذي بالمزدلفة، وقد ثبت أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقف عليه، أخرجه الترمذي، والقازح في اللغة بمعنى المرتفع، وقيل: هو من القزح، بمعنى الطريق واللون.
[1] قوله: وصلى؛ ولا يشترط لهذا الجمع كونه بجماعة، نعم يشترط له الإحرام بالحج، وتقديم وقوف عرفة عليه، وهذا الجمع، وكذا الجمع بعرفة عندنا من مناسك الحج فيأتيه كل من حج، ولو لم يكن مسافراً. كذا في "شرح لباب المناسك".
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram. And he prayed the two evening prayers (Maghrib and Isha) with one adhan and one iqama, and repeats Maghrib if he performed it on the road. It (Qazah) is non-declinable due to the presence of estimated 'adl (like 'Umar), and it is the name of a mountain at Muzdalifah. It has been established that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) stood upon it, reported by al-Tirmidhi. Qazih in language means elevated, and it is said it is from qazah meaning road and color. [1] He said: 'He prayed' — congregation is not a condition for this combination; rather, ihram for Hajj and prior standing at 'Arafah are conditions. This combination, like the combination at 'Arafah, in our school, is a ritual of Hajj, so every pilgrim performs it even if not a traveler. Thus in 'Sharh Lubab al-Manasik'.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on combining Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah during Hajj. The author, commenting on al-Wiqayah, first explains the name 'Qazah' as a mountain at Muzdalifah where the Prophet stood, citing a hadith from al-Tirmidhi. Then he clarifies that this combination does not require being in a congregation; rather, the essential conditions are having entered into ihram for Hajj and having performed the standing at 'Arafah. This combination, like the one at 'Arafah, is considered a ritual (manasik) of Hajj, performed by every pilgrim, whether a traveler or not. Thus, the ruling applies to all pilgrims, emphasizing that the combination is specific to the Hajj context and not a general travel concession.

Key Terms
قزح (Qazah): Name of a mountain at Muzdalifah where the Prophet stood.
العشائين (al-'ishā'ayn): The two evening prayers, i.e., Maghrib and Isha.

intermediate

Number of Adhan and Iqama at Muzdalifah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on number of iqama at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of iqamas for combined prayers at Muzdalifah and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The preponderant Hanafi view is one iqama for both Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah clarifies a subtle difference within the Hanafi school regarding the call to prayer for the combined prayers at Muzdalifah. While the matn states 'with one adhan and iqama,' the commentator unpacks the disagreement: Abu Hanifa held that the iqama is only for the first prayer, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argued for a single iqama for both. We will analyze the evidence and see which view is considered preponderant.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position from the matn
The matn says 'with one adhan and iqama'. The commentator explains that one adhan is agreed upon; the dispute is about the iqama: is it for the first prayer only or for both?
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Abu Hanifa holds that the iqama is only for Maghrib because Isha is in its own time and doesn't need notification. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that one iqama suffices for both prayers.
3
Analyze the proofs cited
Abu Hanifa's proof is a hadith from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: the Prophet combined at Muzdalifah with one adhan and iqama. The Sahibayn rely on authentic hadith in Bukhari and Muslim that show the Prophet prayed with one iqama only.
4
Determine the tarjih
The commentator states that the authentic collections (sihah) establish the iqama (i.e., one iqama) and that this is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, which is 'arjah' (preponderant). The weaker narration is overridden.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa's view, the iqama is called for Maghrib only; under the Sahibayn's view, it is called once for both. The preponderant view is single iqama.

[2] His saying: 'with one adhan and iqama' — meaning one each. As for the unity of adhan, it is apparent because it is for informing of the entry of time, so one suffices, as in the combination at 'Arafah. As for the unity of iqama, it is for the first prayer (Maghrib) because 'Isha is in its time so it does not need notification of its time, unlike the second prayer at 'Arafah which is advanced before its time. This is the view of Abu Hanifa. Supporting it is what is reported in 'Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah': 'The Prophet combined at Muzdalifah with one adhan and iqama'. What is established in the authentic collections is the iqama (by itself), and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said the same, and it is preponderant.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over the number of iqamas for the combined prayers at Muzdalifah. The matn states 'with one adhan and iqama'. The commentator explains that one adhan is agreed upon because it signals the start of time. The dispute is about the iqama: Abu Hanifa holds that the iqama is said only for the first prayer (Maghrib), since 'Isha is prayed in its own time and doesn't need an announcement. In contrast, at 'Arafah, the second prayer (Asr) is advanced, so a separate iqama is needed. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that only one iqama is said for both prayers, based on what is established in the authentic hadith collections (Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim) where the Prophet performed the two prayers with a single iqama. The commentator declares this latter view as preponderant (arjah). The hadith from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah supports Abu Hanifa's view, but the authentic hadith override it. Thus, the relied-upon practice is one iqama for both prayers.

Key Terms
إقامة (iqama): The second call to prayer immediately before the fard prayer.
أذان (adhan): The call to prayer announcing the entry of time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One iqama for both prayers.
C) No iqama, only adhan.
D) It depends on whether one is a traveler.

Key Takeaway
The preponderant Hanafi view is one iqama for both Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, based on authentic hadith.

Repeating Maghrib if Prayed Before Reaching Muzdalifah
Ruling on repeating Maghrib when performed on the road before Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating Maghrib prayed on the road before Muzdalifah and distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Maghrib on the night of Muzdalifah must be combined with Isha at Muzdalifah; praying on the road is invalid and must be repeated before dawn.

In this passage, we examine the ruling when a pilgrim prays Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah before it is time for Isha. The Hanafi school holds that the prayer must be repeated because it violates the prescribed time and place for the combined prayer. However, there is an intra-school disagreement: Abu Yusuf considers the prayer valid but sinful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying Maghrib on the road to Muzdalifah before Isha time. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the prayer is fasid (invalid) and wajib to repeat before dawn.
Focus on the ruling of repetition, not the virtue.
2
Understand the time and place conditions
Maghrib on this night is restricted to the time of Isha and the place of Muzdalifah. Praying on the road violates these conditions.
The hadith 'الصلاة أمامك' supports this restriction.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that the prayer is valid but sinful. Note the practical difference: those following Abu Yusuf do not repeat; those following the majority do.
The text elaborates on the majority's reasoning.
4
Analyze the time limitation for repetition
Repetition is only obligatory before dawn. After dawn, the virtue of combining is lost, so no repetition is required.
The logical argument: repetition would be for the virtue (impossible) or the prayer itself (already done).
5
Synthesize the practical application
If a pilgrim prays Maghrib on the road before Isha, he must repeat it before dawn. If dawn passes, no repetition.
This ruling applies according to the majority view.

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on repeating Maghrib prayer if performed before reaching Muzdalifah. The text from al-Wiqayah states: 'he repeats Maghrib if he performed it on the road'. The commentator explains that this repetition is obligatory (wajib). The reason is that the performance of Maghrib on the night of Muzdalifah is restricted to the time of Isha and to the location of Muzdalifah. A hadith indicates that the Prophet told someone who said 'Prayer' on the road: 'Prayer is ahead of you', meaning wait until Muzdalifah. Similarly, if one prays Isha before arriving, it must be repeated.

Then the text extends the ruling: the same applies at 'Arafat for combining there. If one prays Maghrib before the time of Isha, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule it invalid and require repetition until dawn. The reason given is that the virtue of combining lasts until dawn. Once dawn breaks, the possibility of combining is lost, so the obligation to repeat falls away. The commentator provides logical reasoning: if repetition were required after dawn, it would either be for the virtue of combining (impossible as it has no substitute) or for the prayer itself (already performed in its own time). Hence, no repetition after dawn.

Then an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that the Maghrib is valid as performed in its own time, but the person is sinful for violating the sunna. However, the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the one requiring repetition before dawn. The text does not explicitly state which is mufta bihi, but the elaborateness of the reasoning for the first view suggests it is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
الإعادة (i'adah): Repeating a prayer that was performed invalidly or without proper conditions.
فضيلة الجمع (fadilat al-jam'): The virtue/merit of combining two prayers at Muzdalifah.

D) No repetition is needed.

Key Takeaway
Maghrib on the night of Muzdalifah must be combined with Isha at Muzdalifah; if prayed on the road before Isha, it must be repeated before dawn according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Fajr Prayer at Muzdalifah at Early Dawn
Ruling on Fajr at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for Fajr at Muzdalifah, explain why it is performed at early dawn (ghalas), and identify when the standing may be omitted.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, Fajr is prayed at early dawn, not bright daylight — following the Prophet's practice.

The Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah has a unique timing: it is performed at early dawn (ghalas) rather than delaying to brightness (isfar). This lesson examines the ruling, the evidence, and the significance of the subsequent standing and supplication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the text is ruling on: the Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah. Note that it is performed at early dawn (ghalas) and is followed by standing and supplication. The ruling level is sunna mu'akkada (emphasized sunna).
The text uses 'صلى' which indicates performance, and the commentator clarifies it is sunna.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The evidence cited is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and others. This is a naqli (textual) proof of mutawatir transmission (qat'i thubut) but the ruling itself is zanni al-dalalah because it indicates preference, not obligation.
The phrase 'ثبت عن رسول الله' indicates the hadith is authentic.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (aspect of evidence)
The hadith shows the Prophet performing Fajr at Muzdalifah at early dawn. This becomes the model (sunna) for pilgrims. The commentator emphasizes that delaying to isfar is not recommended (mustahabb) here, establishing the exception.
The Prophet's action (fi'l) is a source of sunna in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the time parameters and exceptions
The text specifies that the earliest time for the standing (wuquf) is dawn on the day of Nahr, and the latest is sunrise, similar to 'Arafat. However, if one misses the standing due to a valid excuse (e.g., crowding), there is no sin or compensation required.
This shows leniency for common hajj difficulties.

[4] قوله: ثم وقف؛ أوّل وقتِهِ طلوع الصبح الصادق من يوم النحر، وآخره كما في عرفة، لكن لو تركه بعذر كزحمة لا شيء عليه.

It is not recommended to delay until the sky is bright (isfar), contrary to the usual preference for Fajr. This practice is established from the Prophet (peace be upon him) in authentic hadith from al-Bukhari. After Fajr, the pilgrim stands at Muzdalifah (the area of the sacred monument) and engages in supplication until sunrise. The time for this standing begins at dawn of the day of Nahr and ends at sunrise, similar to the standing at 'Arafat. However, if one misses this standing due to a valid excuse like overcrowding, there is no sin or obligation.

Validity of Maghrib at Muzdalifah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the ruling and dispute on Maghrib prayer timing at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on praying Maghrib before Isha at Muzdalifah, and explain the reasoning behind the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Core Idea
A pre-Isha Maghrib at Muzdalifah is invalid and must be repeated before Fajr; after Fajr, no repetition is required because the virtue of combining is lost.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling of Hajj: the prayer of Maghrib at Muzdalifah. The Sunnah is to combine Maghrib and Isha. But what if someone prays Maghrib before the Isha time? The Hanafi masters differ on validity. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require repetition before dawn, while Abu Yusuf considers it valid but blameworthy. We will explore the reasoning behind this intra-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is praying Maghrib at Muzdalifah before the appointed time of Isha (i.e., before combining). The dispute is whether this prayer is valid (Abu Yusuf) or invalid and requiring repetition (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).
2
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
According to them, the prayer is not valid (la yajuz) and repetition (i'adah) is obligatory before dawn. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
Zahir al-Riwayah supports this view.
3
State the ruling of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that the prayer is valid and suffices, but the pilgrim is sinful (musi') for opposing the Sunnah. No repetition is required.
His view is based on the prayer being performed in its actual Maghrib time.
4
Explain the talil (reasoning) for the majority
The invalidity is due to missing the virtue of combining (fadilat al-jam‘). That virtue extends until dawn. If repetition is delayed after dawn, the opportunity for that virtue is lost. After Fajr, the obligation drops because repeating would either be for the virtue (impossible, as it has no equivalent) or for the prayer itself (unnecessary, as it was performed in its time).
This is an example of talil: reasoning based on the wisdom behind the ruling.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to the relied-upon position: if the pilgrim does not repeat before Fajr, no further action is needed. According to Abu Yusuf: no action ever, but the pilgrim is sinful.
The difference affects whether any qada' is required after Fajr.

Source Text

Or at Arafat as long as dawn has not appeared, no after it. He prayed Fajr in darkness, then stood and supplicated, or at Arafat as long as dawn has not appeared, no after it. For if he prayed Maghrib before the time of Isha, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, so repetition is obligatory as long as dawn has not appeared. The ruling of invalidity is because of attaining the virtue of combining (prayers), and this extends until dawn. When the possibility of combining is missed, the obligation of repetition falls, because: if repetition is obligatory, then either it is for repeating the virtue of combining, which is impossible, for there is no equal to it; or it is for repeating the prayer itself, but he performed it in its time, so how can its repetition be obligatory? [2] He said: 'Because...' etc.; its summary: if repetition of Maghrib which he prayed in its time after dawn were obligatory, then either it would be for repeating the virtue of combining, which is impossible, for repetition is for something that has an equivalent, and that virtue has no equivalent, so it cannot be performed; or it would be for repeating the prayer itself, which is unintelligible, for he performed it in its time, and repetition is only when one does not perform the prayer in its time.

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific scenario: a pilgrim at Muzdalifah who prays Maghrib before the time of Isha (i.e., before the appointed time for combining). According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, this prayer is invalid and must be repeated before dawn. However, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the prayer is valid but he is sinning by going against the Sunnah. The reasoning for the majority view hinges on the virtue of combining prayers (jam'): the pilgrim intended to attain the virtue of combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, which is a special dispensation. If he delays the repetition until after dawn, the opportunity for that virtue is lost, because the virtue of combining is time-specific and cannot be recovered. Therefore, after dawn, the obligation to repeat drops entirely—neither the virtue nor the prayer itself needs to be repeated, as the prayer was originally performed in its valid time. This is a nuanced intra-madhhab difference that students must understand for practical application.

Key Terms
فضيلة الجمع (fadīlat al-jam‘): The special virtue or merit of combining two prayers (Maghrib and Isha) at Muzdalifah.
الإعادة (al-i‘ādah): Repetition of a prayer due to its previous invalidity.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on Maghrib at Muzdalifah hinges on preserving the virtue of combining; after Fajr, no repetition is needed because the virtue is lost and the prayer itself was performed in its time.

The Wajib Standing at Muzdalifah and Sunnah Actions After Fajr
Describes the rulings and sunnah actions at Muzdalifah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah is wajib (not rukn) and identify the sunnah actions: early Fajr prayer, dhikr, and stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba from the valley floor, citing the prophetic proof.

Core Idea
Standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn; missing it requires a dam but does not invalidate hajj.

The moments after Fajr at Muzdalifah are packed with sunnah and wajib acts. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the legal weight of the standing at al-Mash'ar al-Haram, the timing of Fajr prayer, and the proper way to stone the Jamrat al-Aqaba. We'll walk through the prophetic practice and its Hanafi classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage explicitly states that the standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah is 'wajib, not a rukn'. Confirm this distinction: wajib means obligatory but omission requires a dam (sacrifice), while rukn would invalidate the hajj if missed.
This is a key Hanafi position; other schools differ.
2
Locate the dalil for each action
The text cites hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, and others for: praying Fajr in darkness (ghalas), standing at Mount Quzah with dhikr, departing before sunrise, and stoning from the bottom of the valley. Identify which hadith supports each action.
These are all from the Prophet's actual hajj.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the standing: the Prophet stood at Muzdalifah until very bright, then departed. This continuous action, combined with the command-like description, indicates wujub. For the Fajr prayer and stoning, the Prophet's consistent practice makes them sunnah mu'akkadah.
Hanafis use the principle that the Prophet's continuous practice (al-muwazabah) indicates wujub unless there is a contrary indicator.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage mentions that some scholars (other madhhabs) consider the standing at Muzdalifah a rukn. The Hanafis hold it as wajib. The footnote also records Abu Yusuf's view on Maghrib prayer at Muzdalifah, showing intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The practical difference: if missed, a Hanafi offers a dam; a Shafi'i would need to repeat the hajj.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Consider a pilgrim who, due to extreme crowding, cannot remain standing at Muzdalifah for more than a few minutes. According to the text, the minimum is even a moment ('wa law sa'ah'), so the obligation is fulfilled. If he misses it entirely due to a valid excuse (like being trapped in a vehicle), no penalty applies.
The text says: 'if he leaves it due to an excuse like crowding, there is nothing upon him.'

Then he departed before sunrise.
