(3) From Ibn Umar: He used to throw the first jamrah with seven pebbles, saying takbir after each, then advance until level, stand facing qiblah for a long time, supplicate raising his hands, then throw the middle jamrah, then take the left side, level, stand facing qiblah for a long time, supplicate raising his hands, then throw Jamrat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley, and not stand there, then leave, saying 'Thus I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) do.' In Sahih al-Bukhari (2:623) etc. And from Abd al-Rahman ibn Yazid (may Allah be pleased with him): Abdullah ibn Mas'ud threw Jamrat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles, saying takbir with each. It was said to him: Some people throw from above it. He said: Abdullah...
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage details the sunnah and wajib actions at Muzdalifah. The standing at Muzdalifah (al-Mash'ar al-Haram) is wajib, not a rukn, meaning it is obligatory but if missed, one must offer a dam (sacrifice). The Fajr prayer is to be performed early (ghalas) while it is still dark, as the Prophet did, and it is not recommended to delay it to isfar (brightness). After Fajr, the pilgrim stands at Mount Quzah (or near it) engaged in dhikr and du'a until it becomes very bright, then proceeds to Mina before sunrise. Upon reaching Mina, the first rite is to throw the Jamrat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley, throwing seven pebbles while saying takbir. Standing at the jamrah for du'a after this particular stoning is not done, contrary to the other jamarat. The commentary includes hadith proofs for these actions from Bukhari and Muslim. Additionally, there is a mention of the timing: the standing at Muzdalifah begins at dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and lasts until sunrise; if one misses it due to an excuse, there is no penalty. The text also repeats the Abu Yusuf view from the previous lesson, but here it is a footnote. The overall ruling emphasizes following the Prophet's practice precisely.

Key Terms
غلس (ghalas): The time after true dawn when darkness remains; early dawn.
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-ʿaqabah): The third and largest stoning pillar at Mina, located near Mecca.
وقوف بمزدلفة (wuqūf bi-muzdalifah): Being present at al-Mash'ar al-Haram (Muzdalifah) for any amount of time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Sunnah

D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Standing at Muzdalifah is a wajib act; performing Fajr in darkness, engaging in dhikr, and stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba from the valley floor are sunnah actions established by the Prophet's practice.

Standing at Muzdalifah and Stoning Jamarat al-Aqabah
Commentary on obligations and procedures at Muzdalifah and Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing at Muzdalifah (wajib vs rukn) and describe the procedure for stoning Jamarat al-Aqabah, including the number of pebbles, method (khadhf), takbir, cutting of talbiyah, and the ruling on sacrifice for the mufrid.

Core Idea
Standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, not a rukn; its omission requires a dam but does not invalidate Hajj.

In this lesson, we examine a key passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah that clarifies two crucial obligations at Muzdalifah and Mina. First, the standing at Muzdalifah is classified as wajib — a unique Hanafi category below fard — because its evidence comes from ahad hadith. Second, the stoning of Jamarat al-Aqabah must be performed with seven separate pebbles thrown in the khadhf manner, while reciting takbir, and the talbiyah is cut at the first stone. The passage also distinguishes the sacrifice obligations for different types of Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text opens by stating that standing at Muzdalifah (al-wuquf bi Muzdalifah) is wajib, not a rukn. Note the distinction: in Hanafi usul, a rukn invalidates the act if omitted, while a wajib requires compensation but does not nullify.
This classification is unique to the Hanafi school; Shafi'is consider it a rukn.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites evidence from the 'Sahih' collections (Bukhari and Muslim) showing the Prophet's practice of standing at Muzdalifah before dawn and then departing to Mina. The hadith is ahad (single-chain), hence the hukm is wajib, not fard.
The hadith references are not quoted verbatim but summarised.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent action — stopping at Muzdalifah, leaving before sunrise — combined with the Companions' following, indicates a binding practice. In Hanafi usul, such continuous practice from ahad hadith establishes wujub.
The passage does not elaborate the usul reasoning but implies it.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school classifies standing at Muzdalifah as a rukn, meaning omission invalidates Hajj. The Hanafi position rests on the lower epistemological weight (zanni al-thubut) of the ahad hadith.
This difference leads to different practical consequences for the pilgrim.
5
Apply the stoning procedure
The passage details the stoning: seven separate pebbles thrown with the fingertips (khadhf), each throw accompanied by takbir, and the talbiyah is cut at the first stone. It also mentions that if all pebbles are thrown at once, it counts as only one.
The location must be from the bottom of the valley (batin al-wadi), but other locations are valid (ja'iz).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من كتاب الحج باب الإحرام:
وهو واجب لا ركن، وإذا أسفر أتى بمنى، ورَمَى جَمرة العقبة من بطن الوادي
[١] قوله : وهو ؛ أي الوقوف بمزدلفة ولو ساعة.
[٢] قوله : أتى بمنى ؛ ويسرع في مشيه إذا بلغ وادي محسر بين مزدلفة ومنى.
[٣] قوله : جمرة العقبة ; هو ثالث الجمرات التي بمنى، وهو على طرف منى من جهة مكة، ولا يرمي في ذلك اليوم إلا تلك الجمرة، وفي الأيام الباقية ترمى في الجمرات الثلاث.
[٤] قوله : من بطن ؛ أي أسفل الوادي الذي هناك، كذا ثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عند البخاري، ولو رمى من موضع آخر جاز.
حتى أسفر جداً، وإذا أسفر جداً أفاض من هناك إلى منى قبل طلوع الشمس، ثبت ذلك عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في «الصحاح».

[١] قوله : سبعاً ; أي سبع رميات بسبع حصيات، فلو رماها دفعة واحدة كان عن واحدة. كذا في «النهر».

[٣] قوله : وكبر بكل منها ; أي يقول : الله أكبر مع كل رمي.
[٤] قوله : بأولها ; لما ثبت أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يزل يلبي حتى رمى جمرة العقبة، أخرجه الستة.
[٥] قوله : إن شاء ; وإنما قال هذا لأنّ الكلام في المفرد، ولا يجب عليه الدم، بخلاف القارن والمتمتع؛ فإنّه يجب عليهما الدم، وأما الأضحية فإن كان مسافراً لا يجب.
From the Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram: And it (standing at Muzdalifah) is wajib, not a rukn. And when it becomes bright, he comes to Mina, and stoned Jamarat al-Aqabah from the bottom of the valley. [1] He said: 'And it' meaning standing at Muzdalifah even for a moment. [2] He said: 'He comes to Mina' and he hurries in his walking when he reaches Wadi Muhassir between Muzdalifah and Mina. [3] He said: 'Jamarat al-Aqabah' — with two fatha — is the third of the jamarat in Mina, and it is at the edge of Mina on the side of Mecca, and he does not stone on that day except that jamarah, and on the remaining days he stones all three jamarat. [4] He said: 'From the bottom' meaning the lower part of the valley there; thus it is established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in al-Bukhari, and if he stones from another place it is permissible. Until it is very bright, and when it is very bright he departs from there to Mina before sunrise; that is established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in the 'Sahih' collections. Seven (stones) by khadhf, and he says takbir with each, and he cuts his talbiyah at the first of them, then he sacrifices if he wishes. [1] He said: 'Seven' meaning seven throws with seven pebbles; if he throws them all at once it counts as one. Thus in 'al-Nahr'. [2] He said: 'Khadhf' is a verbal noun to specify the type, meaning throwing khadhf, which is throwing with the tips of the fingers; and it has been reported: 'Upon you is the pebbles of khadhf, lest some of you hurt others,' reported by al-Tabarani, and it indicates that the pebbles should be small. [3] He said: 'And he says takbir with each' meaning he says Allahu Akbar with each throw. [4] He said: 'At the first of them' because it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) continued saying talbiyah until he stoned Jamarat al-Aqabah, reported by the six (hadith scholars). [5] He said: 'If he wishes' and he only said this because the discussion is about the individual (mufrid), and blood sacrifice is not obligatory upon him, unlike the qarin and mutamatti, for upon them blood sacrifice is obligatory; as for the udhiyah, if he is traveling it is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on key rulings regarding actions at Muzdalifah and Mina. The commentator begins by stating that standing at Muzdalifah (al-wuquf bi Muzdalifah) is wajib — an obligatory act — but not a rukn (pillar). In the Hanafi school, a rukn is essential to the validity of Hajj; omission of a rukn invalidates the Hajj. A wajib, on the other hand, requires compensation (dam) if omitted but does not invalidate. The evidence for this being wajib, not rukn, is that it is established by ahad hadith, not by definitive proof. The commentator then explains that when it becomes very bright (asfar jiddan), the pilgrim proceeds to Mina and must stone Jamarat al-Aqabah from the bottom of the valley (batin al-wadi). This location is specifically where the Prophet (peace be upon him) stoned, as recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari. However, stoning from another place is permissible (ja'iz), meaning it is valid but perhaps not optimal. The stoning itself consists of seven pebbles thrown in the manner of khadhf — throwing with the tips of the fingers using small pebbles. Each throw is accompanied by saying 'Allahu Akbar'. The talbiyah is cut at the first stone, based on the established practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who continued talbiyah until he stoned Jamarat al-Aqabah. Finally, the text mentions that the mufrid (individual performing Hajj without qiran or tamattu') may sacrifice if he wishes; no blood sacrifice is obligatory upon him. This contrasts with the qarin and mutamatti, for whom a sacrifice (dam) is wajib. The passage thus provides a clear sequence and detailed rulings from the Hanafi perspective.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act that is not a pillar; omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate Hajj.
ركن (rukn): An essential pillar of Hajj; omission invalidates the Hajj.
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-‘aqabah): The largest stone pillar at Mina, stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
خذف (khadhf): A method of throwing small pebbles with the tips of the fingers, using the thumb and index finger.
تلبيته (talbiyah): The invocation 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited during Hajj; cut at the first stone of Jamarat al-Aqabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of standing at Muzdalifah?
A) It is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj, without which Hajj is invalid.
B) It is wajib; omission requires a sacrifice but Hajj remains valid.
C) It is sunnah; if omitted, no compensation is needed.
D) It is fard; omission invalidates Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Standing at Muzdalifah is wajib in the Hanafi school; its omission requires a sacrifice but does not invalidate Hajj. The stoning of Jamarat al-Aqabah must be done with seven separate small pebbles thrown with the fingertips, accompanied by takbir, and the talbiyah is cut at the first stone.

Rulings on Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah and Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Describes the sequence after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of Hajj rituals after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah and distinguish the rulings (fard, wajib, sunnah, makruh) for each act with their proofs.

Core Idea
After stoning, shaving/trimming and Tawaf al-Ziyarah are required; women become halal only after Tawaf, not after shaving.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah guides us through the precise sequence a pilgrim must follow after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah. It clarifies what is obligatory, what is recommended, and the critical distinction that the prohibition of women is lifted only upon completing Tawaf al-Ziyarah. By studying this text, you will learn not only the order of actions but also the underlying proofs from hadith and the nuances of delaying tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence after stoning
List the actions in order: stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah (7 throws with khadhf), cutting talbiyah, optional slaughter, shaving/trimming, then Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
Note that stoning is wajib, shaving is sunnah muakkadah, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah is fard.
2
Distinguish the hukm levels
For each act, identify its legal classification: fard (Tawaf al-Ziyarah), wajib (stoning), sunnah muakkadah (shaving), makruh tahrimi (delaying tawaf without excuse).
The distinction between fard and wajib is important in Hanafi usul: fard is proven by qat'i dalil, wajib by zanni dalil.
3
Locate the dalil for key rulings
Find the hadith evidence cited: for khadhf (Tabarani), for cutting talbiyah (six books), for delay excuse (Bukhari). Understand how each proof supports the ruling.
The proof for khadhf also indicates the pebbles should be small.
4
Analyze the conditions for Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Identify the time (days of Nahr, best on 10th), the requirement of seven circuits without raml (if sa'y done), and the combination with sa'y if not done earlier.
Raml is omitted because this tawaf is not immediately followed by sa'y.
5
Handle the exception for delay
Determine that delaying Tawaf beyond the days of Nahr is makruh tahrimi unless there is an excuse (e.g., menstruation). The text uses the hadith of the Prophet's wife as evidence.
This ruling is specific to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may view it differently.

سَبْعاً خَذفاً ، وكبر بكل منها ، وقطع تلبيته بأولها ، ثُمَّ ذَبَحَ إن شاء. قوله : سبعاً ؛ أي سبع رميات بسبع حصيات ، فلو رماها دفعة واحدة كان عن واحدة. كذا في «النهر». قوله : خذفاً؛ هو مفعول مطلق؛ لبيان النوع؛ أي رمي حذف وهو الرمي برؤوس الأصابع، وقد ورد: «عليكم بحصى الخذف لا يؤذي بعضكم بعضاً»، أخرجه الطبراني، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه ينبغي أن تكون الحصيات صغاراً. قوله : وكبر بكل منها؛ أي يقول: الله أكبر مع كل رمي. قوله: بأولها؛ لما ثبت أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يزل يلبي حتى رمى جمرة العقبة، أخرجه الستة. قوله: إن شاء؛ وإنما قال هذا؛ لأنّ الكلام في المفرد، ولا يجب عليه الدم، بخلاف القارن والمتمتع؛ فإنّه يجب عليهما الدم، وأما الأضحية فإن كان مسافراً لا يجب. ثُمَّ قَرَ ، وحلقه أفضل، وحلّ له كل شيء إلا النِّساء ، ثُمَّ طاف للزيارة يوماً من أيام النحر سبعة بلا رَمْلٍ وسعي إن كان سعى قبل، وإلا فمعها ، وأَوَّلُ وقته بعد طلوع فجر يوم النحر ، وهو فيه أفضل ، وحلَّ له النِّساء، وإن آخره عنها كُره قصر ، وحلقه أفضل ، وحل له كل شيء إلا النِّساء. قوله : قصر ; من التقصير; أي أخذ من شعره بقدر أنملة. قوله : إلا النساء; أي جماعهن ودواعيه. قوله : بلا رمل ; لأنه مخصوص بطواف يكون بعده سعي. قوله : إن كان سعى قبل ; أي في طواف القدوم، قال رحمة الله السندي : في «المنسك الكبير»: جواز تقديم السعي لمن عليه طواف القدوم متفق عليه، وأما أفضليته ففيه خلاف، وأما جوازه لمن أحرم من مكة ، وليس عليه طواف القدوم، فقد اختاره غير واحدٍ من المشايخ. قوله : أخره ; أي أخر الطواف عن أيام النحر، بأن طاف في اليوم الرابع أو بعده. قوله : كره ; أي تحريماً ; إذا كان بغير عذر ، وإلا فلا ، كما إذا طهرت المرأة من الحيض بعد تلك الأيام، يدلّ عليه أن بعض أزواج النبي حاضت في حجة الوداع ، فقال: «لعلها حابستنا»; أي لطواف الزيارة، أخرجه البخاري.
Seven (throws) by throwing with the fingertips, and say takbeer with each, and cut off his talbiyah with the first. Then he may slaughter if he wishes. (Commentary: Seven means seven throws with seven pebbles; if he throws them all at once it counts as one. Khadhf is an absolute object to specify type: it means throwing the way of khadhf, which is throwing with the tips of the fingers. The hadith 'Upon you are the pebbles of khadhf, they do not hurt one another' was reported by al-Tabarani, indicating that the pebbles should be small. 'Say takbeer with each' means: say 'Allahu Akbar' with each throw. 'Cut off his talbiyah with the first' because it is established that the Prophet ﷺ continued to say talbiyah until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqabah, reported by the six. 'If he wishes' because the discussion is about the mufrid; blood sacrifice is not obligatory for him, unlike the qarin and mutamatti' for whom blood sacrifice is obligatory. As for the udhiyah, if he is a traveler it is not obligatory.) Then he trims, and shaving is better, and everything becomes permissible for him except women. Then he performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah on a day of the days of Nahr, seven circuits without raml, and sa'y if he performed sa'y before, otherwise with it. Its earliest time is after dawn on the day of Nahr, and it is best on that day. Then women become permissible for him. And if he delays it beyond them (the days of Nahr), it is disliked. Trimming and shaving are better, and everything becomes permissible for him except women. (Commentary: 'Trimming' means taking from his hair about a fingertip's length. 'Except women' means intercourse and what leads to it. 'Without raml' because raml is specific to a tawaf after which there is sa'y. 'If he performed sa'y before' means in Tawaf al-Qudum; Rahmatullah al-Sindi said in al-Mansak al-Kabir: The permissibility of advancing sa'y for one who has Tawaf al-Qudum is agreed upon, but there is disagreement on its superiority. As for its permissibility for one who assumed ihram from Makkah and who does not have Tawaf al-Qudum, more than one of the mashayikh have chosen it. 'If he delays it' means he delays the tawaf beyond the days of Nahr by performing it on the fourth day or after. 'It is disliked' means tahriman if without excuse, otherwise not, such as when a woman becomes pure from menstruation after those days. This is supported by the fact that one of the Prophet's wives menstruated during the Farewell Hajj and he said 'Perhaps she will detain us', meaning for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, reported by al-Bukhari.)
Source pages p. 584

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on the matn of al-Wiqayah, explaining the sequence of actions after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah and the rulings of Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The author first discusses the stoning itself: it must be seven separate throws using small pebbles thrown with the fingertips (khadhf), each accompanied by 'Allahu Akbar'. The talbiyah is cut after the first throw, based on the hadith that the Prophet continued talbiyah until stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah. The option to sacrifice (dhabh) applies only to the mufrid (who performs Hajj only); for the qarin and mutamatti', sacrifice is obligatory. As for udhiyah (sacrifice on behalf of the household), it is not obligatory for a traveler. Then the pilgrim trims his hair (qasr) or shaves (halaq), with shaving being better due to the verse 'with shaven heads and trimmed' (48:27). After this, everything becomes permissible except women (i.e., sexual relations and foreplay). The next major ritual is Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah), which is a fard of Hajj. It is performed on the days of Nahr (10th to 13th of Dhul Hijjah), preferably on the day of Nahr itself (10th). The earliest time is after fajr of the 10th. This tawaf is done without raml (brisk walking) because raml is only performed in a tawaf that is followed by sa'y; if sa'y was already performed after Tawaf al-Qudum, then it is not repeated; otherwise, sa'y is included with this tawaf. The text also notes that delaying this tawaf beyond the days of Nahr is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) if there is no excuse, such as menstruation. Once Tawaf al-Ziyarah is completed, women become permissible. The passage thus provides the detailed sequence and conditions for post-stoning actions, clarifying the distinction between obligatory, recommended, and optional acts.

Key Terms
خذف (khadhf): Throwing pebbles with the tips of the fingers, not with cupped hand.
قصر (qasr): Trimming the hair of the head by about a fingertip's length.
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba performed on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) or during the days of Tashreeq.
رمل (raml): Brisk walking with short strides and moving the shoulders in the first three circuits of tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a male pilgrim become fully halal for women after the Hajj rituals according to the Hanafi school?
A) After stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah
B) After shaving or trimming the hair
C) After completing Tawaf al-Ziyarah
D) After performing sa'y

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of women (sexual relations) in Hajj is lifted solely by Tawaf al-Ziyarah, not by stoning or shaving alone.

Rulings on Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Delay Penalty
Rulings on Tawaf al-Ziyarah and its delay penalty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, identify the conditions for its validity, and apply the consequences of delay including the dam penalty.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is wajib; delaying without excuse is makruh tahriman and requires dam.

In the Hajj rites, after shaving or cutting hair, the pilgrim performs the obligatory circumambulation known as Tawaf al-Ziyarah. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains its timing, performance, and the effect of delay. We will examine the legal rulings and the proofs from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a wajib act of Hajj. Note that it is performed after shaving or cutting hair.
Wajib means obligatory; omission requires compensation (dam), not invalidation of Hajj.
2
List conditions and features of the Tawaf
It consists of seven circuits without Raml (brisk walking). Its earliest time is after dawn on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), and performing it on that day is better. If Sa'ee was not done earlier, it must be done after this Tawaf.
Raml is specific to Tawaf that precedes Sa'ee. This Tawaf may be combined with Sa'ee if needed.
3
Identify the consequence of delaying the Tawaf
If the pilgrim delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the days of Nahr (10th-12th) without a valid excuse, it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahriman) and a dam (slaughter of a sheep) becomes obligatory.
If there is an excuse (e.g., menstruation), there is no dislike or penalty.
4
Locate the proofs from the Sunnah
The ruling on delay is based on the hadith of Safiyyah (Bukhari) where the Prophet said 'Perhaps she will detain us,' indicating dislike. The obligation of dam is from the hadith of Ibn Abbas (Muwatta): 'Whoever forgets any of his rituals or leaves it, let him spill blood.'
These ahadith have zanni thubut and dalala, hence the ruling is makruh tahriman, not haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ قَرَ ، وحلقه أفضل، وحلّ له كل شيء إلا النِّساء ، ثُمَّ طاف للزيارة يوماً من أيام النحر سبعة بلا رَمْلٍ وسعي إن كان سعى قبل، وإلا فمعها ، وأَوَّلُ وقته بعد طلوع فجر يوم النحر ، وهو فيه أفضل ، وحلَّ له النِّساء، وإن آخره عنها كُره (1) قوله : قصر؛ من التقصير؛ أي أخذ من شعره بقدر أنملة. (2) قوله : إلا النساء؛ أي جماعهن ودواعيه. (3) قوله : بلا رمل؛ لأنه مخصوص بطواف يكون بعده سعي. (4) قوله : إن كان سعى قبل؛ أي في طواف القدوم، قال رحمة الله السندي : في «المنسك الكبير»: جواز تقديم السعي لمن عليه طواف القدوم متفق عليه، وأما أفضليته ففيه خلاف، وأما جوازه لمن أحرم من مكة، وليس عليه طواف القدوم، فقد اختاره غير واحدٍ من المشايخ. (5) قوله : أخره؛ أي أخر الطواف عن أيام النحر، بأن طاف في اليوم الرابع أو بعده. (6) قوله : كره؛ أي تحريماً؛ إذا كان بغير عذر، وإلا فلا، كما إذا طهرت المرأة من الحيض بعد تلك الأيام، يدلّ عليه أن بعض أزواج النبي حاضت في حجة الوداع، فقال: «لعلها حابستنا )؛ أي لطواف الزيارة، أخرجه البخاري. ووجب دم (1) قوله : ووجب دم؛ أي جبراً لهذا النقصان بترك الواجب، وكلّ ما هو واجب في الحج يجب بتركه دم؛ أي ذبح حيوان، وأدناه شاة؛ لقول ابن عباس : «مَن نسي شيئاً من نسكه أو تركه فليهرق دما»، أخرجه مالك في «الموطأ».
Then he shortens (hair), and shaving is better, and everything becomes permissible for him except women. Then he performs the Tawaf of Visitation on a day of the days of Nahr, seven circuits without Raml, and Sa'ee if he had performed Sa'ee before, otherwise with it. Its earliest time is after dawn of the day of Nahr, and it is better on it. And women become permissible for him. And if he delays it beyond them (the days of Nahr), it is disliked. Commentary: [1] His saying: 'shortened' means taking from his hair by the length of a fingertip. [2] His saying: 'except women' means intercourse and its causes. [3] His saying: 'without Raml' because it is specific to a Tawaf after which there is Sa'ee. [4] His saying: 'if he had performed Sa'ee before' i.e., in the Tawaf of Arrival. Rahmat Allah al-Sindi said in al-Mansak al-Kabir: The permissibility of advancing Sa'ee for one upon whom there is Tawaf of Arrival is agreed upon. As for its superiority, there is a difference. As for its permissibility for one who entered ihram from Makkah and has no Tawaf of Arrival, it has been chosen by more than one of the mashayikh. [5] His saying: 'delays it' means he delays the Tawaf from the days of Nahr, such that he performs it on the fourth day or after it. [6] His saying: 'it is disliked' i.e., prohibitively disliked; if without an excuse, otherwise not, as when a woman becomes pure from menstruation after those days. This is indicated by that one of the wives of the Prophet (PBUH) menstruated during the Farewell Hajj, and he said: 'Perhaps she will detain us?' i.e., from Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Reported by Bukhari. And a dam becomes obligatory. Commentary: [1] His saying: 'and a dam becomes obligatory' i.e., as compensation for this deficiency due to leaving a wajib. Everything that is wajib in Hajj requires a dam if left, i.e., slaughtering an animal, the minimum of which is a sheep, due to the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'Whoever forgets any of his rituals or leaves it, let him spill blood.' Recorded by Malik in al-Muwatta.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof covering the rites immediately after shaving or cutting hair during Hajj. The author states that after shortening or shaving (with shaving being better), all prohibitions of ihram are lifted except for sexual relations with women. Then the pilgrim performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah (the obligatory circumambulation) on any day of the days of Nahr (10th, 11th, 12th of Dhul Hijjah). This Tawaf is seven circuits without Raml (rapid walking with shoulders bared) because Raml is exclusive to the Tawaf that precedes Sa'ee. If the pilgrim already performed Sa'ee after Tawaf al-Qudum (arrival Tawaf), he does not repeat Sa'ee now; otherwise, he performs Sa'ee after this Tawaf. The earliest time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah is after dawn on the 10th, and performing it on the 10th is better. After this Tawaf, women become permissible. If a person delays this Tawaf beyond the days of Nahr (i.e., to the 13th or later) without a valid excuse like menstruation, it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahriman) and a dam (slaughter of a sheep) becomes obligatory as compensation. The proof for the dislike is the hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) expressed concern about Safiyyah menstruating, indicating that delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah is disliked. The proof for the dam is the hadith of Ibn Abbas that any omission requires spilling blood. The commentary clarifies that if there is an excuse, like a woman being pure from menses only after the days, then no dislike or penalty applies.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba performed on the day of Nahr or the following days of Tashreeq, after shaving/cutting hair.
رمل (Raml): Walking briskly with the outer part of the right shoulder bared; specific to the Tawaf that precedes Sa'ee.
دم (Dam): A penalty requiring slaughter of a sheep (or similar) for omitting a wajib act in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah until after the days of Nahr due to menstruation, what is the ruling?
A) It is haram and requires a dam.
B) It is permissible and no penalty.
C) It is makruh tahriman with no penalty.
D) It is invalid and requires repeating Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a wajib performed without raml; delaying it without excuse incurs a dam but does not invalidate Hajj.

Stoning the Three Jamarat on 11th Dhul Hijjah
Rulings on stoning the three Jamarat after Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on stoning the Jamarat on the 11th of Dhul Hijjah, identify the conditions and sunan, and explain the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Stoning the Jamarat after Zawal is wajib; the order and supplication after the first two are sunnah.

After performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah, the pilgrim returns to Mina and spends the days of Tashreeq there. This lesson covers the stoning of the three Jamarat on the second day (11th Dhul Hijjah), detailing the required order, the preferred time, and the sunnah acts based on the practice of the Prophet (PBUH).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that stoning the three Jamarat on the 11th and 12th of Dhul Hijjah is a wajib act of Hajj. Its omission requires a dam (sacrificial animal).
The passage focuses on the 11th, but the same ruling applies to the 12th.
2
Determine the conditions and sunnah acts
List the conditions (intention, after Zawal, with pebbles, seven per Jamrah) and the sunnah acts (Takbir with each pebble, order, and standing after the first two).
The order is: small, middle, then al-Aqaba.
3
Locate the dalil
The practice of standing after the first two Jamarat is proven by a hadith narrated by Abu Dawood and others from the Prophet (PBUH).
This is a sunnah-based proof; the ruling of wajib comes from other evidence.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith describes the Prophet's action of stopping and supplicating after the first two, establishing it as a recommended practice (sunnah).
The passage uses this to show the source of the sunnah.
5
Note the consequence of omission
Leaving a wajib act in Hajj requires a dam. The text quotes Ibn Abbas: 'Whoever forgets any of his rituals or leaves it, let him spill blood.'
This underscores the importance of performing the stoning correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أتى منى ، وبعد زوال ثاني يوم النحر رمي الجمار الثلاث، يبدأ بما يلي المسجد ثم بما يليه، ثم بالعقبة سبعاً سبعاً، وكبر لكل، ووقف بعد رمي بعدَهُ رمى فقط [1] قوله : ثم; أي بعدما طاف طواف الزيارة، يرجع إلى منى، ويقيم بها ثلاثة أيام، يوم النحر ويومين بعده، وإن شاء أقام في الرابع أيضاً وهو السنة. [2] قوله : ثم مما يليه; أي ما يلي الجمرة التي تلي المسجد، وهي الوسطى، وجمرة العقبة يقال لها: الأولى والكبرى. [3] قوله : ووقف; هذا مروي عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره. (1) قوله : ووجب دم; أي جبراً لهذا النقصان بترك الواجب، وكلّ ما هو واجب في الحج يجب بتركه دم; أي ذبح حيوان، وأدناه شاة; لقول ابن عباس : «مَن نسي شيئاً من نسكه أو تركه فليهرق دما»، أخرجه مالك في «الموطأ».
Then he came to Mina, and after the zawal (declination) of the second day of Nahr, he stoned the three Jamarat, starting with the one closest to the mosque, then the one next to it, then the Jamrat al-Aqaba, seven each, and he said Takbir with each, and he stopped after the first and second stoning, but not after the third. Commentary: [1] His saying: 'then' i.e., after he performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah, he returns to Mina and stays there three days: the day of Nahr and two days after, and if he wishes, he stays a fourth as well, which is the sunnah. [2] His saying: 'then the one next to it' i.e., the one next to the Jamrah that is next to the mosque, which is the middle, and the Jamrat al-Aqaba is called the first and the greatest. [3] His saying: 'and he stopped' is narrated from the Messenger of Allah (PBUH), recorded by Abu Dawood and others. (1) His saying: 'and a dam is obligatory' i.e., as compensation for this deficiency due to leaving a wajib, and everything that is wajib in Hajj, if left, requires a dam; i.e., slaughtering an animal, the minimum of which is a sheep; due to the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'Whoever forgets any of his rituals or leaves it, let him spill blood.' Recorded by Malik in al-Muwatta.
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage describes the stoning of the Jamarat after Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The pilgrim returns to Mina and on the second day of Nahr (11th Dhul Hijjah) after Zawal (when the sun declines from its zenith), he stones the three Jamarat in order: first the small Jamrah (al-Ula) which is closest to Masjid al-Khayf, then the middle Jamrah (al-Wusta), then the large Jamrah (al-Aqaba). Each is stoned with seven pebbles individually, and with each pebble he says Takbir (Allahu Akbar). After stoning the first and second Jamrah, he stops, faces the Qibla, raises his hands, and makes long supplication. He does not stop after stoning the Jamrat al-Aqaba. The commentary notes that this practice is from the Prophet (PBUH) as recorded by Abu Dawood and others. The footnote about the dam is a continuation from the previous lesson, but it is placed here; it reinforces that leaving any wajib act in Hajj requires a dam. The staying in Mina is three days (10th, 11th, 12th) with an optional fourth (13th) which is sunnah.

Key Terms
الجمرات (al-Jamarat): The three stone pillars at Mina that are stoned on the days of Tashreeq: al-Ula (small), al-Wusta (middle), and al-Aqaba (large).
زوال (Zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith and begins to decline; the time for Zuhr prayer begins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Start with the small, then middle, then al-Aqaba.
C) Start with the middle, then small, then al-Aqaba.
D) Any order is acceptable.

Key Takeaway
Stoning the three Jamarat in order after Zawal on 11th and 12th is wajib; standing and supplicating after the first two is sunnah.

Rulings on the Days of Tashreeq and the Farewell Tawaf
Expansion commentary on Hajj rituals in Mina and return

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on nafar (departure from Mina), the timing of ramy on the 13th, and the Sunnah of staying at al-Muhassab and performing Tawaf as-Sadr.

Core Idea
Leaving Mina before dawn on the 13th is permissible; ramy before zawal is valid but disliked; staying at Muhassab and Tawaf as-Sadr are Sunnah.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya' expands on the matn regarding the final days of Hajj in Mina and the return to Mecca. The commentator explains the rulings for each action, from the permissibility of nafar to the disliked nature of sending luggage ahead, and the recommended practices of staying at al-Muhassab and performing Tawaf as-Sadr without raml.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions described
List the key actions: ramy, supplication, nafar (departure), sending baggage, staying at Muhassab, Tawaf as-Sadr.
Each action has a distinct ruling (mubah, makruh, sunnah, etc.).
2
Determine the ruling for each action
From the commentary, extract the hukm level: nafar before dawn on the 13th is mubah; ramy before zawal is makruh tanzihi; staying at Muhassab is sunnah kifayah; sending luggage is makruh; Tawaf as-Sadr is performed without raml.
The matn itself states some rulings; the commentary adds nuance.
3
Locate the dalil for nafar
The commentary cites Quran 2:203 to justify permissibility of leaving before dawn. Understand how the verse is applied.
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala.
4
Analyze the sharh structure
Notice how the commentator expands each phrase of the matn, providing justification, hadith references, and practical details.
This is an expansion_probe; the commentator builds on the base text.
5
Note the ikhtilaf on Muhassab
The commentator states staying at Muhassab is sunnah kifayah. Other schools consider it mustahab. Understand the difference.
The thamarah al-khilaf is minor but highlights differing methods.

ولو قَدَّمَ ثَقَلَهُ إلى مكة، وأقام بمنى للرمي كُرِه وإِذا نَفَرَ إلى مكة ، نَزَلَ بِالْمُحَصَّب ، ثم طاف للصدر سبعة أشواط بَلا رَمْل وسعي الأوليان مما يلي مسجدَ الخَيْف ، ثُمَّ ما يليه.

And he supplicated, then he did the same on the following day (the 12th), then similarly after that if he stayed (the 13th), and it is more beloved. And if he performs the ramy on that day (the 4th day) before zawal, it is permissible. And he may leave (nafar) before dawn of the fourth day, not after it. And ramy while riding is permissible, and in the first two (ramy of the 11th and 12th) walking is more beloved, not the last one (the 13th). [Commentary] [1] His saying: 'and he supplicated' meaning with praise, remembrance, and salawat upon the Prophet. [2] His saying: 'then he did the same on the following day' meaning he did on the third day of Nahr (12th Dhul Hijjah) as he did before of stoning the three jamarat, and it is the first day of nafar; if he leaves on that day to Mecca his Hajj is complete, and if he stays for the last day of Tashreeq (13th) he does likewise. [3] His saying: 'more beloved' meaning staying on the 13th day is better following the Prophet. [4] His saying: 'permissible' meaning valid with makruh tanzihi, for the time of ramy on that day is from fajr to sunset, and the night after it is not included, unlike the previous days, but before zawal is disliked time, after zawal is Sunnah. [5] His saying: 'and he may leave' meaning it is permissible for him to return from Mina to Mecca before dawn, i.e., true dawn of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah, due to His saying: 'And whoever hastens in two days, there is no sin upon him' (Quran 2:203). If dawn breaks while he is in Mina, he may not return unless he performs the ramy because he has caught the time of obligation. [6] His saying: 'more beloved not the last one' they explained that it is mustahab to stop for supplication after the first ramy for his need, and it is mustahab to seek forgiveness for himself, his parents, his siblings, his relatives, and believing men and women. And if he sends his heavy baggage to Mecca and stays in Mina for the ramy, it is disliked. And when he leaves (nafar) to Mecca, he stays at al-Muhassab, then performs Tawaf as-Sadr (the farewell tawaf) seven circuits without raml (fast walking) and sa'y, and the first two (circuits) are by the side of Masjid al-Khayf, then what follows it. [1] His saying: 'his heavy baggage' meaning his belongings and servants. [2] His saying: 'disliked' because it causes preoccupation and resemblance to people of luxury, and contradicts humility; therefore Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'Whoever sends his baggage from Mina on the night of nafar, there is no Hajj for him.' [3] His saying: 'by al-Muhassab' is a valley between Mecca and Mina near al-Mualla cemetery of Mecca, also called al-Abtah; staying there is Sunnah on sufficiency. Al-Qari said: it is established in the authentic hadiths that the Prophet (peace be upon him) left Mina on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah and stayed at al-Muhassab, prayed Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha there, slept a little, then entered Mecca at night and performed Tawaf al-Wada'. [4] His saying: 'then' meaning when he intends to travel from Mecca.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn regarding the rituals of the Days of Tashreeq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) and the final acts upon returning to Mecca. The commentator explains each phrase of the matn. First, the order of actions in Mina: after the ramy on the 10th (Yawm an-Nahr), on the 11th the pilgrim supplicates, on the 12th repeats the same (ramy of three jamarat), and if staying on the 13th, again. Staying the 13th is more beloved (mustahab). Performing ramy on the 13th before zawal (midday) is valid but makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked); the preferred time is after zawal. The pilgrim may leave (nafar) Mina on the 12th or 13th; the nafar before dawn of the 13th is permissible based on Quran 2:203; if dawn rises while still in Mina, he must perform ramy of the 13th. Ramy while riding is permissible, but walking is more beloved for the first two days (11th and 12th) due to humility; for the last (13th), riding is acceptable as one needs to depart quickly. Then, the matn states that sending heavy luggage ahead to Mecca while staying in Mina for ramy is disliked (makruh) as it shows luxury; the commentator cites a hadith of Umar. Upon leaving Mina, the Sunnah is to stay at al-Muhassab (a valley near Mecca), then perform Tawaf as-Sadr (farewell tawaf) without raml (brisk walking) and without sa'y (since sa'y has already been done). The first two circuits of this tawaf should be near Masjid al-Khayf, as a specific Sunnah.

Key Terms
النفر (an-nafar): The departure of the pilgrim from Mina to Mecca after completing the stoning rituals.
المحصب (al-muhassab): A valley between Mecca and Mina where the Prophet stayed after leaving Mina; also called al-Abtah.
طواف الصدر (tawaf as-sadr): The farewell circumambulation performed after returning from Mina before leaving Mecca; also called tawaf al-wada'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory to stay until after dawn.
B) It is permissible and he has fulfilled the nafar.
C) It is forbidden because he must stone the jamarat that day.
D) It is makruh tahrimi and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
The final days of Hajj involve precise rulings; knowing the times and hierarchies of actions ensures valid and complete worship.

Rulings on Departure from Mina and Farewell Tawaf
Describes actions after returning from Mina to Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for actions after leaving Mina, identify the status of farewell tawaf as wajib, and list the recommended acts in order.

Core Idea
Farewell tawaf is wajib for non-Meccans; omission requires a dam, and its performance includes specific etiquettes.

After completing the days of Mina, the pilgrim returns to Mecca for the farewell tawaf. This lesson outlines the sequence of actions—from descent at al-Muhassab to the heartfelt exit from the Masjid—and clarifies the legal weight of each act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
Note that sending baggage ahead while staying in Mina for stoning is makruh (disliked).
This shows a preference for humility and avoiding unnecessary occupation.
2
Recognize the sunnah of al-Muhassab
When departing to Mecca, descending at al-Muhassab is a sunnah practice of the Prophet.
3
State the ruling of farewell tawaf
The farewell tawaf is wajib for all pilgrims except the people of Mecca (residents). It is performed without ramal and sa'y.
The level wajib implies obligation from a zanni dalil; omission requires a dam.
4
Enumerate post-tawaf acts
After tawaf, the pilgrim drinks from Zamzam, kisses the threshold, places chest/face on al-Multazam, clings to the curtains, supplicates earnestly, weeps, and walks backwards out of the mosque.
These are recommended acts (sunan) based on the practice of the Prophet and early Muslims.
5
Understand the basis
The wujub of farewell tawaf is established by a hadith (Sahih Muslim). The walking backwards is not from an explicit hadith but is considered commendable out of reverence.
Always distinguish between established rulings (wajib) and recommended etiquettes (sunnah/adab).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قدم ثقله إلى مكة، وأقام بمنى للرمي كره. وإذا نفر إلى مكة، نزل بالمحصب، ثم طاف للصدر سبعة أشواط بلا رمل وسعي وهو واجب إلا على أهل مكة، ثم شرب من زمزم، وقبل العتبة، ووضع صدره ووجهه على الملتزم: وهو ما بين الحجر الأسود والباب، وتشبث بالأستار ساعة، ودعا مجتهداً، ويبكي، ويرجع قهقرى حتى يخرج من المسجد
And if he sent his heavy luggage to Mecca and stayed in Mina for the stoning, it is disliked. And when he departs to Mecca, he descends at al-Muhassab, then performs the farewell tawaf of seven circuits without ramal and without sa'y, and it is obligatory except for the people of Mecca. Then he drinks from Zamzam, and kisses the threshold, and places his chest and face on al-Multazam—which is between the Black Stone and the door—and clings to the cloth curtains for a while, and supplicates earnestly, and weeps, and walks backwards until he exits the mosque.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage from al-Hidayah presents a sequence of rulings and recommended acts for the pilgrim after the days of Mina. The first ruling concerns a person who sends his heavy baggage (thaqal) ahead to Mecca while he himself stays in Mina for the stoning (rami). This is disliked (makruh) because it involves unnecessary occupation and resembles those of luxury, contrary to humility. Next, when the pilgrim departs (nafara) from Mina to Mecca, it is sunnah to descend at al-Muhassab (also called al-Abtah), a valley between Mecca and Mina. Then he performs the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr) of seven circuits, without ramal (quick walking with shoulders swaying) and without sa'y (the running between Safa and Marwa). This tawaf is wajib (obligatory) for all pilgrims except the people of Mecca (i.e., those residing there). After completing the tawaf, he drinks from the well of Zamzam, facing the qibla. Then he goes to the door of the Kaaba, kisses the threshold (al-‘utbah), and places his chest and face on al-Multazam (the area between the Black Stone and the door), clinging to the cloth curtains (al-astar) covering the Kaaba. He remains there for a while, making earnest supplication, weeping, and then withdraws walking backwards (qahqara) so that his face remains toward the Kaaba until he exits the mosque. The walking backwards is not based on an explicit hadith but is considered commendable by scholars out of reverence for the House of Allah.

Key Terms
المحصب (al-Muhassab): A valley between Mecca and Mina, near al-Ma'la cemetery, also called al-Abtah. The place where the Prophet descended after leaving Mina.
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed after completing the rituals of Hajj before leaving Mecca. Also called tawaf al-wada' or tawaf akhir al-'ahd.
الملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba, a place for supplication.
العتلة (al-'utbah): The threshold of the Kaaba's door, elevated from the ground.
الأستار (al-astar): The cloth curtains covering the walls of the Kaaba.
قهقرى (qahqara): Walking backwards, facing the Kaaba while retreating out of reverence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr) for a non-Meccan pilgrim according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is sunnah.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is fard.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The farewell tawaf is a wajib act for non-Meccans, performed with specific etiquettes; omission requires compensation (dam).

Ruling on the Farewell Tawaf
States obligation and description of farewell tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the farewell tawaf, identify its proof, and describe the recommended acts that accompany it.

Core Idea
The farewell tawaf is wajib for all pilgrims except Makkans, based on the Prophet's command.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the obligation of the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-wada') and the recommended acts that follow it. You will learn the proof for its obligation and the spiritual practices that enhance this final act of Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the exception
Read the opening statement: the farewell tawaf is wajib (obligatory) except for the people of Makkah. Note who is exempted.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The commentator cites the hadith from Bukhari: the Prophet ﷺ ordered people to make the tawaf their last covenant with the House. Recognize this as the basis for the ruling.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but the command indicates obligation per Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form in the hadith (an yakuna) is interpreted as a command (amr) that implies obligation (wujub) in Hanafi jurisprudence.
Other schools may interpret the same hadith as recommendation.
4
Describe the sunan (recommended acts)
The passage lists: drinking Zamzam water, kissing the threshold, clinging to the Multazam, supplicating, weeping, and walking backwards out of reverence.
Walking backwards is mustahsan (considered good) even without a specific hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو واجب إلا على أهل مكة، ثم شرب من زمزم، وقبل العتبة، ووضع صدره ووجهه على الملتزم: وهو ما بين الحجر الأسود والباب، وتشبث بالأستار ساعة، ودعا مجتهداً، ويبكي، ويرجع قهقرى حتى يخرج من المسجد. قوله: وهو واجب؛ لأن النبي الله أمر الناس أن يكون آخر عهدهم بالبيت الطواف، أخرجه البخاري. قوله: ثم؛ أي بعد ما فرغ من الطواف يأتي بئراً موسوماً بزمزم، فيشرب من مائه تبركاً قائماً مستقبل القبلة، وقد ثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ذلك، أخرجه أحمد وغيره. قوله: وقبل؛ من التقبيل والعتبة بفتحات أي ثم أتى الكعبة ووضع فمه على عتبة بابه المرتفعة عن الأرض، وقبله والتزم بوضع الصدر والوجه على الملتزم، وتثبث: أي تعلق بأستار الكعبة، كما يتعلق عبد ذليل بطرف ثوب مولى جليل، ويتضرع ويدعو حامداً ومصلياً ومسلماً، ويبكي متحسراً على فراق تلك الأماكن الشريفة، رزقنا العود إليها مرة ثالثة، ثم وثم إلى أن نتوفى في المدينة الطيبة مع السلامة والعافية، ويدعو الله له بأن لا يجعله آخر العهد بتلك المقامات. قوله: قهقرى؛ بفتح القافين بينهما هاء ساكنة بعدهما راء مهملة الرجوع إلى خلف، بحيث لا يقع ظهره إلى الكعبة، بل وجهه، وهذا وإن لم يكن فيه حديث مرفوع أو موقوف، لكنه مستحسن عند العلماء إجلالاً للبيت، وإكراماً له وإكثاراً من النظر إليه عند الوداع.
It is obligatory except for the people of Makkah. Then he drinks from Zamzam, kisses the threshold, places his chest and face on the Multazam, which is between the Black Stone and the door, clings to the curtains for an hour, supplicates earnestly, weeps, and walks backwards until he leaves the mosque. He said: 'It is obligatory' because the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the people that their last covenant with the House should be the tawaf, as related by Bukhari. He said: 'Then' means after finishing the tawaf, he comes to a well known as Zamzam and drinks from its water for blessing, standing facing the qiblah. This is proven from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) as related by Ahmad and others. He said: 'Kisses' from kissing, and 'al-‘atabah' with fatha means then he comes to the Kaaba and places his mouth on the threshold of its door, elevated from the ground, and kisses it, and clings by placing his chest and face on the Multazam. 'Tashabbuth' means clinging to the curtains of the Kaaba like a lowly slave clings to the hem of a great master's garment, and he humbly supplicates, praising, sending blessings and salutations, and weeps regretfully at parting from those noble places – may Allah grant us return to them a third time, and then until we die in the blessed city of Medina with safety and well-being – and he prays to Allah that this not be his last visit to those stations. He said: 'Qahqariy' with fatha on the two qafs, a silent ha in between, and a ra after them, meaning retreating backwards so that his back does not face the Kaaba but his face. Although there is no marfu‘ or mawquf hadith on this, it is considered good (mustahsan) by the scholars out of reverence for the House, honor for it, and to increase looking at it during farewell.
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-wada‘). It opens by stating that this tawaf is wajib (obligatory) for all pilgrims except the people of Makkah. The commentator supports this with the hadith from Bukhari in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded that the last act before leaving Makkah should be the tawaf. The passage then describes the sunan (recommended acts) of the farewell tawaf: drinking Zamzam water for blessing, kissing the threshold of the Kaaba, placing the chest and face on the Multazam (the area between the Black Stone and the door), clinging to the Kiswah curtains, supplicating with humility, weeping, and walking backwards out of the mosque so as not to turn one's back to the Kaaba. The walking backwards is not based on a specific prophetic or companion report, but scholars consider it good practice to show reverence. The commentator also notes that drinking Zamzam while standing and facing the qiblah is established from the Prophet (peace be upon him) via Ahmad and others. The overall tone is one of deep spiritual devotion, with the commentator expressing a personal supplication to return to these holy places.

Key Terms
الملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba where the pilgrim places his chest and face.
العتبة (al-‘atabah): The threshold of the Kaaba's door, raised above the ground, which the pilgrim kisses.
قهقرى (qahqariy): Walking backwards while facing the Kaaba, so as not to turn one's back to it out of reverence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Standing at Arafah and the Dropping of Arrival Tawaf
Explains timing of wuquf and dropping of arrival tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid time for wuquf and explain under which conditions it is valid, and identify when tawaf al-qudum drops according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A moment of wuquf from zawal to dawn suffices; the arrival tawaf drops for those who stand before entering Makkah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies two interrelated Hajj rulings: the broad permissible time for the standing at Arafah and the sunnah nature of the arrival tawaf. Understanding these ensures a pilgrim knows when his Hajj is valid and when additional acts are no longer required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage gives two distinct rulings: (1) the arrival tawaf (tawaf al-qudum) drops for one who stands at Arafah before entering Makkah, and (2) the standing at Arafah is valid under broad conditions including time and personal states.
The first is a sunnah that drops; the second is a rukn that is valid even in challenging circumstances.
2
Locate the time limits for wuquf
Find the two time periods: sunnah time (from zawal to sunset on 9th) and permissible time (from zawal to true dawn of 10th). The hadith cited extends the valid period to dawn.
The 'sunnah time' is recommended; any wuquf within the permissible time is sufficient.
3
Analyze the conditions for validity
The text lists many states in which wuquf is valid: asleep, unconscious, intoxicated, fleeing, in janabah, etc. The key principle is that intention for wuquf is not required separately; the intention at ihram suffices.
This shows the school's leniency: the rukn is not nullified by lack of consciousness or ritual purity.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
On the issue of assuming ihram for an unconscious person without prior permission, Abu Hanifa permits it while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree. The text does not resolve this.
This ikhtilaf is noted in Zahir al-Riwayah; the mufta bihi may be determined by later tarjih.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
A pilgrim who arrives in Makkah after wuquf has already been performed may need to perform tawaf al-qudum, but if he performed wuquf before ever entering Makkah, the tawaf drops.
No compensation (dam) is required for omitting a sunnah.

The tawaf of arrival drops for the one who stood at Arafah before entering Makkah, and nothing is required of him for leaving it, because nothing is required of him for leaving a sunnah. He said: 'It drops' because it is only prescribed at the beginning of the actions; when he begins the actions of Hajj, it is no longer a sunnah. He said: 'Or passes through' from al-ijtiyaz which is passing; meaning he passed through the valley of Arafat while asleep and woke up afterwards. Similarly, one who passed in a state of unconsciousness and his companion assumed ihram for him, or in a state of intoxication, or fleeing, or pursuing a debtor, or was in a state of janabah, hadath, nifas, or walked through quickly, all of that is permissible. Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage combines two related rulings. First, the arrival tawaf (tawaf al-qudum) is a sunnah that is dropped for a pilgrim who stands at Arafah before entering Makkah. No penalty is incurred for omitting it. The reasoning given is that the arrival tawaf is prescribed at the beginning of the actions of Hajj; when one proceeds to Arafah and performs the wuquf, that sunnah is no longer applicable. Second, the standing at Arafah (wuquf) is valid under broad conditions: if done for even a moment between zawal (noon) on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah and the dawn of the 10th (day of Nahr). The sunnah time is from zawal to sunset, but the permissible time extends to dawn. The proof is the hadith from the Sunan collections: 'Whoever comes to Muzdalifah before dawn and stands at Arafah has caught the Hajj.' The validity extends to various states: passing through while asleep, unconscious, intoxicated, fleeing, pursuing a debtor, even in a state of janabah or during menses/postpartum. The commentator explains from al-Binayah that the secret is that wuquf does not require a separate intention; the intention at ihram suffices. Finally, the passage discusses the case of an unconscious person: if a companion assumes ihram on his behalf with permission, it is valid by agreement. Without permission, Abu Hanifa allows it, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree (the text cuts off before completing their argument).

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The arrival tawaf performed upon entering Makkah; it is sunnah and drops if one performs wuquf at Arafah before entering.
الوقوف بعرفة (al-wuquf bi 'Arafah): The standing at Arafah, the essential pillar (rukn) of Hajj, valid from zawal on 9th Dhul Hijjah to dawn on 10th.
الإهلال (al-ihlal): Raising the voice with talbiyah to enter the state of ihram.

Key Takeaway
Wuquf at Arafah is valid from zawal to dawn, even for a moment and in any state, and tawaf al-qudum is a sunnah that drops for those who perform wuquf before entering Makkah.

The Dropping of Tawaf al-Qudum in Hajj
Ruling on the dropping of Tawaf al-Qudum when main actions begin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum for a pilgrim who has begun the Hajj actions and explain the reasoning behind its dropping.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah that drops when Hajj actions begin—no penalty for omission.

This passage from Al-Wiqayah clarifies the status of the Tawaf of Arrival (Tawaf al-Qudum) in Hajj. While it is a recommended sunnah for the pilgrim entering Mecca, it is not obligatory. The key question is: what happens if the pilgrim delays entering Mecca until after standing at Arafat? The text provides a clear ruling and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah act recommended upon entering Mecca for Hajj.
The text explicitly says 'ولا شيء عليه بتركه' confirming it is not wajib.
2
Recognize the condition for dropping
The pilgrim must have stood at Arafat before entering Mecca.
The phrase 'عمن وقف بعرفة قبل دخول مكة' identifies the specific scenario.
3
Understand the consequence
The sunnah is dropped and there is no penalty or compensation required.
No sin, no dam (sacrifice) needed.
4
Analyze the talil (reasoning)
The reasoning is that Tawaf al-Qudum was legislated only at the beginning of the Hajj actions. Once the main actions start, its time has passed.
The commentary explains: 'لأنه ما شرع إلا في ابتداء الأفعال، فإذا شرع في أفعال الحج لم يبق سنة.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسقط طواف القدوم عمن وقف بعرفة قبل دخول مكة، ولا شيء عليه بتركه. قوله : ويسقط؛ لأنه ما شرع إلا في ابتداء الأفعال، فإذا شرع في أفعال الحج لم يبق سنة.
And the Tawaf al-Qudum is dropped for one who stood at Arafat before entering Mecca, and nothing is upon him for leaving it. His statement: 'And it is dropped' because it (Tawaf al-Qudum) was only prescribed at the beginning of the actions, so when he begins the actions of Hajj, it no longer remains sunnah.
Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement followed by commentary. The ruling: The Tawaf of Arrival (Tawaf al-Qudum) is a sunnah for the pilgrim entering Mecca. However, if the pilgrim has already stood at Arafat before entering Mecca (i.e., entered the main actions of Hajj), this sunnah drops and there is no penalty for omitting it. The commentator explains the reasoning: Tawaf al-Qudum was only legislated at the beginning of the Hajj actions; once the pilgrim has commenced the actual rituals of Hajj (like standing at Arafat), the time for this sunnah has passed.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (Tawaf al-Qudum): A circumambulation performed upon arrival in Mecca as a greeting to the Kaaba, considered sunnah in Hajj.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed; omission is not sinful but disliked.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah that drops when a pilgrim begins Hajj actions at Arafat before entering Mecca, with no penalty for omission.

Wuquf at Arafat and the Companion's Proxy Ihram
Expansion on wuquf rules and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on valid wuquf and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding proxy ihram for an unconscious pilgrim.

Core Idea
Wuquf is valid even without intention, but proxy ihram requires explicit permission unless a companionship contract implies it.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah expands on the rules of wuquf at Arafat, clarifying the time limits and the surprising validity of wuquf in various states of consciousness. More importantly, it introduces a key intra-madhhab disagreement: when a companion performs ihram for an unconscious pilgrim without prior permission, does the wuquf count? The answer hinges on the nature of the companionship contract (taqd al-rafaqah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
The passage first discusses the time for wuquf (sunnah and permissible) and the hadith proof, then addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute on proxy ihram for the unconscious pilgrim.
Remember that the first part is agreed upon; the dispute is only the last part.
2
Examine the conditions of valid wuquf
Note that wuquf is valid even while asleep, unconscious, intoxicated, fleeing, menstruating, etc. The reason is that wuquf does not require its own intention; the intention from ihram suffices.
This principle is key to understanding why the dispute arises.
3
State the disputing positions
Both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree that the wuquf is valid if the unconscious person gave explicit permission. The dispute is when no permission was given. Abu Hanifa says valid; the Sahibayn say invalid.
4
Analyze the proofs for each side
Abu Hanifa argues that the companionship contract implies permission (idhn dilalah) for the companion to help in matters the unconscious person cannot perform. The Sahibayn require explicit permission or personal intention.
The hadith proof is for the time, not for this dispute.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a companion performs ihram without permission, according to Abu Hanifa the unconscious pilgrim's hajj is valid; according to the Sahibayn it is invalid and must be repeated.
The later relied-upon position follows Abu Hanifa, as seen in al-Hidayah and al-Binaya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ومن وقف ... الخ؛ اعلم أن الوقت المسنون هو ما بعد زوال يوم عرفة إلى الغروب، ووقت الجواز هو منه إلى طلوع الصبح الصادق يوم النحر؛ لحديث: "من جاء ليلة جمع قبل طلوع الفجر ووقف بعرفة فقد أدرك الحج". قوله : أو اجتاز؛ من الاجتياز وهو المرور؛ أي مر بوادي عرفات حالة النوم، واستيقظ بعده، وكذا من مر عليه حالة الإغماء فأحرم عنه رفيقه، أو حالة السكر، أو هاربا، أو طالب غريم، أو كان جنبا أو محدثا أو نفساء أو مشى فيه مسرعا يجوز في ذلك كله. كذا في «البناية»، والسر فيه : أن الوقوف بعرفة يصح بلا نية، ويغني عنها وجود النية عند الإحرام. قوله : وأهل؛ هو ماض من الإهلال، وهو رفع الصوت بالتلبية، يعني أحرم عن المغمى عليه أحد رفقائه، هذا اتفاقي عند إذن المغمى عليه لأحد من رفقائه بأن يحرم عنه إذا أغمي عليه. وأما إذا لم يأذن فأحرم واحد منهم تجوز عند أبي حنيفة، وخالفاه بناء على أنه لم يحرم بنفسه، ولم يأذن لغيره، فلا يعتبر بوقوفه، وهو يقول لما عاقدهم عقد الرفاقة صار ذلك إذنا بالاستعانة فيما يعجز عن مباشرته بنفسه، وكان الإذن ثابتا دلالة، فلو أحرم عنه غير رفيقه لم يجز إلا بالإذن. كذا في «الهداية» و«البناية».
His statement: 'And whoever stood...' Know that the sunnah time is after noon of the day of Arafah until sunset, and the permissible time is from that until the true dawn of the day of Nahr, due to the hadith: 'Whoever comes to Muzdalifah on the night of Jam' before dawn and stood at Arafah has attained the hajj.' His statement: 'or passed through' – from passing through, meaning passing through the valley of Arafat while asleep and waking up afterwards. Similarly, one who passed through while unconscious and his companion performed ihram for him, or in a state of intoxication, or fleeing, or seeking a debtor, or junub, or in hadath, or menstruating, or walked quickly – all are permissible. As in 'al-Binaya', and the secret is that wuquf at Arafah is valid without intention, and the intention at the time of ihram suffices for it. His statement: 'and his companion performed ihram' – it is the past tense of 'ihlal', which is raising the voice with talbiyah, meaning one of his companions performed ihram for the unconscious person. This is agreed upon when the unconscious person gave permission to a companion to do so if he becomes unconscious. But if he did not give permission and one of them performed ihram, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagreed based on the fact that he did not perform ihram himself nor give permission to others, so his standing is not considered. Abu Hanifa argues that because they contracted companionship, that serves as permission to seek help in what one cannot do himself, so the permission is established indicatively. If a non-companion performs ihram for him, it is not permissible except with permission. As in 'al-Hidayah' and 'al-Binaya'.
Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probing a complex set of rulings. It begins by explaining the time for wuquf at Arafat: the sunnah time is from noon of 9th Dhul Hijjah to sunset, while the permissible time extends until the true dawn of the 10th (the day of Nahr). The proof is a hadith indicating that if one reaches Muzdalifah before dawn and has stood at Arafat, his hajj is valid. The commentator then explains various states in which wuquf is valid: passing through while asleep, unconscious, with a companion performing ihram on his behalf, intoxicated, fleeing, etc. The reason is that wuquf is valid without intention (niyyah) – the niyyah at ihram suffices. The key intra-Hanafi dispute: If a companion performs ihram for an unconscious person without his prior permission, Abu Hanifa says it is valid based on the implied permission from the contract of companionship (taqd al-rafaqah), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say it is invalid because he did not personally intend nor authorize. Abu Hanifa's view is that the companion contract inherently involves mutual assistance, thus permission is established by indication (dalalah). If a non-companion does it, explicit permission is required.

Key Terms
وقوف عرفة (Wuquf Arafah): The standing or presence at the plain of Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; the essential pillar of Hajj.
عقد الرفاقة (Aqd al-rafaqah): A contract of companionship among travelers; implies mutual consent to assist each other in necessary matters.
إهلال (Ihlal): Raising the voice in talbiyah to signify entering ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the proof cited in the passage for the permissible time of wuquf extending until dawn of the 10th?
A) Quranic verse
B) Hadith of the Prophet
C) Ijma of the Companions
D) Qiyas on the time of Fajr

Key Takeaway
Wuquf at Arafat is valid without individual intention, but proxy ihram for an unconscious person requires explicit permission or a companionship contract that implies it.

Missing Arafat and Women's Ihram Covering
Ruling on missing Arafat and gender ihram covering with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fawt al-hajj (missing Arafat) and explain why a woman covers her head but not her face in ihram, citing the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Missing Arafat invalidates hajj; women in ihram cover heads but show faces.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains two critical rulings: the consequences of missing the essential standing at Arafat, and the distinct dress code for women in ihram. While general hajj requirements are shared, the Prophet's hadith establishes a clear gender distinction in what parts are uncovered. The commentary expands on each element, providing the evidence and practical steps.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two distinct legal topics: (1) fawt al-hajj (missing Arafat) and (2) the woman's ihram covering. The text states them consecutively.
The first ruling uses 'wa man lam yaqif' and the second starts with 'wal-mar'atu ka al-rajul'.
2
Analyze the fawt al-hajj ruling
Understand that missing Arafat invalidates the hajj. The pilgrim must perform tawaf and sa'ee (as in umrah), exit ihram (tahallul), and make up the hajj the following year (qada). The commentary clarifies each action.
Qada is wajib for obligatory hajj; for voluntary hajj, it is not required.
3
Analyze the woman's ihram ruling
The woman is like the man in most rulings, but she does not uncover her head; instead she uncovers her face. The commentator explains that her head is 'awrah and must be covered.
The phrase 'bal wajhiha' emphasizes the uncovered part.
4
Extract the dalil
The hadith 'Ihram of a man is in his head, ihram of a woman is in her face' is cited as proof. Identify its source and transmission status (zanni).
The hadith is ahad, found in Sunan al-Bayhaqi and others.
5
Determine the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith directly establishes that the place of ihram (the body part associated with the state) differs: men uncover heads, women cover heads and uncover faces. This proves that a woman's head is not to be uncovered in ihram.
The illa is the explicit command in the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لم يقف فيها فات حجه، فطاف وسعى، وتحلل وقضى من قابل، والمرأة كالرجل لكنها لا تكشف رأسها، بل وجهها. قوله : وتحلل؛ التحلل الخروج من الإحرام، وهو لمن فات الحج منه يكون بأفعال العمرة من الطواف والسعي، ثم الحلق أو القصر. قوله : وقضى؛ أي يجب عليه قضاء حجة الفائت في العام القابل. قوله : كالرجل؛ أي في الأحكام المذكورة. قوله : لكنها؛ بيان للفرق بين الرجل والمرأة. قوله : بل وجهها؛ فإن رأسها عورة، لا يحل كشفها، ويدل عليه حديث "إحرام الرجل في رأسه، وإحرام المرأة في وجهها".
And whoever does not stand in it (Arafat), his hajj is lost; so he should perform tawaf and sa'ee, and exit ihram (tahallul), and make it up from the following year. And the woman is like the man, but she does not uncover her head, rather her face. His statement: 'and exit ihram' – leaving ihram, which for one who missed the hajj is by the actions of umrah: tawaf, sa'ee, then shaving or trimming. His statement: 'and make it up' – meaning he must make up the missed hajj in the following year. His statement: 'like the man' – meaning in the aforementioned rulings. His statement: 'but' – explanation of the difference between man and woman. His statement: 'rather her face' – because her head is 'awrah, it is not permissible to uncover it, and the hadith 'the ihram of the man is in his head, and the ihram of the woman is in her face' indicates this.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that anyone who misses wuquf at Arafat completely (i.e., does not stand there during the valid time) has lost the hajj (fawt al-hajj). He must then perform tawaf and sa'ee (as in umrah), exit ihram by shaving or cutting hair, and then in the next year perform a makeup hajj (qada). This applies whether the original hajj was obligatory, nadhr, or voluntary. The commentator clarifies each step. Then the text addresses women: she is like a man in the above rulings, but with one key difference: she does not uncover her head; rather she shows her face. The reason is that the head is 'awrah for a woman. The proof is the hadith that the ihram of a man is in his head (i.e., he uncovers it) and the ihram of a woman is in her face (she covers her head but uncovers her face).

Key Terms
فوت الحج (Fawt al-Hajj): The situation where a pilgrim misses the standing at Arafat within the valid time, resulting in the invalidation of the hajj for that year.
تحلل (Tahallul): Exiting the state of ihram; in case of fawt al-hajj, it is achieved by performing the actions of umrah.
إحرام المرأة في وجهها (Ihram al-mar'ah fi wajhiha): A woman's ihram is observed by covering her head and uncovering her face; she does not cover her face like a man covers his head.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Uncover both head and face like a man.
B) Cover both head and face.
C) Cover her head and leave her face uncovered.
D) Cover her face but leave her head uncovered.

Key Takeaway
Missing Arafat requires making up the hajj; a woman in ihram covers her head but not her face.

Missing Arafat: Tahallul and Qada'
Ruling on missing Arafat and required actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who misses the standing at Arafat and explain the actions required to exit ihram and the obligation to make up the Hajj.

Core Idea
Missing Arafat voids the Hajj; pilgrim must perform Umrah to exit ihram and repeat Hajj next year.

This lesson focuses on the first part of the passage: what happens when a pilgrim enters ihram for Hajj but fails to stand at Arafat. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: the Hajj is lost, but the pilgrim must complete the acts of Umrah to exit ihram and then make up the Hajj in the following year. This ruling is based on the practice of the Companions and is unified across the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger for the ruling
The ruling applies to a person who has entered ihram for Hajj but does not witness the standing at Arafat (wuquf). The text states 'man lam yaqif fiha fata hajjuh' – whoever does not stand in it, his Hajj is lost.
This implies that wuquf is the essential pillar of Hajj; missing it invalidates the entire Hajj.
2
List the required actions after missing Arafat
The pilgrim must perform Tawaf and Sa'i, then shave or trim hair (tahallul). These are the acts of Umrah, which allow him to exit ihram. Then he must make up the missed Hajj the following year (qada).
3
Determine the legal status of the qada
The commentary clarifies that qada is wajib (obligatory) regardless of whether the original Hajj was fard, nadhr, or tatawwu'. This is based on the principle that a missed obligation must be fulfilled.
This aligns with the Hanafi position that qada is required for any invalidated Hajj.
4
Confirm the absence of intra-school dispute
The Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on this ruling. No difference is reported, so it is a settled position from the Zahir al-Riwayah.
