كتاب الحج باب الإحرام
ومن لم يقف فيها فات حجه، فطاف وسعى، وتحلل وقضى من قابل، والمرأة كالرجل لكنها لا تكشف رأسها، بل وجهها
هذا لمن أحرم، ولم يدرك الحج
أنه لم يحرم بنفسه، ولم يأذن لغيره، فلا يعتبر بوقوفه، وهو يقول لما عاقدهم عقد الرفاقة صار ذلك إذناً بالاستعانة فيما يعجز عن مباشرته بنفسه، وكان الإذن ثابتاً دلالة، فلو أحرم عنه غير رفيقه لم يجز إلا بالإذن. كذا في الهداية والبناية
(1) قوله: وتحلل؛ التحلل الخروج من الإحرام، وهو لمن فات الحج منه يكون بأفعال العمرة من الطواف والسعي، ثم الحلق أو القصر، هكذا روي عن جمع من الصحابة في الموطأ وغيره
(2) قوله: وقضى؛ أي يجب عليه قضاء حجة الفائت في العام القابل؛ أي السنة المستقبلة، سواء كان حجه فرضاً أو نذراً أو تطوعاً
(3) قوله: كالرجل؛ أي في الأحكام المذكورة
(4) قوله: لكنها؛ بيان للفرق بين الرجل والمرأة
(5) قوله: بل وجهها؛ فإن رأسها عورة، لا يحل كشفها، ويدل عليه حديث إحرام الرجل في رأسه، وإحرام المرأة في وجهها، أخرجه البيهقي
ولو سدلت شيئاً عليه، وجافته عنه صح، ولا تلبي المرأة جهراً، ولا تسعى بين الميلين الأخضرين، ولا تحلق بل تقصر، وتلبس المخيط، ولا تقرب الحجر في الزحام
(1) قوله: وجافته؛ أي باعدته عنه، بحيث لا يمس الثوب الوجه، قال في الفتح: وقد جعلوا لذلك أعواداً كالقبة تسدل على الوجه، ويلقى الثوب فوقها
(2) قوله: ولا تلبي جهراً؛ بل تسمع نفسها؛ لأن في جهرها احتمال الفتنة
(3) قوله: ولا تسعى؛ بل تمشي وكذا لا ترمل في الطواف؛ لأن كل ذلك مخل بالستر
(4) قوله: بل تقصير؛ يدل عليه حديث: ليس على النساء الحلق، إنما على النساء التقصير، أخرجه أبو داود
(5) قوله: وتلبس المخيط؛ أي ما بدأ لها؛ لأن اشتراط تركه يخل بسترها
(6) قوله: ولا تقرب الحجر؛ أي لا تقبل ولا تمس الحجر الأسود عند الزحمة؛ لأنها ممنوعة عن ملامسة الرجال، وتطوف من وراء الناس، وتكتفي باستقبال الحجر كما مر
اختلفوا في حكم تغطية وجه المرأة في الحج ومجافاته على أربعة أقوال: الأول: جواز ذلك، وهو ظاهر كلام المصنف، والبدائع، والهداية، والتبيين وغيرهم. الثاني: استحباب وندب ذلك، وهو اختيار صاحب الفتح والدر المختار وغيرهم. الثالث: وجوب ذلك، وهو اختيار صاحب النهاية. الرابع: التفصيل: وهو أن محمل الاستحباب عند عدم الأجانب، وأما عند وجودهم فالارخاء واجب عليها عند الامكان، وعند عدمه يجب على الأجانب غض البصر وهو اختيار صاحب البحر، ومال إليه ابن عابدين في رد المحتار. قال صاحب الخانية والمحيط البرهاني والفتح: دلت المسألة على أن المرأة منهية عن اظهار وجهها للاجانب بلا ضرورة؛ لأنها منهية عن تغطيته لحق النسك لولا ذلك وإلا لم يكن لهذا فائدة.
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram. Whoever does not stand at Arafat, his Hajj is lost; so he performs Tawaf, Sa'i, removes ihram, and makes up the Hajj the following year. And the woman is like the man except that she does not uncover her head but [uncover] her face. This is for one who had entered ihram and did not catch the Hajj. Explanation: 'tahallul' means exiting ihram, for one who misses the Hajj it is by the acts of Umrah: Tawaf, Sa'i, then shaving or trimming, as reported from a group of Companions in al-Muwatta etc. 'qada' means he must make up the missed Hajj in the coming year, whether the Hajj was obligatory, vowed, or voluntary. 'like the man' means in the aforementioned rulings. 'but she' is a clarification of the difference between man and woman. 'but her face' because her head is 'awrah, it is not permissible to uncover it, and the hadith indicates it: 'The ihram of a man is in his head, and the ihram of a woman is in her face' reported by al-Bayhaqi. And if she drapes something over her face such that it is kept away from it, it is valid. And the woman should not recite talbiyah loudly, nor walk quickly between the two green milestones, nor shave but rather trim, and she may wear sewn garments, and she should not approach the Black Stone in crowded conditions. Explanation: 'kept away' means she distances it so the cloth does not touch the face. 'do not recite loudly' but she makes herself hear, because loudness risks temptation. 'does not walk quickly' but walks normally, and similarly does not run in Tawaf, because all that compromises modesty. 'but trim' is indicated by the hadith: 'Shaving is not for women; women only trim' reported by Abu Dawud. 'wears sewn garments' meaning whatever occurs to her, because requiring her to avoid it would compromise covering her. 'does not approach the Stone' meaning she does not kiss or touch the Black Stone during crowding, because she is prevented from touching men; she circumambulates behind the people and is content with facing the Stone as before. They differed on the ruling of covering the woman's face and keeping it away in Hajj into four opinions: first: permissibility, which is the apparent statement of the author, al-Bada'i, al-Hidayah, al-Tabyin etc. Second: recommendation, chosen by the author of al-Fath, al-Durr al-Mukhtar etc. Third: obligation, chosen by the author of al-Nihayah. Fourth: detail: that the recommendation applies when no foreign men are present, but when they are present, covering is obligatory upon her if possible, and if not possible, the foreign men must lower their gaze, chosen by the author of al-Bahr, and Ibn 'Abideen inclined to it. The authors of al-Khaniyah, al-Muhit al-Burhani, and al-Fath said: The issue indicates that the woman is prohibited from showing her face to foreign men without necessity, because she is prohibited from covering it due to the right of the ritual; otherwise there would be no benefit.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage combines two distinct rulings within the chapter of Ihram. The first ruling states that a person who enters Ihram for Hajj but misses the standing at Arafat (wuquf) has effectively lost that Hajj. He must complete the remaining Umrah actions (Tawaf, Sa'i, shaving/trimming) to exit Ihram, and then make up the missed Hajj in the following year. The commentary clarifies that this applies whether the Hajj was obligatory, voluntary, or a vow. The second ruling addresses women's Ihram: a woman is generally like a man in the rulings of Ihram except that she must not uncover her head (as men do), but rather she may keep her face uncovered. The commentary explains that a woman may drape a cloth over her face in a way that avoids contact (mujafafah), and this is valid. The hadith of Ibn 'Umar is cited: 'The Ihram of a man is in his head, and the Ihram of a woman is in her face.' The passage further details specific differences for women: they do not recite talbiyah loudly, do not walk briskly between the green milestones (raml or sa'i), do not shave but only trim their hair, may wear sewn garments (because their entire body is 'awrah), and refrain from touching the Black Stone in crowds to avoid contact with men. The commentary then presents a four-opinion ikhtilaf on the ruling of covering the woman's face in Ihram: permissibility (the Hanafi view), recommendation, obligation (in some opinions), and a detailed view distinguishing absence/presence of foreign men. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that covering the face is permissible but not required, though in the presence of non-mahram men, covering is necessary to avoid fitnah, which aligns with the principle of sadd al-dhara'i.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj/Umrah, marked by specific prohibitions and intentions.
تحلل (tahallul): Exiting the state of ihram by completing the required acts (shaving/trimming hair, etc.).
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or invalidated religious obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a person do after missing the standing at Arafat in order to exit the state of ihram?
A) Continue the remaining Hajj rites and sacrifice an animal.
B) Perform Umrah (Tawaf, Sa'i, shaving/trimming).
C) Return home immediately and repeat Hajj next year without doing anything else.
D) Only make up the Hajj next year, no need to exit ihram now.

Key Takeaway
Missing Arafat invalidates Hajj; immediate tahallul via Umrah and qada the following year are obligatory.

Women's Ihram: Covering the Face and Other Distinctions
Specific rules for women in ihram and four opinions on face covering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific differences between men and women in ihram according to the Hanafi school and evaluate the four opinions on women covering their faces.

Core Idea
Women may cover their face in ihram with cloth away from skin; they differ from men in talbiyah, sa'i, shaving, and clothing.

This lesson delves into the second part of the passage: the unique rules for women in ihram. While women are generally like men in the basic obligations, they have distinct rules regarding covering the face, reciting talbiyah, performing sa'i, shaving vs. trimming, and wearing sewn garments. The passage also presents a detailed four-opinion ikhtilaf on the ruling of covering the woman's face, allowing us to trace the Hanafi tarjih.

Guided Path
1
List the general principle for women in ihram
The text begins 'al-mar'atu ka al-rajul' – the woman is like the man in the rulings mentioned, i.e., the same rules for missing Hajj apply. Then it deduces exceptions.
2
Identify the major difference: head covering vs face covering
Men uncover their heads; women uncover their faces. The hadith 'Ihram of a man is in his head, ihram of a woman in her face' indicates that the face is the part that must be uncovered to signify ihram.
This hadith is used to argue that covering the face is not prohibited as long as it does not touch the skin.
3
Work through each specific rule for women
The text enumerates: do not recite talbiyah loudly, do not walk quickly between green milestones, do not shave but trim, may wear sewn garments, and do not approach the Black Stone in crowds.
Each rule is explained by the commentary: loudness risks fitnah, brisk walking compromises modesty, shaving is not prescribed for women, sewn garments are needed for covering 'awrah, and touching the Stone risks contact with men.
4
Analyze the four opinions on covering the face
The passage details four views: permissibility (mubah), recommendation (mustahabb), obligation (wajib), and a detailed view distinguishing presence/absence of non-mahram men. The mufta bihi is the detailed view: permissible but obligatory when non-mahram men are present.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of tarjih among conflicting opinions within the school.
5
Connect to the principle of 'sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking means to evil)
The underlying rationale is preventing fitnah. Women are prohibited from displaying their faces to non-mahram without necessity, but also from covering the face due to the right of the ritual? Actually, the rule balances both.

Source Text

The first ruling states that a person who enters Ihram for Hajj but misses the standing at Arafat (wuquf) has effectively lost that Hajj. Key Terms
مجافاة (mujafafah): Keeping the covering (e.g., cloth over face) away from the skin so it does not touch.
المخيط (al-makhit): Sewn garments (i.e., tailored clothing) that men are prohibited from wearing in ihram, but women may wear.
تقصير (taqsir): Trimming the hair, specifically for women exiting ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred (mufta bihi) Hanafi opinion, what is the ruling on a woman covering her face in ihram?
A) It is completely prohibited.
B) It is permissible only in the absence of non-mahram men.
C) It is recommended and becomes obligatory when non-mahram men are present.
D) It is obligatory at all times.

Key Takeaway
Women in ihram have distinct rules; covering the face is permissible with mujafafah, and obligatory in the presence of non-mahram men.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Women's Ihram Rulings: Face Covering, Talbiyah, Sa'ee, and More
Listing rulings for women in ihram with commentary and ikhtilaf on face covering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six specific rulings for women in ihram according to the Hanafi school and evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on covering the face, identifying the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A woman's modesty in ihram takes precedence, allowing loose face covering, soft talbiyah, walking in sa'ee, and sewn garments.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on al-Wiqayah lists six key rulings for a woman in ihram, each with a clear rationale rooted in modesty and evidence. The commentary then enlarges on the first point—face covering—by presenting a detailed intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: whether it is permissible, recommended, obligatory, or detailed. By working through this text, you will learn how the school balances the prohibitions of ihram with the overriding duty of avoiding fitna, and how later authorities settled on a nuanced position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six rulings
Read the base text (first paragraph) and list the six distinct actions or prohibitions for women in ihram: covering the face with the cloth held away (mujāfāt), lowering the voice in talbiyah, walking (not running) during sa'ee between the two green milestones, trimming (not shaving) hair, wearing sewn garments, and avoiding the Black Stone in crowds.
Note that each ruling is followed by a brief commentary in the brackets [1]–[6].
2
Understand the rationale for each ruling
For each ruling, find the reason given in the commentary: modesty (sitr) and avoiding fitna (temptation). The hadith 'There is no shaving upon women; only trimming' provides explicit proof for the hair ruling.
The rationale for wearing sewn garments is that forbidding them would undermine modesty—a unique Hanafi leniency.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on face covering
Read the second part of the passage (starting at (۱)). Identify the four opinions: (1) jawaz (permissibility)—apparent from the base text; (2) istihbab (recommendation); (3) wujub (obligation); (4) tafsīl (detailed: obligatory when non-mahram are present if possible, otherwise men must lower gaze).
The ikhtilaf is internal to the Hanafi school; all four are based on valid evidence.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Note that later scholars (Ibn Abidin, author of al-Bahr) favored the detailed view. The tarjih authority is Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar. The mufta bihi today: when non-mahram men are present and she can cover loosely, it is obligatory; if impossible, the men must lower their gaze.
The authority weight is 'fatawa mutakhkhirin' (later fatwa works).
5
Apply to a contemporary scenario
Consider a woman in ihram at the Haram during Hajj. Use the rulings to answer: Can she wear a face veil (niqab) that touches her face? She should avoid touching, but if she can use a dome-like structure or hold it away, it is valid. Must she cover her face from non-mahram men? According to the mufta bihi, yes, if possible.
This step connects the classical text to modern practice.

And the woman should not raise her voice in talbiyah, and she should not do sa'ee between the two green milestones, and she should not shave but should trim [her hair], and she wears sewn garments, and she should not approach the Stone in crowding.
[1] His statement: 'and holds it away from it' means she distances it from her face such that the cloth does not touch the face. He said in al-Fath: 'They have made for that sticks like a dome, she lets down [the cloth] over the face, and throws the cloth over them.' [2] His statement: 'and does not raise her voice in talbiyah' rather she makes herself hear; because in raising her voice there is possibility of temptation. [3] His statement: 'and does not do sa'ee' rather she walks, and similarly she does not do ramal in tawaf; because all that undermines concealment. [4] His statement: 'but she trims' is indicated by the hadith: 'There is no shaving upon women; only trimming is upon women' narrated by Abu Dawud. [5] His statement: 'and she wears sewn garments' means whatever is available to her, because requiring avoidance of that would undermine her concealment. [6] His statement: 'and does not approach the Stone' means she does not kiss nor touch the Black Stone during crowding, because she is prohibited from touching men, and she circumambulates from behind the people, and suffices with facing the Stone as previously.
(1) They differed on the ruling of covering a woman's face in hajj and holding it away in four opinions: First: permissibility of that, and it is the apparent statement of the author, and al-Bada'i', al-Hidayah, al-Tabyin, and others. Second: it is recommended (istihbab), and it is the choice of the author of al-Fath, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and others. Third: obligation, and it is the choice of the author of al-Nihayah. Fourth: detail: that the basis of recommendation is when there are no non-mahram men, but when they are present, letting down [the cloth] is obligatory upon her if possible, and if not possible, then it is obligatory for non-mahram men to lower their gaze, and it is the choice of the author of al-Bahr, and Ibn Abidin inclined to it in Radd al-Muhtar. The author of al-Khaniyyah, al-Muhit al-Burhani, and al-Fath said: The issue indicates that the woman is prohibited from showing her face to non-mahram men without necessity, because she is prohibited from covering it for the sake of the rite; if not for that, there would be no benefit in this.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings for women in ihram, found in the base text of al-Wiqayah. The commentator explains each point: (1) covering the face: it is permissible if the cloth is held away from the face, and they even constructed a dome-like structure for this. Followed by a detailed discussion of the four opinions within the Hanafi school on covering the face. (2) Talbiyah: women should not raise their voices to avoid temptation. (3) Sa'ee: women should walk, not run (ramal), due to modesty. (4) Hair: women trim, not shave, based on hadith. (5) Sewn garments: women may wear them because not doing so would compromise modesty. (6) Black Stone: women avoid touching or kissing it in crowds to avoid contact with men. The ikhtilaf on face covering shows the breadth of the school.

Key Terms
المخيط (al-makhīṭ): Sewn garments; in the context of ihram, clothing that is tailored and sewn.
التقصير (al-taqṣīr): Trimming the hair, specifically for women in ihram, as opposed to shaving (halq).
الميلين الأخضرين (al-mīlayn al-akhḍarayn): The two green milestones located between Safa and Marwah, where men run during sa'ee.
المجافاة (al-mujāfāh): Holding the covering cloth away from the face so it does not touch the skin.
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The chant recited by pilgrims: Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...

B) Recommended (istihbab)
C) Obligatory (wujub) in all cases

Women in ihram must balance the prohibition of covering the face tightly with the obligation of modesty, leading to a nuanced mufta bihi: cover loosely when non-mahram are present if possible, otherwise the men must lower their gaze.

Menstruation and Its Effect on Hajj Rites
Clarifying that menstruation only prevents tawaf, not other Hajj rites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which hajj acts are prevented by menstruation and explain when tawaf al-sadar is dropped.

Core Idea
Menstruation does not invalidate hajj; only tawaf is prevented and farewell tawaf is dropped after tawaf al-ziyarah.

This lesson clarifies that menstruation does not bar a woman from performing most hajj rites. The key exception is tawaf (circumambulation), which requires ritual purity. The commentator explains the evidence from the Sunnah and the practical ruling when a woman menstruates after completing key rites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling statement
Read the base text: 'وحيضها لا يمنع نُسكاً إلا الطواف، وهو بعد ركنيه يسقط طوافِ الصَّدَر'. This states that menstruation prevents only tawaf, and after its two pillars (wuquf and tawaf al-ziyarah), the farewell tawaf is dropped.
2
Examine the first hadith proof
The Prophet ﷺ told Aisha: 'افعلي ما يفعل الحاج غير أن لا تطوفي' – do what the pilgrim does except do not circumambulate. This proves that all hajj acts except tawaf are valid during menstruation.
The imperative 'افعلي' indicates permissibility and validity.
3
Analyze the second hadith proof
The story of Safiyyah shows that if a woman has performed tawaf al-ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf) before menstruating, her farewell tawaf is dropped: 'فلا إذا' – then no problem.
The Prophet ﷺ initially feared she would detain them if she had not done tawaf al-ziyarah.
4
Understand the condition for tawaf
The commentator corrects a misperception: purity is a condition for tawaf itself, regardless of location. A woman cannot circumambulate even outside the mosque while menstruating.
So the phrase 'for it is in the mosque' is insufficient; the real condition is purity.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a woman menstruates after standing at Arafah and performing tawaf al-ziyarah, her farewell tawaf is waived and her hajj is complete.
No sacrifice is required; the hajj is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[١] قوله : لا يمنع نُسكاً ؛ - بضمتين : أي فعلاً من أفعال الحج، كالوقوف بعرفة وغيره لما روى مسلم وغيره : أن النبي الله قال لعائشة رضي الله عنها حين حاضت : افعلي ما يفعلُ الحاج غير أن لا تطوفي)) . [٣] قوله : يسقط ؛ لما روى أن بعض أزواج النبي يا حاضت أيام حجه فقال : «لعلها حابستنا)، ظناً منه أنها لم تطف طواف الزيارة، فقالوا : قد طافت معنا ، فقال : فلا إذن»، وهذه القصة مخرجة في «الصحاح».

في «الموطأ» (١): ٤١٤) ، و (سنن أبي داود»(١ : ٦١٢)، وغيرها.
And her menstruation does not prevent any rite except tawaf, and after its two pillars it drops the tawaf al-sadar.
[1] His statement: 'does not prevent any rite' with two dammas: i.e., any action of hajj, like standing at Arafah and others, because of what Muslim and others narrated that the Prophet (saw) said to Aisha (ra) when she menstruated: 'Do what the pilgrim does except do not circumambulate.' [2] His statement: 'for it is in the mosque' i.e., the Sacred Mosque. This is insufficient, because if she tawaf from outside the mosque it is also not permissible, for purity from major ritual impurity is a condition for the tawaf itself. [3] His statement: 'it drops' because of the narration that one of the wives of the Prophet (saw) menstruated during his hajj, so he said: 'Perhaps she will detain us,' thinking that she had not done tawaf al-ziyarah, but they said: 'She did tawaf with us,' so he said: 'Then no problem.' This story is recorded in the Sahihs.
(1) From Aisha (ra) when she menstruated, the Prophet (saw) said to her: 'That is something Allah has written upon the daughters of Adam, so do what the pilgrim does except do not circumambulate the House until you become pure.' In Sahih al-Bukhari, Sahih Muslim, etc. (2) With wording: 'Is Safiyyah detaining us?' in Sahih Muslim and Sahih al-Bukhari, etc. And from Aisha (ra): 'The Messenger of Allah (saw) mentioned Safiyyah bint Huyay and it was said that she had menstruated, so the Messenger of Allah (saw) said: "Perhaps she will detain us." They said: "O Messenger of Allah, she has performed ifadah (tawaf al-ziyarah)." He said: "Then no problem."' In al-Muwatta, Sunan Abi Dawud, etc.
Source pages p. 593

Commentary
This passage clarifies the effect of menstruation on hajj rites. The base text states that menstruation only prevents tawaf, not other rites like standing at Arafah, staying at Muzdalifah, or throwing stones. The commentator provides evidence: the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet commanded her to do all acts of hajj except tawaf. Additionally, the story of Safiyyah shows that if she performed tawaf al-ziyarah before menstruation, the farewell tawaf is dropped. The commentator also notes that the condition for tawaf is purity, so even if a woman were to circumambulate outside the mosque, it would not be valid.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (ṭawāf al-ṣadar): The farewell circumambulation (tawaf al-wada') performed before leaving Mecca.
نُسك (nusuk): A ritual act of hajj or umrah, such as standing at Arafah, staying at Muzdalifah, throwing stones, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Menstruation only prevents tawaf; farewell tawaf is waived if tawaf al-ziyarah was performed.

Defining Badana and Hady in Sending a Sacrificial Animal
Defining badana and its relation to hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of badana and distinguish it from hady, and identify the condition of intending to slaughter in the Haram.

Core Idea
Badana is specific to camels and cows; hady is broader, including sheep.

This passage begins a new sub-topic: how one can enter ihram by sending a sacrificial animal. The commentator clarifies the key terms 'badana' and 'hady', which are essential for understanding the rulings that follow. The distinction between the two matters because the term used affects how the animal is treated and whether a person is considered in ihram solely by sending it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Terms
Locate the terms 'badana' and 'hady' in the Arabic text. Note that the author defines badana as camels and cows, while hady includes these plus sheep.
The terms appear in the first sentence: 'man qallada badana' and then the commentary.
2
Understand the Scope of Each Term
Recognize that badana is a subset of hady. Not all hady is badana, but all badana is hady. This distinction affects which animals can be used for specific rites.
3
Note the Condition of Intention
The text states that for the term 'hady', one must intend to slaughter the animal in the Haram. Similarly, for 'badana', according to some scholars, the same intention is required. This condition is crucial for the validity of the act.
The phrase 'ويعتبر في إطلاق هذا اللفظ أن ينوي بذبحِهِ في الحرم' indicates the condition for hady; 'وكذا يعتبر ذلك في إطلاق البدنة عند بعضهم' shows the difference of opinion.
4
Apply the Definitions Practically
Consider a scenario: a person sends a camel and a sheep. The camel can be called badana (and hady), while the sheep is only hady. This has implications for the rules of ihram via sending (sawq al-hady).

[١] قوله : بَدَنَة؛ - بفتحات : هو الإبل والبقر، والهدي – بالفتح يشملها والغنم ويعتبر في إطلاق هذا اللفظ أن ينوي بذبحِهِ في الحرم، وكذا يعتبر ذلك في إطلاق البدنة عند بعضهم، كما بسطه محمد بن الحسن الله في «الموطأ»(۳)، وفصلته في تعليقاتي عليه.

This passage introduces a new topic: entering ihram by sending a sacrificial animal. The commentator defines 'badana' as camels and cows, while 'hady' is more general, including sheep. This ruling is important for understanding the actions of one who sends a sacrificial animal while remaining at home; such a person enters ihram by sending the animal, as will be explained.

Key Terms
بدنة (badana): A sacrificial animal from camels or cows; specifically used for the animal sent to the Haram for sacrifice.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal sent to the Haram, including camels, cows, and sheep.

Menstruation Does Not Prevent Hajj Rites Except Tawaf
Ruling that menstruation does not affect other Hajj rites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a menstruating woman may perform all Hajj rites except tawaf, and explain the proof from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
Menstruation prevents only tawaf; all other Hajj acts remain valid.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling regarding menstruation during Hajj. The text from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies that a menstruating woman may perform all rituals—standing at Arafah, sa'i, etc.—except tawaf. The primary proof is the Prophet's instruction to Aisha. We will also explore why the farewell tawaf is dropped if the obligatory tawaf has been performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is a menstruating woman's performance of Hajj rites. The ruling is that she may do all rites except tawaf.
The passage explicitly states: 'Her menstruation does not prevent any ritual act except tawaf.'
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith narrated by Muslim: the Prophet told Aisha, 'Do what the pilgrim does except do not perform tawaf.'
This is a hadith ahad, but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'افعلي' (do) indicates permissibility for all acts, and the exception 'غير أن لا تطوفي' (except do not perform tawaf) explicitly excludes only tawaf.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub, but here it is interpreted as permissibility because the context is a general permission for the pilgrim's acts.
4
Understand the consequence of tawaf al-ziyarah
If the woman performs the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-ziyarah) before menstruating or after purification, then the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr) is dropped. This is based on the hadith of one of the Prophet's wives who menstruated after performing tawaf al-ziyarah.
The passage says: 'after its two pillars, the farewell tawaf is dropped.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الإحرام
وحيضها لا يمنعُ نُسكاً إلا الطواف ، وهو بعد ركنيه يسقط طوافِ الصَّدَر

[١] قوله : لا يمنع نُسكاً ؛ - بضمتين : أي فعلاً من أفعال الحج، كالوقوف بعرفة وغيره لما روى مسلم وغيره : أن النبي الله قال لعائشة رضي الله عنها حين حاضت : افعلي ما يفعلُ الحاج غير أن لا تطوفي)). [٢] قوله : فإنّه في المسجد ؛ أي المسجد الحرام، هذا قاصر، فإنّها لو طافت من خارج المسجد أيضاً لم يجز ، فإنّ الطهارة من الجنابة شرط لنفس الطواف. [٣] قوله : يسقط ؛ لما روى أن بعض أزواج النبي يا حاضت أيام حجه فقال : «لعلها حابستنا)، ظناً منه أنها لم تطف طواف الزيارة، فقالوا : قد طافت معنا ، فقال : فلا إذن»، وهذه القصة مخرجة في «الصحاح».
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram. And her menstruation does not prevent any ritual act except tawaf, and after its two pillars, the farewell tawaf is dropped. [Commentary:] 'And her menstruation does not prevent any ritual act except tawaf, because it is in the mosque, and it is not permissible for a menstruating woman to enter it, and after its two pillars, the farewell tawaf is dropped': meaning menstruation after standing at Arafah, and the tawaf al-ziyarah drops the farewell. [1] His saying: 'does not prevent a ritual act' - with two dammas: meaning an action from the actions of Hajj, like standing at Arafah and others, because Muslim and others narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to Aisha, may God be pleased with her, when she menstruated: 'Do what the pilgrim does, except do not perform tawaf.' [2] His saying: 'because it is in the mosque' - meaning the Sacred Mosque, this is deficient, because even if she performed tawaf outside the mosque, it would not be permissible, since purity from major impurity is a condition for tawaf itself. [3] His saying: 'is dropped' - because it is narrated that one of the wives of the Prophet, peace be upon him, menstruated during the days of his Hajj, and he said: 'Perhaps she will detain us,' thinking that she had not performed tawaf al-ziyarah, and they said: 'She performed tawaf with us,' so he said: 'Then no.' And this story is recorded in the authentic books.
Source pages p. 593

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that menstruation only prevents tawaf, not any other Hajj act. The commentator explains that the prohibition of tawaf for a menstruating woman is because tawaf is performed in the mosque, and she cannot enter. However, the commentator notes that even if she were to perform tawaf outside the mosque, it would still be invalid because purification is a condition for tawaf itself. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet told Aisha to do all Hajj acts except tawaf. The passage also mentions that if a woman performs tawaf al-ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf), then the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr) is dropped. This is based on the hadith of one of the Prophet's wives who menstruated and had already performed tawaf al-ziyarah, so she was not required to do the farewell tawaf.

Key Terms
نسك (nusk): A ritual act of Hajj or Umrah, such as standing at Arafah, tawaf, sa'i, etc.
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed when leaving Mecca, also called tawaf al-wada'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Tawaf
C) Sa'i
D) Stoning the Jamarat

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman may perform all Hajj rites except tawaf; tawaf al-ziyarah must be performed after purification, and the farewell tawaf is dropped if she has performed tawaf al-ziyarah.

Sending a Sacrificial Animal and Becoming Muhrim – The Hanafi Distinction
Ruling on when sending a badanah necessitates ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the conditions for becoming muhrim when sending a badanah for tamattu' versus for nafal/nadhr, and state the ruling for each case.

Core Idea
For a tamattu' sacrifice, intention alone makes you muhrim; for others, you must physically catch up with the animal.

The Hanafi school teaches that becoming muhrim by sending a sacrificial animal depends on the type of sacrifice. The matn and sharh clarify that a sacrificial animal sent for tamattu' (or qiran) is itself a ritual of Hajj, so merely intending ihram while dispatching the animal suffices. In contrast, voluntary, vowed, or compensatory animals require the person to personally accompany or reach the animal for the ihram to take effect. This lesson unpacks this distinction and its legal basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Types of Sacrificial Animals
List the categories mentioned: nafal (voluntary), nadhr (vow), jaza' sayd (hunting compensation), and tamattu' (includes qiran). Note the terminology: badanah is camels/cows; hady includes sheep.
The term 'hady' is broader than 'badanah'.
2
Note the Common Condition
In all cases, the person must intend Hajj. However, the act of becoming muhrim is triggered differently.
Intention is a prerequisite for ihram.
3
Differentiate Tamattu' from Others
For tamattu', the animal is legislated as a ritual of Hajj itself. Therefore, merely proceeding (tawajjuh) with the intention of ihram makes one muhrim, even if not accompanying the animal. For others (nafal, nadhr, etc.), the animal is not inherently a Hajj ritual, so one does not become muhrim until physically catching up with it.
This is the core legal distinction.
4
Understand the Reasoning (Talil)
The commentary explains that the tamattu' sacrifice is a 'shukr' (thanksgiving) for combining two rituals in one journey, so it is placed as a Hajj ritual from the start. For other types, the animal is a separate obligation; thus, the intention must be connected to the action physically.
This talil justifies the different ruling.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Scenario
Example: A person sends a vowed badanah while staying home. He does not become muhrim until he travels and reaches the animal. Contrast with: if he sends a tamattu' animal, he becomes muhrim immediately upon intending ihram.
Practice distinguishing the two cases.

Source Text

[٤] قوله : بَدَنَة؛ - بفتحات : هو الإبل والبقر، والهدي – بالفتح يشملها والغنم ويعتبر في إطلاق هذا اللفظ أن ينوي بذبحِهِ في الحرم، وكذا يعتبر ذلك في إطلاق البدنة عند بعضهم، كما بسطه محمد بن الحسن الله في «الموطأ»، وفصلته في تعليقاتي عليه.
[١]قوله : نفل ؛ بأن يسوق بها طلباً لحصول الثواب.
أو نذر؛ بأن نذر عليه أن يذبح بدنة.

[٣]قوله : لمتعة ؛ - بالضم - : وهو التمتع ، والمراد به أعـم مـن التمتع الاصطلاحي، والقرآن، وسيجئ تفسيرهما وأحكامهما ، فإنّ في كل واحد منهما يجب الدم.
[٤]قوله : وتوجه ... الخ ؛ الفرق بين بدنة المتعة وبدنة النذر والتطوع وغيرهما : أن بدنة المتعة شرع ابتداءً نُسُكاً من مناسك الحج وضعاً، فإنّه مختص بمكة، واجب شكر للجمع بين أداء النسكين في سفر واحد، فاكتفى فيه في حصول الإحرام بالتوجه بنيّة الإحرام، وإن لم يذهب معها، بل بعثها أولاً ثم توجه، فيصير بمجرد التوجه محرماً بخلاف بدنة التطوع والنذر وغيرهما.
فإنّه إن بعث بهما ولم يسقها لم يصر محرماً ، فإن توجه بعد ذلك لا يصير محرماً بمجرد التوجه حتى يلحقها ، فإذا أدركها اقترنت نيته بالعمل، وهو من خصائص الإحرام، فيصير محرما. كذا في «الهداية).
Whoever garlands a badanah as a voluntary offering, or a vow, or a compensation for hunting, or similar, intending Hajj, or sends it for tamattu' and proceeds with the intention of ihram, then he has entered ihram. [4] His saying: 'badanah' - with fatha: it is camels and cows, and 'hady' - with fatha includes them and sheep, and it is considered in the usage of this term that he intends to slaughter it in the Haram, and likewise this is considered in the usage of 'badanah' according to some, as Muhammad ibn al-Hasan elaborated in al-Muwatta', and I have detailed it in my commentaries on it. [1] His saying: 'voluntary offering' - by driving it seeking reward. Or a vow: by vowing to slaughter a badanah. Or compensation for hunting: by killing it during ihram or in the Haram, so its value becomes obligatory, and he buys a badanah with that value. Or similar: like the blood required due to a violation during ihram. [2] His saying: 'due to the violation' - meaning committing what is prohibited in ihram that requires blood, and its detail will come, God willing. [3] His saying: 'for tamattu'' - with damm: it is tamattu', and what is meant is broader than the technical tamattu', and qiran, and their interpretation and rulings will come, because in each one, blood is required. [4] His saying: 'and proceeds... etc.' The difference between the badanah of tamattu' and the badanah of vow and voluntary offering and others: that the badanah of tamattu' is legislated from the beginning as a ritual from the rituals of Hajj by placement, because it is specific to Mecca, an obligatory thanksgiving for combining the performance of two rituals in one journey. So it sufficed in it for achieving ihram by proceeding with the intention of ihram, even if he does not go with it, but rather sends it first then proceeds, so he becomes muhrim by mere proceeding, contrary to the badanah of voluntary offering and vow and others. For if he sends them and does not drive them, he does not become a muhrim, and if he proceeds after that, he does not become a muhrim by mere proceeding until he catches up with them. So when he reaches them, his intention is connected with the action, and that is from the characteristics of ihram, so he becomes a muhrim. Thus in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 593

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on a person who sends a sacrificial animal (badanah) and the conditions that make him a muhrim. The matn states that if a person garlands a badanah—whether as a voluntary offering, a vowed animal, compensation for hunting, or similar—intending Hajj, or if he sends it for tamattu' and proceeds intending ihram, he becomes muhrim. The commentary clarifies the types: nafal (voluntary), nadhr (vow), jaza' sayd (hunting compensation), and similar (like other mandatory blood offerings). The word 'badanah' refers to camels and cows, while 'hady' includes sheep as well. The key distinction is between the badanah of tamattu' (and qiran) and others. For tamattu', the animal is a ritual of Hajj itself, so merely intending ihram while sending the animal suffices to make one muhrim, even if one does not accompany the animal. For other types (voluntary, vow, etc.), one does not become muhrim by mere intention; one must physically catch up with the animal and only then does the intention connect with the action, making one muhrim. This is a unique characteristic of ihram.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A sacrificial animal, specifically camels and cows but sometimes includes sheep.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal, including camels, cows, and sheep.
متعة (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first, then Hajj in the same year with a break, requiring a sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes tamattu' sacrifices from others: only the former triggers ihram by intention alone; others require physical accompaniment.

Becoming Muhrim by Sending a Sacrificial Animal: The Tamattu' Distinction
Commentary on when one becomes muhrim by sending a sacrificial animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when sending a badanah makes one muhrim, and distinguish between tamattu' and other types.

Core Idea
For tamattu', intention alone suffices; for other badanahs, physical conjunction is required.

The timing of assuming ihram for Hajj is critical. Sending a sacrificial animal ahead can trigger ihram, but the rules differ based on the purpose of the animal. This commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies when a mere intention suffices and when you must physically catch up to the animal.

Guided Path
1
List the types of badanah mentioned
Identify the categories: supererogatory (nafl), vowed (nadhr), penalty for hunting (jaza' sayd), and similar obligations (like blood for violations). Each has a specific cause.
The passage begins with these categories before contrasting them with tamattu'.
2
Understand the tamattu' exception
For a tamattu' badanah, the animal is itself a Hajj ritual (nusk). Therefore, merely intending ihram and proceeding (tawajjuh) toward it makes you muhrim, even if you don't physically travel with it.
This is a leniency because tamattu' requires thanks for combining 'Umrah and Hajj.
3
Apply the condition of physical conjunction for non-tamattu'
For nafl, nadhr, and similar badanahs, you do not become muhrim until you physically reach (tulhiq) the animal. Sending it ahead without accompanying it does not trigger ihram.
The intention becomes effective only when connected to the action of approaching the animal.
4
Note the madhhab difference on definition of badanah
In the Hanafi school, badanah includes both camels and cows. The Shafi'i school restricts it to camels only. The commentary affirms the Hanafi view with 'this is with us'.
This affects which animals can be used for the sacrifice and thus for triggering ihram.

(ولو أشعرها): أي شقّ سنامَها؛ ليعلَم أَنَّها هَدي، (أو جَلَّلها): أي ألقى الجُلَّ على ظهرها، أو قلد شاة لا، وكذا لو بعث بدنة، وتوجه حتى يُلحقها): أي إن لم يتوجه مع البدنة، ولم يسقها، بل بعثها لا يصير محرماً حتى يلحقها، فإذا لحقها يصير محرما. والبدن من الإبل والبقر): هذا عندنا، وأما عند الشَّافِعِي فالبدنةُ من الإبل فقط. قوله: أن يربط؛ كيفيته أن يفتل خيطاً من صوف أو شعر ويربط به قطعة نعل أو من جلد أو قشر شجرة ونحو ذلك، فيربطه في عنقها ليعلم أنه هدي، فلا يتعرض له أحد، ولا يأكل منه غني إذا عطب وذبح في الطريق. قوله: سنامها؛ - بالفتح -: ما ارتفع من ظهرِ البعير، بالفارسية: كوهان. قوله لا؛ الحاصل إنّ ما كان من خصائص الحج يصير به محرماً، والإشعار والتجليل وتقليد الشاةِ ليس كذلك، فلا يصير محرماً بخلاف تقليد البدنة.
Optional, or supererogatory, or a penalty for hunting, or similar: he intends Hajj, or he sends it for tamattu' and proceeds with the intention of ihram, then he has entered ihram. Optional, or supererogatory, or a penalty for hunting, or similar: like blood required due to an offense in the past year, (he intends Hajj, or he sends it for tamattu'): meaning he sends the sacrificial camel for tamattu', and proceeds with the intention of ihram, then he has entered ihram. His statement: 'optional'—by driving it seeking reward. Or 'vowed'—by vowing to slaughter a sacrificial camel. Or 'penalty for hunting'—by killing it in ihram or the sanctuary, so its value becomes obligatory, and he buys a sacrificial camel with that value. Or similar: like the blood required due to an offense during the state of ihram. His statement: 'due to an offense'—meaning committing what is prohibited in ihram for which blood is required, and its detail will come if Allah wills. His statement: 'for tamattu''—with a damma—and it is tamattu', and what is meant is general, including terminological tamattu' and qiran, and their interpretations and rulings will come, for in each one blood is required. His statement: 'and proceeds... etc.'—the difference between the sacrificial camel of tamattu' and the sacrificial camel of a vow and supererogatory and others: the tamattu' sacrificial camel is legislated initially as a ritual from the rites of Hajj by placement, for it is specific to Mecca, obligatory as thanks for combining two rites in one journey, so he suffices in obtaining ihram by proceeding with the intention of ihram, even if he does not go with it, but rather sends it first then proceeds, so he becomes muhrim merely by proceeding, unlike the supererogatory and vowed sacrificial camel and others. For he, if he sends them and does not drive them, does not become muhrim, and if he proceeds afterwards, he does not become muhrim merely by proceeding until he catches up to it, and when he reaches it his intention becomes connected with the action, and this is from the characteristics of ihram, so he becomes muhrim. As in al-Hidayah. His statement: 'then he has entered ihram'—meaning he becomes muhrim, so it is obligatory upon him to remove stitched garments and avoid its prohibitions. And if he marks it or covers it or puts a necklace on a sheep, no, and likewise if he sends a sacrificial camel and proceeds until he catches up to it. And the sacrificial camels are from camels and cows. The meaning of taqlid is to tie a necklace on the neck of the sacrificial camel, and by it he becomes muhrim as by talbiyah. (And if he marks it): meaning he splits its hump; so that it is known it is a sacrificial animal, (or covers it): meaning he throws a cloth on its back, or put a necklace on a sheep, no, and likewise if he sends a sacrificial camel and proceeds until he catches up to it): meaning if he does not proceed with the sacrificial camel and does not drive it, but rather sends it, he does not become muhrim until he catches up to it, and when he catches up to it he becomes muhrim. And the sacrificial camels are from camels and cows: this is with us, and with al-Shafi'i the sacrificial camel is only from camels. His statement: 'to tie'; its manner: he twists a thread from wool or hair and ties with it a piece of sandal or leather or tree bark and the like, and ties it on its neck to know that it is a sacrificial animal, so that no one interferes with it, and no rich person eats from it if it perishes and is slaughtered on the way. His statement: 'its hump'; with a fatha: what is raised from the back of the camel, in Persian: kuhan. His statement: 'no'; the conclusion: whatever is from the characteristics of Hajj makes him muhrim by it, and marking, covering, and putting a necklace on a sheep are not so, so one does not become muhrim by them, unlike putting a necklace on a sacrificial camel.
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah, explaining the ruling on when a person becomes muhrim (consecrated for Hajj) by sending a sacrificial animal (badanah). The commentator begins by listing the categories of sacrificial animals that, when sent with the intention of Hajj or tamattu', and the person proceeds with the intention of ihram, result in becoming muhrim: these include supererogatory (nafl), vowed (nadhr), penalty for hunting (jaza' sayd), or similar obligations. The commentary elaborates on each: nafl is seeking reward by driving the animal; nadhr is a vow to slaughter a badanah; jaza' sayd is when one kills game during ihram or in the Haram, requiring payment of its value with which a badanah is purchased; and 'similar' includes blood due for other ihram violations. The key distinction is between the badanah of tamattu' and other types. For tamattu', since the badanah is itself a Hajj ritual specially legislated for combining 'Umrah and Hajj, one becomes muhrim merely by intending (proceeding) towards it, even without physically accompanying it. In contrast, for supererogatory or vowed badanahs, one does not become muhrim by merely sending it ahead; one becomes muhrim only upon physically reaching it and connecting intention with action. The passage then discusses that acts like ish'ar (marking the hump with a slit), tajlil (covering with a cloth), or taqlid (putting a necklace) on a sheep do not make one muhrim, but taqlid of a badanah does, because it is a characteristic of Hajj. Finally, a madhhab difference is noted: in the Hanafi school, badanah refers to both camels and cows, whereas in the Shafi'i school, it is only camels. The commentary provides details on the manner of taqlid and explains that ish'ar and tajlil are not effective for becoming muhrim.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A sacrificial animal sent to the Haram for Hajj rituals; in this passage, specifically a camel or cow offered for tamattu' or other purposes.
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, initiated by intention (niyyah) and talbiyah, requiring abstention from prohibitions.
تقليد (taqlid): The act of putting a necklace on a sacrificial animal to mark it as a hadiy; doing so on a badanah makes one muhrim in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical difference in the Hanafi school between sending a tamattu' badanah and a vowed (nadhr) badanah regarding when one becomes muhrim?
A) For both, one becomes muhrim upon sending the animal.
B) For tamattu', one becomes muhrim immediately upon proceeding with intention; for vows, only upon reaching the animal.
C) For both, one becomes muhrim only upon reaching the animal.
D) For tamattu', one becomes muhrim only after slaughtering the animal; for vows, upon sending.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the type of sacrificial animal determines the moment of ihram: tamattu' badanah triggers ihram by intention alone, while other types require physical connection.

Actions That Enter One into Ihram: Talbiyah and Taqlid
Ruling on what actions make one a muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which actions, according to the Hanafi school, cause a person to become a muhrim, and distinguish effective actions (talbiyah, taqlid of badanah) from ineffective ones (ish'ar, tajlil, taqlid of sheep).

Core Idea
Only talbiyah and taqlid of a camel or cow make one a muhrim; marking or covering the animal does not.

In this lesson, we examine the specific actions that establish the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah. The text clarifies that mere intention or preparation is insufficient; a defined action—talbiyah or taqlid of a sacrificial animal—is required. We will also see which actions, such as marking or covering the animal, have no effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions considered
List the actions mentioned: talbiyah, taqlid, ish'ar, tajlil, and sending a badanah.
2
Classify each action as effective or ineffective
Determine which actions cause one to become a muhrim. Talbiyah and taqlid of a camel/cow are effective; ish'ar, tajlil, and taqlid of a sheep are not.
Taqlid is equated to talbiyah in effect.
3
Examine the sent badanah scenario
If one sends a badanah without accompanying it, one becomes a muhrim only upon catching up to the animal.
The condition is that one must physically meet the animal.
4
Understand the basis
The text indicates that taqlid is like talbiyah—a verbal or symbolic act that initiates ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : فقد أحرم ؛ أي صار محرماً ، فيجب عليه التجرد من المخيط ، والاجتناب عن محظوراته. ولو أشعرَها أو جَلَّلَها أو قلّد شاة لا ، وكذا لو بعث بدنة، وتوجه حتى يُلحقها والبدن من الإبل والبقر المراد بالتلقيد : أن يربط قلادة على عُنُق البَدَنة ، فيصير به مُحرماً كما بالتلبية ( ولو أشعرها) : أي شقّ سنامَها ؛ ليعلَم أَنَّها هَدي ، (أو جَلَّلها) : أي ألقى الجُلَّ على ظهرها ، أو قلد شاة لا ، وكذا لو بعث بدنة، وتوجه حتى يُلحقها) : أي إن لم يتوجه مع البدنة، ولم يسقها، بل بعثها لا يصير محرماً حتى يلحقها ، فإذا لحقها يصير محرما. والبدن من الإبل والبقر ) : هذا عندنا ، وأما عند الشَّافِعِي ) فالبدنةُ من الإبل فقط.
His statement: 'So he has entered ihram' means he has become a muhrim, so it is obligatory upon him to remove sewn garments and avoid its prohibitions. And if he marked it (the animal) by cutting its hump, or covered it, or tied a necklace on a sheep, no (he does not become a muhrim). Likewise, if he sent a badanah and proceeded until he caught up to it. And badanah is from camels and cows. The meaning of taqlid is to tie a necklace on the neck of the badanah, by which he becomes a muhrim just as by talbiyah. (And if he marked it) means he cut its hump so that it is known as a sacrificial animal. (Or covered it) means he placed a covering on its back. Or tied a necklace on a sheep, no. Likewise, if he sent a badanah and proceeded until he caught up to it means: if he did not go with the badanah nor drive it but sent it, he does not become a muhrim until he catches up to it; when he catches up to it, he becomes a muhrim. (And badanah is from camels and cows): this is according to us; as for according to al-Shafi'i, badanah is only from camels.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the actions that cause one to enter the state of ihram and the definition of badanah. The commentator explains that becoming a muhrim requires either uttering talbiyah or performing taqlid on a badanah (camel or cow). Actions like ish'ar (marking by cutting the hump), tajlil (covering the animal's back), or taqlid of a sheep do not effect ihram. If one sends a badanah without accompanying it, one becomes a muhrim only upon catching up to it. The Hanafi position defines badanah as both camels and cows, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it to camels alone. The practical consequence is that according to Hanafis, sending a cow as a badanah can initiate ihram via taqlid, whereas Shafi'is would not recognize this.

Key Terms
تلقيد (taqlid): Tying a necklace (of wool, leather, etc.) around the neck of a sacrificial animal to mark it as hady.
إشعار (ish'ar): Cutting the hump of a camel to mark it as a sacrificial animal.
تجلين (tajlil): Placing a covering on the back of a sacrificial animal.
بدنة (badanah): A sacrificial animal; according to Hanafis, includes camels and cows; according to Shafi'is, only camels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following actions does NOT make one a muhrim?
A) Talbiyah
B) Taqlid of a camel
C) Ish'ar (cutting hump)
D) Catching up to a sent badanah

Key Takeaway
Only talbiyah and taqlid of a camel or cow establish ihram; marking, covering, or taqlid of a sheep do not.

Defining Badanah: Hanafi vs Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on the definition of badanah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of badanah (camels and cows) and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute with al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Hanafis include cows as badanah; Shafi'is restrict it to camels, affecting when taqlid initiates ihram.

The term badanah in the context of sacrificial animals is a point of disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. While both agree that taqlid of a badanah makes one a muhrim, they differ on which animals qualify. This lesson examines the dispute and its tangible effect on ihram rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested term
The term 'badanah' is defined differently: Hanafis include camels and cows; Shafi'is limit to camels.
2
State the Hanafi position
The text says 'والبدن من الإبل والبقر' – badanah is from camels and cows.
This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
3
State the Shafi'i position
The text notes that according to al-Shafi'i, badanah is only from camels.
No further evidence is given in the passage.
4
Analyze the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a person sends a cow with taqlid, a Hanafi considers him a muhrim upon catching up; a Shafi'i would not, because a cow is not a badanah in his school.
This difference directly impacts the timing of ihram obligations.

Superiority and Definition of Qiran in Hanafi Fiqh
States the superiority and definition of Qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the superiority of Qiran, define Qiran, and explain its conditions and evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Qiran is the best form of Hajj because the Prophet ﷺ performed it, and it means combining Hajj and Umrah from the Miqat.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary establishes the superiority of Qiran over Tamattu’ and Ifrad. It provides a precise definition of Qiran, including the restriction that it applies only to those coming from outside Mecca (Afaqi). The commentator also clarifies that one can become a Qarin by adding Hajj to Umrah (or vice versa) after initially entering Ihram for one, as long as the addition occurs before the rituals of the first begin. The evidence is a hadith from Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's actions in the Farewell Pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position that Qiran is absolutely better (afdal mutlaqan) than Tamattu' and Ifrad.
The text says 'القران أفضل مطلقاً'.
2
Define the act of Qiran
Explain what Qiran is: entering Ihram for both Hajj and Umrah from the Miqat, either simultaneously or sequentially before starting the rituals of the first.
The commentary allows adding the second later.
3
Note the condition of being an Afaqi
Recognize that only an Afaqi (non-Meccan) can perform Qiran; Meccans cannot combine.
The restriction 'من الميقات' implies the pilgrim must come from outside the Miqat.
4
Locate the evidence
Find the hadith of Ibn Umar and understand how the Hanafi school uses it to prove Qiran's superiority.
The hadith is cited from Sahih Muslim and Sahih Bukhari.
5
Address potential confusion
Clarify that one can still be a Qarin even if they enter Ihram for one first and then add the other, as per the commentary.
The commentary says: 'if he assumed Ihram from the Miqat for one of them, then entered the other upon it and combined both, he would also be a Qarin.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القرآن والتمتع
القران أفضلُ مطلقاً وهو أن يُهل بحج وعمرة من الميقات معاً
[1] أي أفضلُ من التَّمتع والإفراد، (وهو أن يُهل بحج وعمرة من الميقات معاً) : الإهلالُ رفعُ الصَّوتِ بالتلبية
[2] قوله : وهو أن يهل؛ هو معناه الشرعي، ولغة : هو الجمع بين الشيئين.
[3] قوله : من الميقات؛ هذا القيد للإشارة إلى أنّ القارن وكذا المتمتع لا يكون إلا آفاقياً، والمكي لا تمتع له ولا قرآن وليس المراد به دخوله في مفهوم القران ، فإنه لو أحرم من الميقات بأحدهما ثم أدخل الآخرَ عليه وجمع بينهما يكون قارناً أيضاً. كذا في «البحر».
(۱) فعن ابن عمر : تمتع رسول الله الله في حجة الوداع بالعمرة إلى الحج وأهدى فساق معه الهدي من ذي الحليفة وبدأ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فأهل بالعمرة ثم أهل بالحج وتمتع الناس مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالعمرة إلى الحج ، فكان من الناس من أهدى فساق الهدي ، ومنهم من لم يهد فلما قدم رسول الله الله مكة قال للناس : مَن كان منكم أهدى فإنه لا يحل من شيء حرم . يقضي حجه، ،، ومن لم يكن منكم أهدى فليطف بالبيت وبالصفا والمروة وليقصر وليحلل ثم ليهل بالحج وليهد...» في (صحيح مسلم (۲) : ٦٠١) ، و (صحيح البخاري (٢ : ٦٠٧) ، وغيرهما.
(۲) (زاد المعاد»(ص۱۰۲).
(۳) (البحر الرائق (۲) : ٣٨٥)
منه
حتى
Chapter of Qiran and Tamattu'. Qiran is absolutely better, and it is to raise the voice (i.e., enter into Ihram) for Hajj and Umrah from the Miqat together. [1] That is, better than Tamattu' and Ifrad. (And it is to raise voice for Hajj and Umrah from the Miqat together): Ihlal is raising the voice with Talbiyah. [2] His saying: 'and it is to raise voice' is its legal meaning; linguistically it is the joining of two things. [3] His saying: 'from the Miqat' – this restriction indicates that the Qarin, and likewise the Mutamatti', cannot be except an Afaqi (one coming from outside Mecca), and the Meccan has no Tamattu' or Qiran, and the intent is not to include it in the concept of Qiran, for if he assumed Ihram from the Miqat for one of them, then entered the other upon it and combined both, he would also be a Qarin. Thus in 'al-Bahr'. (1) From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah performed Tamattu' in the Farewell Pilgrimage with Umrah to Hajj and brought the sacrificial animal and drove it with him from Dhul Hulaifa, and the Messenger of Allah began and performed Ihlal for Umrah, then performed Ihlal for Hajj, and the people performed Tamattu' with the Messenger of Allah with Umrah to Hajj...
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of Qiran and Tamattu' from a Hanafi fiqh work. It begins by stating the ruling that Qiran is absolutely superior to Tamattu' and Ifrad. The commentator explains that the Prophet's practice in the Farewell Pilgrimage is the basis for this preference, and despite differing reports, the preferred opinion is that he performed Qiran. The definition of Qiran is given: it is to enter Ihram for both Hajj and Umrah simultaneously from the Miqat, with the act of Ihlal (raising the voice with Talbiyah). The commentator then clarifies that the term 'Ihlal' legally means raising the voice, while linguistically 'Qiran' means combining. A key point is that the restriction 'from the Miqat' indicates that only those coming from outside Mecca (Afaqi) can perform Qiran or Tamattu'; residents of Mecca cannot. However, if someone initiates Ihram for one from the Miqat and then adds the other later, they still become a Qarin. The footnote provides the hadith evidence from Sahih Muslim and Sahih Bukhari showing the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
القران (al-qirān): The type of Hajj where one enters Ihram for both Hajj and Umrah together from the Miqat, or enters for one and then adds the other before beginning the rituals of the first.
التمتع (al-tamattu‘): A type of Hajj where one performs Umrah first (during the Hajj season), then exits Ihram, and later enters Ihram for Hajj from Mecca.
الإهلال (al-ihlāl): Literally raising the voice; technically, it means entering the state of Ihram by reciting the Talbiyah.
الميقات (al-mīqāt): The designated station where pilgrims intending Hajj or Umrah must enter Ihram; for Qiran, the Ihram for both must be entered from the Miqat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The pilgrim must be a resident of Mecca.
B) The Ihram for both must be entered from the Miqat.
C) The pilgrim must perform Umrah first.
D) The pilgrim must sacrifice a camel.

Key Takeaway
Qiran is the most excellent form of Hajj, defined as combining Hajj and Umrah from the Miqat, and it is supported by the Prophet's example.

Qiran and Tamattu': Sequence, Sacrifice, and Invalidating Conditions
Sharh on qiran/tamattu' with proofs and rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid qiran/tamattu', explain why a separate tawaf and sa'y for each is makruh, and apply the ruling on dam and fasting when unable to sacrifice.

Core Idea
In qiran, a single tawaf and sa'y suffices; separating them is makruh, and dam is wajib as gratitude.

This passage from the sharh of al-Wiqayah delves into the practical details of performing qiran and tamattu'. It clarifies that the recommended supplication after the ihram prayer is a juristic recommendation, not a required part of the ritual. More critically, it explains the correct sequence of actions, the ruling on performing multiple tawafs, and the obligation of the sacrificial animal. Understanding these points ensures that the pilgrim avoids makruh acts and fulfills the wajib of dam correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
First, recognise that the passage discusses qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) and tamattu' (Umrah followed by Hajj separately). The focus is on the sequence of tawaf, sa'y, and the obligation of dam.
Qiran and tamattu' are both valid forms of Hajj, but they have different fiqh rulings.
2
Analyse the rulings on supplication and tawaf
The passage begins by noting the du'a said after the two rak'ahs of ihram. It explains that this is not from the sunnah but a juristic recommendation (istihsan) to align heart and tongue. Then, for the qarin, a single tawaf and sa'y is the norm. Performing two separate tawafs and two sa'ys is makruh because it delays the Umrah.
The dislike is due to contradicting the ideal sequence.
3
Examine the obligation of dam
The passage cites the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:196) to establish that a sacrificial animal (dam) is wajib for tamattu' and qiran as gratitude. If unable, fasting three days during Hajj (the last being Arafah) and seven days after returning home is an alternative. If the three days are missed before the Day of Sacrifice, the dam becomes mandatory again.
The dam is a distinct category of wajib, not a sunnah.
4
Determine the invalidity of Umrah when standing at Arafat prematurely
A critical ruling: if a qarin stands at Arafat before completing the Umrah (specifically, before performing most of its tawaf, i.e., less than four circuits), the Umrah becomes invalid because the sequence of actions cannot be maintained. However, if four or more circuits have been completed, the Umrah remains valid and is completed on the Day of Sacrifice.
This shows the importance of the order of rites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقول بعد الصلاة : اللهم إني أريدُ الحج والعمرة فَيَسِّرْهُما لي، وتقبلهما منّي . وطاف للعمرة سبعةً يرْمُلُ للثلاثة الأول، ويسعى بلا حَلْق ، ثُمَّ يحج كما مَرَّ ، فإن أتى بطوافين وسعيين لهما كره . ويقول بعد الصلاة : أي بعد الشفع الذي يصلي مريدا للإحرام: اللَّهُمَّ إنِّي أريدُ الحج والعمرة فيسرْهُما لي، وتقبلهما مني. وطاف للعمرة سبعة يرْمُلُ للثلاثة الأول، ويسعى بلا حَلْق، ثم يحج كما مر، فإن أتى بطوافين وسعيين لهما كره : أي يطوفُ أربعة عشر شوطاً ، سبعة للعمرة، وسبعة لطواف القدوم للحج ، ثُمَّ يسعى لهما، وإنما كره ؛ لأنَّه أَخَّرَ العمرة، وقَدَّمَ طواف القدوم. [١]قوله : ويقول ; هو بالرفع، جملة على حدة، لا بالنصب ; ليكون عطفاً . على يهل، فإنّ القول بهذا ليس داخلاً في حد القران، بل التلفظ بهذا الدعاء في القرآن، وكذا في الإفراد والتمتع لم يرد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، وإنما المنقولُ الاكتفاء بالنية القلبية مع التلبية، وهي : لبيك بحج في الإفراد، وبعمرة في التمتع ، وبحج وعمرة في القرآن، وإنما هو شيء استحسنه الفقهاء ليجتمع القلـب واللسان. [٢] قوله : ويقول ; وكذلك يجمعُ بينهما في التلبية، فيقول : لبيك بحجة وعمرة، كما ثبت عن النبي عند البخاري وغيره. [٣] قوله : بعد الشفع ; أي بعد الركعتين اللتين يصليهما عند إرادة الإحرام. [٤] قوله : بلا حلق ; أي لا يحلق رأسه ولا يقصر ولا يرتكب شيئاً من محظورات الإحرام بعد الفراغ من طواف العمرة وسعيها ; لأنه لم يتحلل من الإحرام بعد. [0] قوله : ثم يحج ; اي يسكن بمكة محرماً ، ويحجّ في أوانه على الصفة التي مرّت ، ويتحلّل بعد الفراغ منه. [٦] قوله : فإن أتي ... الخ ; قال في «اللباب» و «شرحه(۲) : لو طاف طوافين ; أي متواليين متقدمين، وسعى سعيين : أي متأخرين متتابعين، أو متعاقبين، وكذا الحكمُ فيهما إذا كانا مُرتبين للعمرة والحج : أي اجمالاً ولم ينو الأول : أي من الطوافين لعمرة، والثاني للحج، أو نوى على العكس : بأن نوى الأول للقدوم، والثاني للعمرة، أو نوى مطلق الطواف فيهما، ولم يُعين فيه يكون الأول للعمرة، والثاني للقدوم، وكره له ذلك ; أي ذلك لمخالفته السنة من وجوه كثيرة. وذَبَحَ للقران بعد رمي يوم النحر ، وإن عَجَزَ صام ثلاثة أيام آخرها عرفة ، وسبعة بعد حجه أين شاء، فإن فاتت الثلاثة تعين الدم، فإن وقف قبل العمرة بطلت وذَبَحَ للقران بعد رمي يوم النحر، وإن عَجَزَ صام ثلاثة أيام آخرها عرفة، وسبعة بعد حجّهِ أين شاء ) : أي بعد أيام التشريق، فإن فاتت الثلاثة) تعين الدم. فإن وقف قبل العمرة بطلت) : أي العمرة متواليين متقدمين، وسعى سعيين : أي متأخرين متتابعين، أو متعاقبين، وكذا الحكمُ فيهما إذا كانا مُرتبين للعمرة والحج : أي اجمالاً ولم ينو الأول : أي من الطوافين لعمرة، والثاني للحج، أو نوى على العكس : بأن نوى الأول للقدوم، والثاني للعمرة، أو نوى مطلق الطواف فيهما، ولم يُعين فيه يكون الأول للعمرة، والثاني للقدوم، وكره له ذلك ; أي ذلك لمخالفته السنة من وجوه كثيرة. [1] قوله : وذبح ; أي شاة أو بقرة أو بدنة أو سبعاً منهما، وهذا دم الشكر يجب في التمتع والقران، شكراً لِمَا وفقه الله للمنسكين في سفر واحد ، لقوله : فَمَن تَمَنَّعَ بالعمرة إلى الحج فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدَى فَمَن لَّمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَج وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ ) [٢) قوله : آخرها عرفة ; أي يصومُ اليوم السابع والثامن والتاسع من ذي الحجة ، وهذا على الندب، ويجوز أن يصوم قبل ذلك مجتمعاً أو متفرّقاً ولا يؤخِّرَ عن يوم النحر. ٣١) قوله : أي بعد أيام التشريق ; فإنّ الصوم فيها وكذا في يوم النحر ممنوع مطلقاً. [٤]قوله : فإن فاتت الثلاثة ; أي الأول بدخول يوم النحر. [0]قوله : تعين الدم; لأنّ الصوم كان بدلاً عنه، ووقته قبل يوم النحر، فعند فوته عاد وجوب الأصل. [٦] قوله : فإن وقف...الخ ; يعني أنّ القارنَ إن لم يفرغ من أفعال العمرة ووقف بعرفات بعد الزوال قبلها، بطلت عمرته ; لتعذر أدائها عليه ; لأنه لا يصير بانياً أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج، وهذا إذا كان الوقوف قبل أكثر طواف العمرة، فإن طاف لها أربعة أشواط ثم وقف لم تبطل، بل يتمها يوم النحر. كذا في «البحر»).
And he says after the prayer: O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah, so make them easy for me and accept them from me. And he performs seven circuits for Umrah, trotting in the first three, and performs the sa'y without shaving, then he performs Hajj as mentioned. If he performs two tawafs and two sa'ys for them, it is disliked. And he says after the prayer: after the two rak'ahs which he prays intending to enter into ihram: O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah, so make them easy for me and accept them from me. And he performs seven circuits for Umrah, trotting in the first three, and performs the sa'y without shaving, then he performs Hajj as mentioned. If he performs two tawafs and two sa'ys for them, it is disliked: i.e., he performs fourteen circuits, seven for Umrah and seven for the arrival tawaf for Hajj, then he performs two sa'ys. It is disliked because he delayed the Umrah and advanced the arrival tawaf. [1] His saying: 'And he says': it is in the nominative, a separate sentence, not in the accusative to be a conjunction with 'he raises the voice', because saying this is not part of the definition of qiran. Rather, uttering this supplication in qiran, and similarly in ifrad and tamattu', is not reported from the Prophet, his family, and his companions. What is transmitted is sufficing with the intention of the heart along with the talbiyah, which is: 'Labbayk bi-Hajj' in ifrad, 'bi-Umrah' in tamattu', and 'bi-Hajj wa- Umrah' in qiran. This is something the jurists considered good so that the heart and tongue come together. [2] His saying: 'And he says': likewise, he combines between them in the talbiyah, saying: 'Labbayk bi-Hajjah wa- Umrah,' as established from the Prophet in al-Bukhari and others. [3] His saying: 'after the shaf': i.e., after the two rak'ahs which he prays when intending to enter ihram. [4] His saying: 'without shaving': i.e., he does not shave his head nor does he shorten his hair nor does he commit any of the prohibitions of ihram after completing the tawaf and sa'y of Umrah, because he has not yet become free from ihram. [5] His saying: 'then he performs Hajj': i.e., he resides in Mecca as a muhrim, and performs Hajj at its proper time in the manner that has passed, and becomes free after completing it. [6] His saying: 'If he performs...' etc. He said in al-Lubab and its commentary: If he performs two tawafs — i.e., two successive ones occurring early — and two sa'ys — i.e., two late ones following one another or alternating — the ruling is the same when they are arranged for Umrah and Hajj: i.e., in summary without specifying, and he did not intend the first of the two tawafs for Umrah and the second for Hajj, or he intended the opposite: that he intended the first for arrival and the second for Umrah, or he intended absolute tawaf in both without specifying, then the first is for Umrah and the second for arrival, and this is disliked for him; i.e., because it contradicts the sunnah in many ways. And he slaughters for qiran after the stoning on the Day of Sacrifice, and if he is unable, he fasts three days whose last is the Day of Arafah, and seven days after his Hajj wherever he wishes. If the three days are missed, the blood sacrifice becomes incumbent. And if he stands at Arafat before the Umrah, it becomes invalid. [1] His saying: 'And he slaughters': i.e., a sheep, a cow, a camel, or a seventh share of either. This is the blood sacrifice of thanksgiving required in tamattu' and qiran, as gratitude for what Allah enabled him of two acts of worship in one journey, due to His saying: 'Whoever performs tamattu' with Umrah to Hajj, then what is easy of sacrificial animals. Whoever does not find, then fasting three days in Hajj and seven when you have returned.' [2] His saying: 'whose last is the Day of Arafah': i.e., he fasts the seventh, eighth, and ninth of Dhu al-Hijjah. This is recommended, and it is permissible to fast before that consecutively or intermittently, and not to delay beyond the Day of Sacrifice. [3] His saying: 'i.e., after the days of Tashriq': for fasting on those days and likewise on the Day of Sacrifice is absolutely prohibited. [4] His saying: 'If the three days are missed': i.e., the first (of them) by the entry of the Day of Sacrifice. [5] His saying: 'the blood sacrifice becomes incumbent': because fasting was a substitute for it, and its time was before the Day of Sacrifice, so when it is missed, the obligation of the original returns. [6] His saying: 'If he stands...' etc.: meaning that if the qarin does not complete the actions of Umrah and stands at Arafat after noon before it, his Umrah becomes invalid because performing it becomes impossible for him, as he cannot make the actions of Umrah follow those of Hajj. This is if the standing occurs before most of the tawaf of Umrah. If he performed four circuits for it then stood, it does not become invalid, rather he completes it on the Day of Sacrifice. Thus in al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rulings of qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah) and tamattu' (performing Umrah first and then Hajj). It begins by discussing the recommended supplication after the two rak'ahs of the ihram prayer. The commentator clarifies that saying this dua is not a required part of qiran but is a juristic recommendation (istihsan) to unite intention and speech. It then explains that in qiran, the pilgrim should make a single tawaf and sa'y for both, and that performing two separate tawafs and sa'ys (one for each) is disliked (makruh) because it delays the Umrah, contradicting the ideal sequence. The passage then addresses the obligation of a sacrificial animal (dam) for qiran and tamattu', citing the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:196). If the pilgrim cannot afford the animal, they must fast three days during Hajj (the last being Arafah) and seven days after returning home. If they miss the three days before the Day of Sacrifice, the dam becomes obligatory again. Finally, the passage addresses a critical rule: if a qarin stands at Arafat before completing the Umrah (most of the tawaf), the Umrah is invalidated because the actions cannot be properly sequenced. However, if they have performed four circuits, the Umrah remains valid and can be completed on the Day of Sacrifice.

Key Terms
قران (qiran): The combining of Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram with the intention of performing both together.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah in the months of Hajj and then exiting ihram, then performing Hajj separately later in the same year.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep, cow, or camel) required as compensation or thanksgiving in certain Hajj contexts.
شرع (shaf): Two rak'ahs of the ihram prayer before intending the Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a qarin (one performing qiran) stands at Arafat after noon before completing the Umrah tawaf, when is the Umrah invalidated?
A) It is always invalidated regardless of how many circuits were completed.
B) It is invalidated only if less than four circuits of tawaf were performed.
C) It is invalidated if the pilgrim had not yet performed sa'y.
D) It is never invalidated; the Umrah can be completed after Hajj.

Key Takeaway
For a valid qiran or tamattu', perform a single tawaf and sa'y, offer the dam (or fast if unable), and ensure Umrah tawaf is mostly complete before standing at Arafat.

Rulings on the Qiran: Sacrifice, Fasting, and Invalidation of Umrah
Commentary on Qiran Hajj rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the primary obligation for the Qarin (dam al-shukr or fasting) and explain the ruling when the Qarin stands at Arafah before completing Umrah.

Core Idea
The Qarin must sacrifice or fast; if he stands at Arafah before finishing Umrah, his Umrah is invalid and requires qada and a penalty sacrifice.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the rulings for the Qarin who combines Umrah and Hajj. We learn the primary obligation of sacrifice (dam al-shukr) and the alternative of fasting, as well as the consequences of performing the standing at Arafah before completing the Umrah rituals. The commentary clarifies timing, missed fasts, and the threshold (four tawaf circuits) that saves the Umrah from invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary obligation
State that the Qarin must sacrifice an animal (dam al-shukr) as gratitude. If unable, fasting is wajib. Note the Quranic evidence (2:196).
2
Understand the fasting alternative
The fast is three days during Hajj (last day Arafah) and seven after returning. If the three days are missed (by day of Nahr), the obligation shifts back to sacrifice.
Fasting on day of Nahr and days of Tashriq is prohibited.
3
Recognize the condition for invalidating Umrah
If the Qarin stands at Arafah before completing Umrah actions, his Umrah becomes invalid because he cannot build Umrah upon Hajj.
4
Determine the threshold (four circuits)
If the Qarin has performed four or more circuits of tawaf for Umrah before standing, the Umrah is not invalidated; he completes it on the day of Nahr.
Less than four circuits triggers invalidation.
5
Identify consequences of invalidation
When Umrah is invalidated, the Qarin must make it up (qada) and sacrifice a dam al-rafd (for abandoning the Umrah). The dam al-qiran drops.
Umrah becomes obligatory upon commencement (shuru').

Source Text
