The Ruling on Ish'ar and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining Abu Hanifa's dislike and the Sahibayn's permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar and state the mufta bihi position on the ruling.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa disliked ish'ar for unskilled people; the relied-upon position is permissibility when done correctly.

Ish'ar is the practice of marking the sacrificial animal (hadi) with a small cut to indicate it is for sacrifice. Within the Hanafi school, there is an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa considered it makruh tahriman for those who might overdo it, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, held it to be absolutely permissible (ja'iz). Later Hanafi authorities reconciled the two views and adopted the disciples' position as the operative ruling for fatwa, provided the cut is limited to the skin and does not cause unnecessary harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling according to each imam
State what ish'ar is. Then note that Abu Hanifa ruled it makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked) for unskilled people, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) ruled it permissible (ja'iz) absolutely.
The dispute is not about the permissibility in principle, but about the degree of dislike for certain people.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's justification
Abu Hanifa argued that ish'ar can be a form of mutilation (mutlah) if done excessively. He disliked it for unskilled individuals who might cut too deeply, causing harm or death to the animal.
The Prophet performed ish'ar, but Abu Hanifa interpreted that as a special necessity because the polytheists would otherwise attack the animals.
3
Examine the reconciliation by later scholars
Commentators like al-Tahawi and al-Maturidi explained that Abu Hanifa did not reject the Sunnah; he only disliked the practice as performed by the common people of his time who exaggerated the cut. They restricted his dislike to unskilled practitioners.
This interpretation preserves both the Sunnah and Abu Hanifa's concern.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later authorities such as Ibn al-Humam and al-Haskafi adopted the Sahibayn's view as the relied-upon position. The mufta bihi is that ish'ar is permissible (ja'iz) when done properly by cutting only the skin.
Thus, the practical fatwa follows the Sahibayn, but the caution of Abu Hanifa remains relevant for unqualified individuals.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on ish'ar (marking the sacrificial animal by making a cut or wound). The base matn from Al-Hidayah likely stated that Abu Hanifa disliked it. The commentator explains that Abu Hanifa disliked the practice because it constitutes mutilation (mutlah), cutting a limb while the animal is alive. However, the Prophet himself performed ish'ar, as the polytheists would not refrain from attacking his animals without such marking. The commentator reconciles this by noting that Abu Hanifa's dislike was specific to his time: people would overdo the cutting, causing harm and potentially death. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) held that ish'ar is permissible (ja'iz) when done properly by cutting only the skin. Later Hanafi authorities such as Ibn al-Humam and al-Haskafi adopted the view of the disciples as the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). Thus, the practical ruling is that ish'ar is permissible if performed correctly without excessive mutilation.

Key Terms
الإشعار (al-ishʿār): Marking the sacrificial animal (hadi) by cutting or wounding it to indicate it is for sacrifice.
مثلة (mutlah): Mutilation, specifically cutting a limb from a living animal, considered reprehensible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Sunnah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits ish'ar when performed properly, based on the Prophet's practice and the view of the Sahibayn, with a caution that unskilled people should avoid it to prevent harm.

The Maki's Hajj: Only Ifrad Permitted
Defining the Maki and stating he can only perform Ifrad Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Maki and state the prescribed type of Hajj for him according to the Hanafi school, including the ruling if he performs Qiran or Tamattu'.

Core Idea
The Maki must perform Ifrad Hajj; Qiran and Tamattu' are concessions for non-residents only.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the meaning of al-Makki and the ruling that he can only perform Ifrad Hajj. The key Quranic basis is verse 2:196, which restricts the Tamattu' and Qiran concessions to those not residing at the Sacred Mosque. The Hanafi school holds that for a Maki, Qiran and Tamattu' are not prescribed, but if performed, they are valid yet deficient, requiring a dam.

Guided Path
1
Define al-Makki
Identify who qualifies as a Maki according to the Hanafi school. The text defines him as one whose residence is within Makkah or between Makkah and the mawaqit (miqat boundaries).
This is based on the Quranic verse '...for whoever his family is not present at the Sacred Mosque'.
2
Identify the prescribed Hajj type
State that the Maki is required to perform Ifrad Hajj only. He has no option for Qiran or Tamattu' as primary forms.
The phrase 'al-Makki yufridu faqat' is explicit.
3
Understand the dalil
Examine the Quranic evidence: Al-Baqarah 2:196. The verse grants the concession of Tamattu' and Qiran to those not present at the Sacred Mosque, implying that those present (Maki) do not have this concession.
The dalil is qat'i in both transmission and meaning.
4
Explore the consequence of violation
If a Maki performs Qiran or Tamattu', the Hanafi ruling is that it is valid (sahih) but deficient (naqis). He must offer a dam (blood sacrifice) as compensation.
This is based on later works like Jala' al-Adhhan and Durar al-Hukkam.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a Maki who performs Hajj al-Tamattu', determine the ruling and required action.
This tests practical application.

And he performs Umrah, and does not remove his ihram from it, then he enters ihram for Hajj as mentioned, and he shaves (his head) on the day of Nahr, and he is released from both his ihrams. And the Maki (resident of Makkah) performs Ifrad only (according to taqlid). (And he performs Umrah, and does not remove his ihram from it): i.e., from the Umrah, and this is when he drives the hadi. As for when he does not drive the hadi, he removes his ihram from the Umrah as mentioned. (Then he enters ihram for Hajj as mentioned): i.e., on the day of Tarwiyah, and before it is better, and he shaves on the day of Nahr, and is released from both his ihrams. [2] He said: 'does not remove his ihram from it' i.e., by shaving etc., rather he remains in ihram because of the Prophet's statement: 'Were it not that I have the hadi with me, I would have removed my ihram.' (4) (3) He said: 'better' because it is more difficult and more suited to hastening towards good. (4) He said: 'and the Maki' i.e., the one who is from the people of Makkah, and likewise whoever is between them and the mawaqit; and this is meant by His statement: 'That is for whoever his family is not present at the Sacred Mosque' (al-Baqarah 196), (0) thereby pointing to Tamattu', and it includes Qiran. [0] He said: 'only' i.e., he has no (option) except Ifrad in Hajj, even if he performs Umrah before it in the months of Hajj. [6] He said: 'he has no Qiran... etc.' admits two interpretations: first: negation of legislation and existence, so his Tamattu' and Qiran would be invalid. (2) Because their (Qiran and Tamattu') legislation is for comfort by eliminating one of the two journeys, and this pertains to the afaqi (non-resident). See: Durar al-Hukkam (1:237-238). (3) But if he performs Qiran or Tamattu', it is valid but deficient, and he must offer a dam (blood sacrifice) as compensation. Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling concerning the type of Hajj permissible for a person who is a resident of Makkah (Maki). The base matn states 'wal-Makki yufridu faqat' (the Maki performs Ifrad only). The commentator explains that the Maki is defined as one whose residence is within Makkah or between Makkah and the mawaqit (miqat boundaries), based on the Quranic verse 'That is for whoever his family is not present at the Sacred Mosque' (al-Baqarah 196). For such a person, Qiran (combining Umrah and Hajj in one ihram) and Tamattu' (performing Umrah then Hajj with separate ihrams but within one journey) are not prescribed. The rationale is that these forms are concessions for those who travel from afar (afaqi), allowing them to combine two journeys into one for comfort. The Maki does not need this concession. If a Maki nevertheless performs Qiran or Tamattu', the Hanafi ruling is that it is valid (sahih) but deficient (naqis), and he must offer a dam (blood sacrifice) as compensation (jubran). The hadith of the Prophet is cited: 'Were it not that I have the hadi with me, I would have removed my ihram,' indicating that when one drives a hadi, one remains in ihram until the day of Nahr.

Key Terms
المكي (al-Makki): A person whose residence is within Makkah or between Makkah and the mawaqit (miqat boundaries).
الإفراد (al-ifrād): Performing Hajj alone without combining with Umrah in the same ihram or journey.
القران (al-qirān): Combining Umrah and Hajj in a single ihram without performing Umrah first.
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing Umrah first, then removing ihram, then entering ihram for Hajj in the same journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person resides in Makkah (Maki) performs Hajj al-Tamattu', what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The Hajj is invalid (batil).
B) The Hajj is valid but deficient, and he must offer a dam.
C) The Hajj is valid and complete without any compensation.
D) The Hajj is valid only if he also performs Umrah.

Key Takeaway
The Maki must perform Ifrad Hajj; Qiran and Tamattu' are not prescribed for him, but if performed, they are valid with a compensatory dam.
